# M07 Phase 9 — Cluster Synthesis — structural input

**Date:** 2026-05-20
**Cluster:** M07 — Shame, Disgrace and Humiliation

---

## §1 — Cluster overview

M07 (Shame, Disgrace and Humiliation) holds 6 inner-being characteristics:

| Char | Short name | One-line definition |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Shame as experienced inner state | The painful inner experience of being exposed as inadequate, wrong, or unworthy — the felt collapse of dignity, confidence, and standing. |
| 2 | Humiliation as enforced abasement | Shame inflicted through an active downward movement of standing — the enforced lowering of a person, people, or pride-structure through social demotion, military defeat, physical exposure, or divine judgment. |
| 3 | Dishonour as relational worth-denial | The relational dimension of shame — treating persons as having less worth than they possess; the active denial or stripping of honour through attitude, conduct, or social judgment. |
| 4 | Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment | The category of what is morally shameful, indecent, or degraded — the conscience's recognition that certain conduct or conduct-patterns violate inner propriety and cannot bear scrutiny before God or community. |
| 5 | Shame produced by contempt and rejection | The shame experience arising from being treated with dismissive contempt or active rejection — the received, experiential face of the contempt-shame dynamic. |
| 6 | Innocence as structural counter to shame | The inner moral-purity state that functions as the structural opposite and protection against shame — blameless conscience, clean inner will, and moral integrity as the inner condition that shields against guilt-shame, allows approach to God without shame, and whose absence sustains the shamed condition before God. |

Each characteristic produced 189 findings in its Phase 9 batch (1,323 rows total in `cluster_finding`).

---

## §2 — Confirmed cluster observations (with resolution notes)

These four observations were raised at characteristic-mapping time and confirmed during Phase 9. They name the boundaries already validated and are direct inputs to the synthesis.

### Observation #5 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 8)

**Title:** CHAR-1 volume-split across M07-A / M07-B / M07-C

**Description:**

> CHAR-1 (Shame as experienced inner state) is the cluster's dominant characteristic (224 of 359 substantive verses = 62%). Per v2_8 §8.0 rule 2, volume-split across three sub-groups by moral-direction axis: M07-A (unjust wound), M07-B (moral consequence), M07-C (divine encounter). The characteristic identity persists across the three sub-groups; Phase 9 catalogue prompts should evaluate CHAR-1 as a single inner-being faculty manifesting in three registers, not as three separate characteristics.

---

### Observation #6 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 12)

**Title:** M07-G shame ↔ M06 contempt as relational complements

**Description:**

> Phase 3 v2 cross-register analysis (per v2_7 §6.3.2 verse-level relationship test) confirmed the M07-G sub-group holds the shame-recipient face of a contempt-shame dynamic whose source-side (contempt-projection) lives in M06. Every verse in M07-G's 24-verse corpus (especially the 11 exoutheneō verses) evidences contempt as the active mechanism producing shame in the recipient. The two characteristics are relational complements: M06 contempt produces; M07-G shame receives. Phase 9 T6 (Structural Relationships with Other Characteristics) should make this M06 ↔ M07 relationship explicit; M06's eventual Phase 9 will see the same dynamic from the contempt side.

---

### Observation #7 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 13)

**Title:** M07-H innocence ↔ M12 purity as structural counters to shame

**Description:**

> Phase 3 v2 cross-register analysis flagged niq.qa.von and qe.ha.von with M12 (purity/holiness) as the terms' primary register; they remain in M07 because every verse evidences the innocence-shame polarity directly (innocence as shield, innocence in tension with experienced shame, incapacity-for-innocence sustaining the shamed condition). Phase 9 T6 should articulate the M07 ↔ M12 cross-cluster relationship: innocence is the inner moral state that protects against guilt-shame; its absence sustains the condition shame names.

---

### Observation #8 — CROSS_CLUSTER_HANDOFF (cluster-wide)

**Title:** M09 pickup note: Pro 16:19 sha.phel (set-aside at Phase 8.5)

**Description:**

> At Phase 8.5 BOUNDARY resolution, Pro 16:19 (sha.phel — 'a lowly spirit with the poor', voluntary lowliness as morally superior) was SET-ASIDE from M07 because the verse evidences M09 (Humility/Meekness/Submission) directly, not M07 shame. ROUTE-TO-CLUSTER M09 was blocked at §18.2 eligibility check because no M09 term exists at this verse yet. WHEN M09 OPENS: sha.phel (H8213) is a likely M09 home-registry term; Pro 16:19 should be picked up there. CC tracks this for the M09 session-start prep.

---

### Observation #9 — CROSS_CLUSTER_HANDOFF (cluster-wide)

**Title:** M09 pickup note: Pro 29:23 sha.phel (kept in M07-D at Phase 8.5; M09 dimension present)

**Description:**

> Pro 29:23 (sha.phel — 'one's pride will bring him low, but he who is lowly in spirit will obtain honor') was PROMOTED to M07-D at Phase 8.5 based on the 'pride brings him low' half (researcher decision). The 'lowly of spirit obtains honor' half is M09 content. Phase 9 T6 should articulate this M07 ↔ M09 pairing in one proverb. When M09 opens, sha.phel may need to also pick up Pro 29:23 as a secondary/shared-anchor case across clusters.

---

## §3 — Per-prompt synthesis matrix

For each of the 189 prompts (T0.1.1 … T7.3.4), the 6 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim below. Read all 6 before authoring the cluster-scope row in your output.

### T0

#### T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected

##### T0.1.1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame as an experienced inner state reflects God's moral seriousness and his investment in the dignity of persons. The evidence from M07-C is most direct: the God who receives Ezra's shame-before-holiness (Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you") is a God before whom exposure is real and moral standing matters. The repeated Psalm promise that those who trust in God "will not be put to shame" (Psa 22:5; 25:2; 31:1; 119:31; Rom 5:5; 9:33; 10:11) reveals that God is the guardian of the inner dignity of those who rely on him — he takes personal responsibility for protecting them from shame's inner collapse. The M07-B evidence shows God actively deploying shame as a moral verdict (putting enemies to shame; exposing idol-makers' inner bankruptcy), revealing that shame participates in divine judgment and justice. Shame also reflects God's holiness — the fact that coming into his presence without atoned sin produces the inability to lift one's face (Ezr 9:6; Eze 36:32) reveals a God whose holiness generates the experience of shame in the morally uncleansed.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The dominant revelation in CHAR-2 is divine sovereignty over human standing. M07-D-VCG-03 (27 sha.phel verses) shows God as the primary agent of abasement: "God brings low and exalts" (1Sa 2:7, vc=21164); "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" (2Sa 22:28, vc=21165); "God alone executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another" (Psa 75:7, vc=21169). God's character revealed is a God for whom the proud inner disposition is intolerable, and who acts against it with terrifying sovereign force (Isa 10:33, vc=21178). Pride reaches for what belongs to God alone (Isa 2:11 — "the Lord alone will be exalted in that day"), and God's enforcement of that boundary is the judicial expression of his holiness.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 reveals God as the one who assigns and guards worth — the one whose evaluation of persons is authoritative and cannot be overridden by human contempt-judgments. Joh 8:49 (vc=35000) — "I honor my Father, and you dishonor me" — places dishonour as a relational act directed at Jesus personally, revealing a God whose worth is real and whose engagement with persons is worthy of honour. Rom 9:21 (vc=34960) — the potter's sovereign right to assign vessels for honourable or dishonorable use — reveals God as the primary worth-assigning agent; human dishonour-assignments are derivative and fallible.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 reveals God as the standard against which moral shamefulness is measured. Paul's renunciation of "shameful, underhanded ways" (2Cor 4:2, vc=34972) is grounded in conduct that must bear "open scrutiny before God" — God's sight is the evaluative standard. Eph 5:12 (vc=34985) — deeds done in secret so morally degraded "it is shameful even to speak of them" — presupposes a moral standard before which certain conduct cannot stand. The conscience recognising shamefulness reflects God's own moral judgment about what violates the propriety of created existence.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 reveals God as the one who reverses contempt-verdicts. Act 4:11 (vc=54638) — "the stone rejected by the builders has become the cornerstone" — God overturning the contempt-verdict of the builders and establishing the rejected as the foundation. 1Cor 1:28 (vc=54643) — "God chose what is low and despised in the world to nullify things that are" — God deliberately selecting what contempt has marked as of no account, thereby exposing the contempt-assessments of the world as false. This reveals a God who specifically positions himself against contempt-generated shame by choosing, accepting, and vindicating the despised.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 reveals God as both the standard and the source of moral innocence. The inner moral purity that CHAR-6 names — the clean conscience, the blameless will, the hands free of deliberate wrongdoing — reflects God's own moral purity in its creaturely form. Gen 20:5 (vc=22817/22821) — Abimelech's claim to have acted "in the integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" — presupposes a moral standard (heart-integrity and hand-cleanness) that is real and assessable before God, who responds by acknowledging the claim (Gen 20:6). The God who can verify and acknowledge innocence is the God whose own character makes moral innocence a meaningful category.

---

##### T0.1.2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The evidence does not directly attribute shame as an experienced inner state to God himself. Psa 113:6 (sha.phel, set aside at Phase 8.5) uses sha.phel for God's own "stooping down" to behold creation, but this is God's condescension rather than shame. No verse in the 224-verse CHAR-1 corpus attributes shame as a felt inner experience to the divine person. The analytical significance of this silence is considerable: shame as experienced here is the product of exposure, inadequacy, or moral failure — none of which can characterize God. The characteristic is distinctively creaturely. The one asymmetry is that the evidence shows God *producing* shame in others as a moral and judicial act, which is a function of his holiness and justice rather than an experience he shares with the human person.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

God is the primary agent of CHAR-2 in VCG-03: he brings low (1Sa 2:7), brings down haughty eyes (Psa 18:27, vc=21168), casts the wicked to the ground (Psa 147:6, vc=21171). The attribution is not that God experiences humiliation but that he exercises it as a judicial act — revealing CHAR-2 as a morally ordered phenomenon: God's deployment of it is the appropriate leveling of what has elevated itself beyond its proper place.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Within the CHAR-3 corpus, God is the ultimate arbiter whose dishonouring of a vessel or person (Rom 9:21) is the authoritative assignment, contrasted with human worth-denial which may be arbitrary or unjust. God does not dishonour unjustly; human dishonour-extension frequently does.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

Scripture does not explicitly attribute CHAR-4 to God — God does not engage in moral-evaluative judgment from within his own experience of shamefulness. God is the standard against which shamefulness is assessed, not one who possesses the characteristic himself. Silent on God possessing CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Scripture does not explicitly attribute CHAR-5 — shame as the received experience of being treated with contempt — to God himself. Jesus receives contempt and mockery (Luk 23:11, vc=54640) — but this is God incarnate in the creaturely condition, not God in his eternal nature receiving contempt from equals. God as such is not susceptible to the experience of being treated as of no account by a more powerful agent, because no such agent exists. Silent on God possessing CHAR-5.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

Scripture does not explicitly attribute the experience of innocence-as-structural-counter-to-shame to God in the way CHAR-6 is defined — as an inner state that protects against guilt-shame. God has no guilt-shame to be protected against. God is holy; the innocence of CHAR-6 is a creaturely moral state that reflects, imperfectly and derivatively, what God is by nature. Silent on God possessing CHAR-6 in its M07-H form.

---

##### T0.1.3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, what does that silence suggest about the characteristic's place in the divine image?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The silence confirms that shame as experienced inner state is a creaturely characteristic arising from moral vulnerability, exposure, and the gap between what the person is and what is required. God possesses no such gap. The characteristic's absence from the divine nature establishes it as a response-function rather than an originating-function — it is what happens to a morally situated creature when exposed before what is holy, when trust collapses, or when moral failure is uncovered. The creation-contrast is sharpest in Gen 2:25 (vc=34835): before the fall, the human pair "were not ashamed," evidencing shame as belonging to the fallen creaturely condition rather than the created design. This suggests shame is a post-fall reality that nonetheless reflects real moral structure (the capacity for guilt, the awareness of one's standing before God and community) that the divine image-bearer retains even in the fallen state.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

God exercises CHAR-2 but does not experience it as a creaturely condition. The silence confirms CHAR-2 is a fallen-world phenomenon: it is what happens to the creature that has over-reached. God humbles; he is not humbled by another.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The CHAR-3 corpus is primarily silent on God experiencing relational worth-denial as something that falls upon him from another equal. The dishonour directed at Jesus (Joh 8:49) reveals that God-incarnate can be the recipient of unjust worth-denial — but this is the creaturely context. Silent on God experiencing CHAR-3 in his eternal nature.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The silence confirms that CHAR-4 is a creaturely characteristic: it is the conscience's recognition, from within creaturely existence, of what violates the moral propriety of that existence. God's own moral character is the standard; the creature's conscience is the faculty that registers when conduct departs from that standard. CHAR-4 is the inner registrar of moral propriety, not the standard itself.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The silence confirms that CHAR-5 is a creaturely characteristic arising from the vulnerability of created persons to the contempt-judgments of others. God's systematic reversal of contempt-verdicts (1Cor 1:28; Act 4:11) reveals that he takes the contempt-produced shame of his people seriously — he does not ignore it but acts against it. The characteristic belongs to creaturely moral vulnerability; its resolution belongs to divine sovereign counter-action.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The silence confirms that CHAR-6 is a creaturely moral state — the creature's approximation to, and protection by, the moral purity that characterises God. The innocence that protects the image-bearer against guilt-shame is a creaturely participation in the moral order that God himself constitutes. CHAR-6 is exclusively creaturely in its M07 function (as protection against shame), though it derives from and reflects the divine moral character.

---

#### T0.2 — Created Purpose

##### T0.2.1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Gen 2:25 (vc=34835) is the critical datum: the absence of shame in the pre-fall pair marks the state of "inner transparency and relational wholeness." Shame as experienced inner state is therefore not part of the original created design's positive content — it does not serve a purpose in the unfallen person. Its design-function appears only in the fallen context: the M07-B evidence shows shame functioning as a moral corrective (entrepō — 2Th 3:14; 1Cor 6:5 entropē; Eze 43:10-11), exposing moral failure and driving the person toward right orientation. The M07-C evidence shows shame before God functioning as the gateway to restoration — "only if Israel is ashamed of all they have done will the full design of the temple be disclosed to them" (Eze 43:11, vc=38514). In the fallen condition, shame serves the purpose of moral orientation — it registers reality accurately about the person's standing, prompting return and correction.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 has no positive purpose in the original created design — it is a judicial-corrective mechanism operating in the fallen world. Its purpose is to restore the moral order pride has distorted: the Isa 2 series shows "the Lord alone will be exalted in that day" — the humiliation of the proud is in the service of God's rightful exaltation.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 in its negative form (the active denial of worth) serves no positive purpose in the original created design. However, CHAR-3 presupposes a capacity — the capacity to recognise and assign worth to persons — that belongs to the created design. The judge who "neither fears God nor respects man" (Luk 18:2, vc=34990) is failing to exercise a faculty that belongs to proper human functioning: the capacity to perceive and honour the worth of others.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 serves the purpose of moral calibration in the human person — it is the conscience's capacity to distinguish the shameful from the honourable, the indecent from the proper. This calibrating function equips the person to recognise conduct that violates inner propriety (Eph 5:12), to refuse shameful gain (Tit 1:11, vc=34982), to renounce underhanded ways (2Cor 4:2). CHAR-4 equips the person to hold themselves to the standard of what can bear moral scrutiny before God.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 in its ordinary form (received contempt producing shame) serves no positive purpose in the original created design. However, CHAR-5 presupposes the capacity for worth-recognition and its violation — and this capacity belongs to the created design. The ability to receive contempt as a wound presupposes that the person has genuine worth that can be misassigned. CHAR-5 serves an indirect revelatory purpose: it reveals what the world's contempt-systems distort, thereby pointing toward the true worth-assignment of God.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 serves the purpose of enabling the person to approach God and engage in genuine relational integrity without the barrier of guilt-shame. Psa 26:6 (vc=22819/22823) — "I wash my hands in innocence and go around your altar, O Lord" — shows innocence as the inner moral condition that enables worship and approach to God. CHAR-6 equips the person to stand before God and before the community with a clean inner conscience — the condition under which genuine relationship with God and others is possible.

---

##### T0.2.2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The evidence positions shame as primarily a response to the fallen condition, not original created design. Gen 2:25 (vc=34835) explicitly names the pre-fall state as one without shame — the absence of shame is the positive mark of created wholeness. The fall produces the shame-condition. However, the capacity for shame — the inner moral apparatus that registers exposure, guilt, and relational brokenness — appears to belong to the image-bearing structure itself. The evidence from M07-C (Ezr 9:6; Jer 31:19; Eze 43:10-11) shows shame operating as the morally appropriate response to one's own sin, suggesting that the faculty which produces shame (moral consciousness, conscience) is part of the created design, while the experience of shame is a response to the fallen condition. Both dimensions are present: shame-as-experience is post-fall; shame-as-moral-signal depends on image-bearing moral awareness.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is a response to the fallen condition. Social demotion (VCG-01), military defeat (VCG-02), and divine abasement-of-pride (VCG-03) all presuppose a world of human pride, violence, and political hubris. CHAR-2 is the corrective mechanism against fallenness rather than a feature of the unfallen design.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 as worth-denial is a response to the fallen condition — the failure of the worth-recognition capacity that belongs to the image. The failure takes two forms: active willful dishonour (VCG-01) and structural assigned dishonour (VCG-02). The created design included the worth-recognition capacity; its corruption produces CHAR-3.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The evidence is ambiguous on whether CHAR-4 belongs to the original created design or is a response to the fallen condition. The shamefulness-of-conduct register (VCG-01) presupposes a moral standard against which conduct is assessed — this standard-sensitivity belongs to the created design (image-bearers are morally responsive). The inverted-conscience register (VCG-03 — Phili 3:19; Hos 4:18) is definitionally a fallen-condition phenomenon: the conscience that glories in what is actually shame is a corrupted conscience. CHAR-4 in its functioning form is part of created moral design; in its inverted form it is a fall-response.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is a response to the fallen condition — contempt is a fallen-world mechanism, and the shame it produces arises because the fallen world denies worth to persons who genuinely have it. The VCG-02 evidence (the servants beaten by violent tenants; Herod mocking Jesus) is specifically about fallen-world contempt structures being enacted against innocent persons. CHAR-5 does not belong to the original created design; it is a fallen-condition phenomenon that God specifically acts to reverse.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 in its full functioning form is part of the original created design: the pre-fall Adam and Eve were innocent — they lacked guilt-shame because they had no moral failure to produce it (Gen 2:25, in CHAR-1's corpus). The capacity for innocence, and the inner state of innocence, belongs to the created design. However, the specific function of CHAR-6 as a protection against guilt-shame is a response to the fallen condition: in the unfallen state, no protection against guilt-shame was needed because there was no guilt. CHAR-6 is therefore both created-design (the innocence itself) and fallen-condition-response (its function as protection against shame).

---

##### T0.2.3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Strong evidence. The M07-A evidence (VCG-04) documents God's explicit promises to remove shame permanently: "you will forget the shame of your youth" (Isa 54:4, vc=34838/37319/37352/38534), shame transformed into a double portion (Isa 61:7, vc=37320/37482), "my people shall never again be put to shame" (Joe 2:26, vc=65582; Joe 2:27, vc=65583). The M07-C evidence (VCG-04) confirms the eschatological direction: everlasting salvation means never put to shame or confounded "to all eternity" (Isa 45:17, vc=65543). Rev 3:18 (vc=34975) — the naked shame of spiritual destitution covered by Christ's garments — frames the present shame-condition within an eschatological transaction. The future fullness is a state where shame's inner collapse is permanently resolved — not merely managed but removed by divine act, replaced by honour, double portion, and praise. Shame's orientation toward its own removal is built into the evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. The Day-of-the-Lord material (Isa 2:9-17; 13:11) points toward eschatological completion: the final abasement of all human pride so God alone is exalted. 1Cor 15:43 (vc=34962) — "sown in dishonor, raised in glory" — frames the mortal body's humiliation as the eschatological transition point. The future fullness replaces humiliation with the glory of God's restored order.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Yes. The structural-dishonour mode (VCG-02) implies an eschatological dimension in which worth-assignment is finalised. The eschatological fullness is a state in which worth is perfectly assigned according to God's standard — the world's dishonour-judgments overturned, and all persons standing before God at their true worth.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Yes. The inverted conscience that "glories in their shame" (Phili 3:19, vc=65486) has a future that is named: "their end is destruction." Rev 16:15 (vc=34967) — the one who stays awake and keeps his garments on avoids "being seen exposed and indecent" — frames the maintenance of CHAR-4's proper functioning as oriented toward Christ's coming. The eschatological fullness is a moral condition in which no shamefulness is present because the conscience is properly calibrated.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Yes. Act 4:11 (vc=54638) — the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone — is the paradigmatic statement of CHAR-5's eschatological reversal. The shame produced by contempt and rejection is oriented toward its final reversal: what was despised and of no account is chosen and vindicated by God. The Bartimaeus episode (Mar 10:50, vc=37238) — the abandonment of the beggar-identity in eager response to Jesus's call — is an enacted eschatological moment: the contempt-formed shame-identity is discarded as Jesus calls the person into a new worth-assignment.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Yes. Psa 73:13's lament (vc=22818/22822) — "all in vain have I kept my heart clean and washed my hands in innocence" — shows the present experience of innocence that seems futile but is oriented toward a future vindication. The resolution of the Psa 73 lament in its wider context (the sanctuary, Psa 73:17) shows that innocence's protection is vindicated eschatologically even when it appears to fail in the present. The eschatological fullness is a state in which innocence's protective function is fully operative and the incapacity-for-innocence (Hos 8:5) is resolved by the new covenant's transformed inner life.

---

#### T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression

##### T0.3.1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame as experienced inner state expresses the divine image primarily through the moral consciousness it presupposes. The person who can feel shame is a person who has a built-in reference point for moral standing — a sense of what they should be, how they should stand before others and before God. The M07-C evidence (Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you, my God") shows that shame before God is possible only because the image-bearer retains the capacity for moral self-assessment in the divine presence. The M07-B evidence (Jer 6:15 — "they did not know how to blush," vc=65551; Jer 8:12, vc=65553) reveals the inverse: the loss of the capacity for shame marks the degradation of the image, specifically the destruction of the moral-evaluative faculty. Shame as experienced inner state therefore expresses the divine image's moral dimension — the capacity to stand before the holy and register the gap between what one is and what one ought to be.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 expresses the divine image indirectly through the moral structure it presupposes. The image-bearer's standing before God is morally real — it can be wrongly exalted by pride and must be brought to its proper level. The sha.phel material targeting inner dispositions (haughty looks, self-exaltation) shows that God takes the creature's inner moral orientation seriously enough to act against its distortions.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 expresses the divine image through the worth-recognition capacity it presupposes and violates. The human person is equipped to see worth in others — to recognise that other persons are not instruments but ends, that they bear dignity before God. Jam 2:6 (vc=35003) — "you have dishonored the poor man" — presupposes that the poor man has worth that is being violated.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 expresses the divine image through the moral-evaluative faculty — specifically through the conscience's ability to assess conduct against the standard of God's own moral character. The person who can recognise that certain things "should not be named, let alone done" (Eph 5:12) has a moral-evaluation capacity that reflects the image: they carry within them a reference to the moral order God has established. The inverted conscience of VCG-03 represents the image's moral-evaluative faculty corrupted — glorying in shame is the worst form of this corruption.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 expresses the divine image through the worth-bearer's genuine dignity that contempt violates. The person who receives contempt and experiences CHAR-5 is a person whose worth is real — the contempt is false in its assessment. God's election of the despised (1Cor 1:28) confirms that the image-bearer's worth is divinely established and cannot be finally cancelled by human contempt. The capacity to be shamed by contempt reflects the real worth that is being violated — shame under unjust contempt is itself evidence of genuine dignity.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 expresses the divine image through the moral-integrity faculty — the capacity for blameless inner will and clean-handed action that mirrors God's own moral purity in creaturely form. The "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" (Gen 20:5) names the two dimensions of the image's moral faculty: the inner will (heart-integrity) and the outward action (hand-cleanness). Together these constitute the image-bearer's moral wholeness that CHAR-6 names and protects.

---

##### T0.3.2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

As noted at T0.1.2, the evidence does not attribute shame as experienced inner state to God. It is a creaturely analogue: the moral seriousness that shame reflects (the reality of moral standing, exposure before holiness, the weight of guilt) has a divine correlate in God's holiness and just judgment, but God does not experience the felt collapse of dignity that constitutes shame. The characteristic is exclusively creaturely in its experiential form.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

God exercises CHAR-2 but does not undergo it. Enforced abasement as a creaturely condition is exclusively creaturely — it cannot be imposed on God.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The worth-recognition faculty is shared analogically: God perfectly assigns and recognises worth; humans do so derivatively and fallibly. The dishonour-failure (CHAR-3) is exclusively creaturely — God does not fail to recognise worth. The sharing is asymmetric: God honours perfectly; humans honour derivatively and can fail to honour (producing CHAR-3).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

God does not share the characteristic of shamefulness-as-moral-judgment in the sense that CHAR-4 names — he does not have a conscience that registers his own conduct as shameful. The moral judgments CHAR-4 makes are creaturely assessments against God's standard, not God's self-assessment. CHAR-4 is a creaturely analogue to God's moral purity, mediated through the creature's conscience. Silent on God sharing CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Shame produced by contempt is exclusively creaturely — it arises from vulnerability to others' worth-assessments, a vulnerability God does not share. God's positioning against contempt (electing the despised) is the divine response, not God experiencing CHAR-5. Silent on God sharing CHAR-5.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The moral purity that CHAR-6 names is shared analogically: God's purity is original and absolute; the creaturely innocence of CHAR-6 is derivative and limited (it can be lost, as Hos 8:5 shows; it can be maintained with effort, as Psa 26:6 shows). The sharing is asymmetric: God is holy without effort or threat; the image-bearer maintains innocence within a morally vulnerable creaturely existence.

---

##### T0.3.3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The M07-B seared-conscience evidence (VCG-04) is definitive: the loss of the capacity for shame — "they did not know how to blush" (Jer 6:15; 8:12) — is presented as moral collapse, the sign that the inner faculty of conscience is "dead" (M07-B-VCG-04 Phase 7 description). This is the image degraded. Conversely, the capacity for shame — the ability to feel the inner weight of one's own moral failure, to be "ashamed and blush to lift one's face" before God (Ezr 9:6) — is evidence that the moral-evaluative faculty remains operative. Zophar's challenge to Job (Job 11:3, vc=38520 in M07-B-VCG-03) implies that the capacity for shame in response to moral failure is part of what healthy moral persons should have. The presence of appropriate shame signals the image functioning; its absence signals its corruption.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Reception of humiliation is morally neutral in itself — David's envoys are humiliated unjustly (2Sa 10:5, vc=38517); Sennacherib justly (2Ch 32:21, vc=37326). What the evidence reveals is that the proud's insulation from appropriate humiliation is a sign of moral disorder: Pro 11:2 (vc=37501) presents "when pride comes, then comes disgrace" as a moral law. The person whose pride elevates them beyond proper standing is in a condition of image-disorder that CHAR-2 corrects.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The person who characteristically dishonours others — treating persons as of diminished or no worth — evidences a degraded image in their relational-moral faculty. Jam 2:6 — showing favouritism to the rich while dishonoring the poor — is a failure of moral perception that contradicts the image-bearing moral vision of persons as equally worthy before God. The absence of worth-recognition (the judge who neither fears God nor respects man) reveals the image's relational faculty as non-functional.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

A functioning CHAR-4 — the conscience that can recognise and recoil from the shameful — evidences the image's moral faculty as operative. The inverted conscience of VCG-03 (Phili 3:19 — glorying in shame) evidences the image's moral faculty as corrupted. The absence of moral shame-recognition (the seared conscience of Jer 6:15; 8:12 in CHAR-1) evidences the image as degraded toward the loss of the conscience faculty. CHAR-4's presence and health is a moral-image indicator.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The person who receives contempt and experiences CHAR-5 is in a condition of creaturely vulnerability — their image-bearing worth is real but being violated. The person who extends contempt (the source-side, M06's territory) has their image in the distorted form of the contempt-disposition — they are suppressing the image's proper function of worth-recognition. God's reversal of contempt-verdicts (1Cor 1:28; Act 4:11) reveals that the image's proper condition is worth-recognition rather than contempt-dismissal.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The presence of CHAR-6 (functioning innocence — clean conscience, blameless will) evidences the image's moral faculty as operative and engaged. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5 — "how long will they be incapable of innocence?") evidences the image's moral faculty as impaired or corrupted by sustained idolatry. The loss of innocence-capacity is not merely moral failure but the degradation of the inner moral faculty that makes return to God possible — it is the image's moral dimension damaged at its root.

---

#### T0.4 — Typological Significance

##### T0.4.1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate (covenantal, eschatological, christological)?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, in at least three directions. First, the servant's bearing of disgrace and spitting (Isa 50:6, vc=37481 in M07-A-VCG-02) — "I hid not my face from disgrace and spitting" — functions typologically toward Christ's passion, with Act 8:32's silence of the lamb (vc=28925) confirming the christological reading: the willed inner stillness under unjust suffering that shame normally overwhelms. Second, Heb 12:2 (vc=34970) explicitly deploys Jesus's endurance of the cross's shame as the anchor for CHAR-1's voluntary-suffering register — "despising the shame" in full awareness, motivated by the joy set before him. Third, the eschatological shame-removal promises (Isa 54:4; 61:7; Joe 2:26; Rev 3:18) function typologically toward the final state — shame's removal is the image-bearing person's eschatological fullness, toward which the present experience of shame (and its partial lifting through faith and trust) is oriented.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. The Day-of-the-Lord material (Isa 2:9-17; 5:15; 13:11) deploys cosmic humiliation typologically — all human pride brought low so God alone is exalted, pointing toward eschatological consummation. 1Cor 15:43 deploys the body's mortal dishonor as the type for the resurrection state — mortal humiliation is the seed-state for eschatological glory.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Yes, in the christological direction. Joh 8:49 (vc=35000) — the dishonour directed at Jesus by his accusers — operates typologically: the dishonour inflicted on God-incarnate by those who should have recognised his worth points toward the cross's dynamic of dishonour received and vindicated. Heb 6:6 (vc=34996) — those who fall away "crucify once again the Son of God... and hold him up to contempt" — explicitly links apostolic dishonour of Christ to the crucifixion.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Yes. Rev 16:15 (vc=34967) — "blessed is the one who stays awake, keeping his garments on, that he may not go about naked and be seen exposed" — deploys the shameful-nakedness image typologically: physical nakedness as the type for moral-spiritual unpreparedness at Christ's coming. The image of shameful exposure echoes Gen 2:25's pre-fall un-shamedness and Gen 3's post-fall covering — CHAR-4's shamefulness is typologically connected to the fall's introduction of the shame-condition.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Strongly evidenced typologically. Act 4:11 (vc=54638) — Jesus as the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone — is one of the NT's most explicit typological deployments of CHAR-5: Israel's experience of rejected-then-vindicated (Psa 118:22) is the type; Jesus's rejection-and-resurrection-vindication is the antitype. The Luk 23:11 mockery of Jesus (vc=54640) is a CHAR-5 event that carries christological-typological weight: the world's contempt-verdict on God incarnate, overturned by resurrection.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 carries typological significance through the Psa 26:6 connection to the washing of hands as the preparation for worship. This gesture finds its christological type in Pilate's hand-washing (Mat 27:24 — outside the CHAR-6 corpus but typologically connected): the gesture of innocence-declaration is deployed in the very act of delivering the innocent Jesus to death, revealing the limits of human-declared innocence and pointing toward the one who alone can provide the innocence that genuinely protects. The innocence that CHAR-6 describes in the image-bearer points toward the innocence of Christ as the ultimate fulfilment.

---

##### T0.4.2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology — does the human instance point toward the divine, or does the divine instance establish the pattern for the human?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Primarily human-to-divine with christological fulfilment, and secondarily eschatological anticipation. The human experience of bearing unjust disgrace without self-defense (servant, the silent lamb) points toward Christ's passion. Christ's despising the cross's shame (Heb 12:2) establishes the pattern that human believers are invited to inhabit (1Pe 4:16 — "let him not be ashamed, but let him glorify God in that name"). The direction is bidirectional in the VCG-03 material: human unjust shame points toward Christ; Christ's disposition toward shame in the cross establishes the pattern for human response.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Primarily eschatological: present enforced humiliation (especially mortal bodily dishonor) anticipates its reversal in resurrection. The Day-of-the-Lord typology moves from present divine acts of humiliation toward their eschatological completion.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The direction is human worth-denial directed at the divine — the creature dishonours the Creator through active contempt, mockery, and apostasy. The divine response is not to match the dishonour but to override it through resurrection-vindication (the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone, Act 4:11 in CHAR-5).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The direction is from the creaturely moral condition (bodily nakedness as shameful) toward the eschatological spiritual condition (moral-spiritual unpreparedness exposed at Christ's coming). The human bodily-shame instance (exposed nakedness) points toward the spiritual-shame instance (moral unpreparedness). The typology moves from physical to spiritual.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The typology runs in both directions. Human rejection of persons points toward the rejection of Jesus. Jesus's reception of contempt and shame (Luk 23:11; Heb 12:2 in CHAR-1) establishes the pattern for how his followers receive contempt: it is what Jesus bore. The divine instance (God choosing the despised, 1Cor 1:28) establishes the pattern for how the community should re-evaluate who has worth.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The typological direction is from human-creaturely innocence (CHAR-6 in Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) toward the divine-ground of all innocence (God's own holiness) and christologically toward the one in whom innocence is perfect. The human instance points toward the divine ground and the christological fulfilment.

---

##### T0.4.3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; typological use is evidenced above at T0.4.1.

---

## T1 — Defining the Characteristic

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Not applicable; typological use is evidenced.

---

## T1 — Defining the Characteristic

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Not applicable; typological use is evidenced.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Not applicable; typological use is evidenced.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Not applicable; typological use is extensively evidenced.

---

## T1 — Defining the Characteristic

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Not applicable; typological significance is identified above.

---

## T1 — Defining the Characteristic

---

### T1

#### T1.1 — Name and Naming

##### T1.1.1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

"Shame as experienced inner state." The name's three components are all analytically load-bearing: "shame" names the emotion/condition; "as experienced" marks it as a phenomenological reality — the felt inward event, not a moral verdict assigned from outside; "inner state" locates it constitutionally within the person, not merely in their reputation or social standing. The name explicitly distinguishes this characteristic from M07's other characteristics (enforced humiliation = M07-D; relational worth-denial = M07-E; shamefulness as moral judgment = M07-F). The CHAR-1 name signals that what is under investigation is the inner life of the person who feels shame — not what others think of them, not the moral quality of what they did, but the collapse of dignity, confidence, and standing that they experience.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

"Humiliation as enforced abasement": "humiliation" names the characteristic experience; "as enforced" specifies the mechanism (done to the person by another agent — military defeat, social demotion, divine judgment); "abasement" names the direction (downward movement of standing). The name distinguishes CHAR-2 from CHAR-1 (felt inner experience without specifying enforcement) and locates it in socially enacted, divinely executed, or circumstantially produced downward movement of standing.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

"Dishonour as relational worth-denial." The name is precise: "dishonour" names the specific register (stripping of honour/worth); "as relational" specifies the operational field (it always operates between persons or between person and God); "worth-denial" names the mechanism (what is being denied is the worth the other person actually has). The name distinguishes CHAR-3 from CHAR-1 (felt inner shame) and CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing): dishonour is specifically a relational act of worth-misassignment.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

"Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment." The name's structure: "shamefulness" names the quality being evaluated (the condition of being shameful, as distinct from the experience of shame); "as moral-evaluative judgment" specifies the operation — this is the conscience's assessment rather than a felt experience. The name distinguishes CHAR-4 from CHAR-1 (the felt inner experience of shame) by locating it in the evaluative rather than the experiential register: CHAR-4 is what conscience says about conduct or objects, not what the person feels in response to their own exposure.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

"Shame produced by contempt and rejection." The name identifies: (1) the characteristic experience ("shame"); (2) its specific mechanism ("produced by contempt and rejection" — not by guilt, not by social demotion, but by the attitude of contemptuous dismissal or active rejection directed at the person). The name positions CHAR-5 as the received face of the contempt-shame dynamic whose source-side (contempt-projection) is M06's territory. CHAR-5 holds what the person experiences when contempt is directed at them.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

"Innocence as structural counter to shame." The name has three components: "innocence" names the inner moral state (blameless conscience, clean will, hands free of deliberate wrongdoing); "as structural counter" identifies the function (not merely adjacent to shame but constitutively opposed to it — the inner state that makes guilt-shame structurally impossible or practically protects against it); "to shame" names the characteristic it counters (specifically guilt-shame, the M07-C register of shame before God). The name positions CHAR-6 as the positive inner-moral condition that CHAR-1's guilt-shame register presupposes the absence of.

---

##### T1.1.2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The primary Hebrew root *bosh* (H0954, 108 verses in cluster, majority in CHAR-1) means to be ashamed, to feel shame — a stative verb whose basic sense is the felt inner state of shame. The root produces the nominal forms *bo.shet* (H1322 — shame as noun, the condition itself) and *bu.shah* (H0955 — the covering/enveloping shame). *Ke.lim.mah* (H3639 — dishonour, ignominy) names the experience of being publicly exposed and reduced — the social-facing dimension of shame. *Cha.pher* (H2659) adds the element of embarrassment and being disgraced, often with the connotation of being found out or let down. The Greek *aischunē* (G0152) and *aischunō* (G0153) are closely parallel to *bosh* — the noun and verb of the felt shame experience. *Kataischunō* (G2617) adds the prefix kata- (down, thoroughly) giving "to thoroughly shame" or "to put to shame completely." Together the terms confirm at the definitional level: CHAR-1 is about what happens *inside the person* — the felt state of inner collapse in the face of exposure, inadequacy, or moral failure.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Ka.lam (H3637): root sense of wounding or cutting — humiliation is something done to the person that wounds their social existence. The shaved-beard episodes (2Sa 10:5; 1Ch 19:5) show ka.lam in its most concrete bodily register. Sha.phel (H8213): root means to be low, to be brought down; Hiphil (causing to be low) expresses God's active execution of the downward movement against the proud. Together: CHAR-2 is both physically embodied (ka.lam) and spiritually judicial (sha.phel).

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Atimazō (G0818) — to dishonour, treat as worthless; root: atimos — without honour, without worth. Atimia (G0819) — dishonour as a state of assigned worth-denial. Entrepō (G1788) — "to have regard for" in its absence: the judge who "does not respect man" lacks the inner movement of regard that would recognise worth. Paradeigmatizō (G3856) — to expose publicly, to hold up to contempt. Together these terms reveal CHAR-3 as constituted by the failure or refusal of the worth-recognition act: one sees another person and assigns them less worth than they have.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Aischros (G0150) — shameful, base, disgraceful — an adjective naming the moral quality of conduct or objects. Aischunē (G0152) in its evaluative register (2Cor 4:2; Phili 3:19) — the shame-quality of conduct recognised by conscience. Aschēmosunē (G0808) — indecency, improper form — the quality of what violates proper form or order. Atimia (G0819) in VCG-02 — dishonorable passions — names the moral-evaluative quality of certain appetites. Together: CHAR-4 is the adjectival-quality register of shame — shameful is a quality of things and conduct, not only an experience of persons.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Exoutheneō (G1848): the primary term — to treat as of no account, to utterly despise, to regard as nothing. Root: ex (out of) + ouden (nothing) = to make out of nothing. This is the strongest contempt-vocabulary in the NT: the person being treated as if they were literally nothing. Atimazō (G0818) in VCG-02: to dishonour through violent contemptuous action. Loidoria (G3059): verbal reviling as reputation-attack. The root meanings together reveal CHAR-5's source-mechanism: the contempt-er assigns zero worth to the contempt-ed, producing shame in the recipient by the force of that worth-cancellation.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Niq.qa.von (H5356A): innocence, cleanness — from naqah (to be clean, to be free from guilt). The root sense is freedom from moral blemish or guilt-stain — the state of being morally uncontaminated by deliberate wrongdoing. Qe.ha.von (H5356B): in this context functions as a near-synonym or parallel term to niq.qa.von — the bluntness/cleanness of hands, pointing to the same moral-freedom condition. Both terms together locate CHAR-6 in the hands-and-heart moral-integrity domain: the inner will (heart) and the outward action (hands) both free from guilt-stain.

---

##### T1.1.3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Directional: shame moves the person *downward* — toward collapse, withdrawal, covering, face-hiding. The evidence consistently shows the shamed person unable to lift their head (Job 10:15, vc=37502), covering their face (Jer 14:3, vc=38535; Eze 7:18, vc=34978), unable to lift their face toward God (Ezr 9:6, vc=65495). Relational: shame is inherently relational — it arises in the face of someone (God, enemies, community). The three sub-group registers (unjust wound, moral consequence, divine encounter) all locate shame in a relational field. Constitutional: the name's "inner state" tag signals that the primary register is psychological/volitional — the collapse happens to the faculty of dignity, confidence, and self-perception. These implications together orient the enquiry: CHAR-1 is a downward, relational, inner event.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Strongly directional (downward); relational (inflicted by an agent on a recipient); constitutional (operates at the social-bodily interface — the body bears the sign of disgrace and community recognises it).

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is relational by definition — it always operates in the space between persons. Directionally, it moves from the dishonour-er toward the dishonoured. The constitutional implication is that CHAR-3 engages the moral-evaluative and relational faculties: it is produced by a failure of moral perception and has its primary effect in the relational standing of the dishonoured.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is constitutive rather than directional: it names a quality (what is shameful) rather than a direction. The relational implication is toward God's sight and the community's moral standard — the shameful is what cannot bear scrutiny before God (2Cor 4:2) or community (Eph 5:12). The constitutional implication is that CHAR-4 is located in the conscience — the faculty that registers moral quality.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is relational by definition — it always arises from the interaction between a contempt-er and a contempt-ed. Directionally: contempt moves from the dismisser toward the dismissed, producing shame in the recipient. Constitutional implication: CHAR-5 engages the person's sense of worth (the inner faculty that registers their standing before others), which is affected by the contempt-verdict even when that verdict is false.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is constitutive: it names an inner state rather than a direction. However, it carries a directional implication as a counter: it moves against guilt-shame, protecting the person from the inner collapse that guilt-shame would produce. Constitutional implication: CHAR-6 is located primarily in the conscience (the moral-recognitive faculty that registers guilt or its absence) and in the will (the faculty whose freedom from deliberate wrongdoing constitutes the innocence).

---

#### T1.2 — Kind

##### T1.2.1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 appears primarily as a *condition* — a state that falls upon the person or arises within them — rather than a discrete act or a stable disposition. The bosh corpus evidences this: "they are ashamed" (stative), "shame has covered my face" (condition received), "my days are spent in shame" (ongoing condition). However, CHAR-1 also has a volitional dimension: the corrective-shame register (M07-C-VCG-03, M07-B-VCG-05) shows shame being invoked or directed — used as a moral tool. And the borne-for-God's-sake register (M07-A-VCG-03) shows shame voluntarily accepted, which requires an act of the will. CHAR-1 is therefore primarily a *condition* with volitional dimensions — the condition can be received passively, resisted by trust, accepted willingly, or deployed correctively.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is a condition imposed from outside — it arrives through external agents (armies, God, social community) and produces an inner-standing collapse in the recipient. It is neither a discrete act by the recipient nor a stable inner disposition they possess, but a condition that falls upon them as the result of what others do.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is primarily an act in VCG-01 — the willful act of dishonoring another: boasting in the law while breaking it (Rom 2:23, vc=35002); showing favoritism to the rich while dishonoring the poor (Jam 2:6); holding Christ up to contempt (Heb 6:6). In VCG-02, CHAR-3 is a condition — assigned or received standing (the potter's assignment, Rom 9:21; nature's teaching about disgrace, 1Cor 11:14). Both act and condition are present in the evidence.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is primarily a quality — a property of conduct, objects, or inner orientations — rather than an act, condition, or disposition in the usual sense. "It is shameful for a woman to speak in church" (1Cor 14:35) — shamefulness is a quality of the act. "Disgraceful, underhanded ways" (2Cor 4:2) — shameful is the quality of the conduct-type. In VCG-03, the inverted-conscience cases (Phili 3:19; Hos 4:18) are a disposition: the person has a perverted evaluative faculty.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily a condition produced by an external agent's act (contempt). The person does not produce CHAR-5 in themselves; it is inflicted upon them by another's dismissive attitude or active rejection. In VCG-01 (dismissive inner attitude), the contempt is internal to the contempt-er but produces an external social effect — the recipient is treated as of no account. In VCG-02 (violent rejection), the contempt is actively enacted. In VCG-03 (verbal contempt), contempt is communicated through speech.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is primarily a condition or quality — the inner moral state of being innocent, of having a clean conscience and blameless hands. It is not an act (though it is maintained through moral choices — Psa 26:6's "I wash my hands in innocence" suggests active maintenance). It is not a stable disposition in the sense of a permanent trait — Psa 73:13 shows it can be maintained but seems futile; Hos 8:5 shows it can be lost. CHAR-6 is a moral-condition that requires active maintenance and can be damaged or lost.

---

##### T1.2.2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 is structurally complex. The volume-split into three sub-groups (M07-A: unjust wound; M07-B: moral consequence; M07-C: divine encounter) reflects three distinguishable registers, all of which are manifestations of the same underlying phenomenon — the felt collapse of dignity and standing. The constituent elements identifiable from the evidence include: (1) a trigger — the exposure, failure, or enemy-action that initiates shame; (2) the felt inner collapse — the specific phenomenology of shame's impact; (3) the behavioural expression — face-covering, head-bowing, silence, turning back; (4) the moral assessment — whether the shame is deserved or unjust; (5) the relational direction — toward God, toward enemies, toward community; and (6) the resolution direction — removal, persistence, or acceptance. These are not separate characteristics but the internal anatomy of CHAR-1.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 has four operational registers: (1) Social/bodily demotion through visible enacted downward movement (VCG-01); (2) Military-national collapse stripping power and identity (VCG-02); (3) Divine abasement of pride as sovereign counteraction to self-exaltation (VCG-03); (4) Humiliation as enduring carried burden (VCG-04). These are facets of the same enforced-downward-movement characteristic differently situated.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Two constituent elements: (1) Active worth-denial (VCG-01): the willful act of refusing to acknowledge or withdrawing acknowledgment of another's worth. (2) Assigned or structural dishonour (VCG-02): dishonour as an objective state assigned by sovereign authority without being the product of a malicious human will.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Three constituent elements across the three VCGs: (1) Shameful conduct and objects (VCG-01): the moral quality of specific conduct-types and objects — violations of inner propriety, deceptive ways, idolatrous shameful objects. (2) Indecent desires and moral disorder (VCG-02): the moral quality of specific inner-appetite types — dishonorable passions as the inner driving force of moral disorder. (3) Inverted conscience (VCG-03): the corruption of the evaluative faculty itself — the conscience that treats disgrace as honour.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Three constituent elements: (1) Dismissive contempt as inner attitude (VCG-01): the inner disposition of treating others as of no account, producing shame through exclusion and devaluation. (2) Active contempt through violence, mockery, and rejection (VCG-02): contempt enacted through physical violence, public mocking, or willful rejection. (3) Verbal contempt and reputation attack (VCG-03): contempt communicated through reviling, hostile speech, slanderous verbal attack — shame produced through the destruction of the person's reputation.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Two constituent elements corresponding to the two VCGs: (1) Innocence as active inner defence (VCG-01): the functioning innocence — clean conscience, blameless will, hands free of deliberate wrongdoing — that enables approach to God without guilt-shame (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6). (2) Innocence questioned and incapacity for innocence (VCG-02): the innocence whose protective function is doubted or whose loss is named — the psalmist's maintained innocence that seems futile (Psa 73:13), and Samaria's incapacity for innocence under sustained idolatry (Hos 8:5).

---

##### T1.2.3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame as experienced inner state is the felt collapse of a person's inner dignity, confidence, and standing — produced by exposure to what exceeds one's moral capacity, by the failure or destruction of what one trusted, or by the discovery of one's own moral failure before God and community. The experience is inner (the collapse happens within), relational (it always has a referent — God, enemies, community, self-assessment), and directional (it drives the person toward concealment, withdrawal, or stillness). It manifests across three registers in the evidence: as an unjust wound received from enemies or circumstances (M07-A), as a deserved moral consequence of sin and folly (M07-B), and as the appropriate inner response of the person before God's holiness (M07-C). The characteristic is primarily a condition rather than an act, though it has volitional dimensions. Its vocabulary centres on *bosh*, *ke.lim.mah*, *aischunē*, and their cognates.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Humiliation as enforced abasement is the condition of a person, people, or pride-structure whose standing has been actively moved downward by an external agent. The mechanism is external enforcement: the person is brought low rather than choosing lowness. The experience is primarily social and bodily (disgrace that bars re-entry to public life, the retreat of the defeated, the stripped crown) but carries an inner dimension. Primary vocabulary: ka.lam, sha.phel, bosh (defeat/abasement register), atimia (mortal dishonor), qa.lon (pride reversed).

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Dishonour as relational worth-denial is the act or condition of treating a person as having less worth than they actually possess — either through the willful refusal to acknowledge worth (VCG-01) or through the objective assignment of diminished standing (VCG-02). It operates relationally, always with a dishonour-er and a dishonoured. Primary vocabulary: atimazō, atimia, entrepō (in its absence register), paradeigmatizō, kataischunō (in the head-covering symbolic-disrespect register).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment is the conscience's recognition that certain conduct, objects, or inner orientations violate the moral propriety established by God's standard and mediated through created order, community norms, and scripture. It is the evaluative-qualitative dimension of shame (what is shameful) rather than the experiential dimension (what shame feels like). Primary vocabulary: aischros, aschēmosunē. Secondary: aischunē and atimia in their evaluative registers. Three registers: the shameful quality of conduct/objects, the shameful quality of disordered desires, and the inverted evaluative faculty that treats shameful as honourable.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Shame produced by contempt and rejection is the condition of being treated as of diminished or no worth by another's active contempt — whether through dismissive inner attitude (VCG-01), violent mockery and rejection (VCG-02), or reputation-destroying speech (VCG-03). The mechanism is contempt (M06's characteristic); the characteristic within M07 is the shame produced in the recipient by that contempt. Cross-register note: M06 (contempt-projection) is the source-side; CHAR-5 is the received face of the same dynamic. Primary vocabulary: exoutheneō (the dominant term across VCG-01's 11 verses); atimazō (Mar 12:4; Luk 20:11 in VCG-02); loidoria (1Ti 5:14; 1Pe 3:9 in VCG-03).

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Innocence as structural counter to shame is the inner moral state of a blameless conscience and clean-handed will — the condition in which the person is free from the deliberate moral failure that would produce guilt-shame before God or community. CHAR-6 is the positive moral condition that protects against M07-C's guilt-shame register: when CHAR-6 is present, the person can approach God without the barrier of guilt-shame; when CHAR-6 is absent or its capacity is lost, the guilt-shame condition of M07-C is inevitable. Primary vocabulary: niq.qa.von (H5356A) and qe.ha.von (H5356B), shared across the 4 verse-records (8 verse_context rows because of the two-term structure). Cross-register note: M12 (purity/holiness) is the terms' primary register; they are retained in M07 because every verse evidences the innocence-shame polarity directly.

---

#### T1.3 — Boundary

##### T1.3.1 — What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The structural opposite is *honour* or *dignity* — the inner standing, confidence, and worth-recognition that shame displaces. The evidence names this opposition explicitly: "instead of your shame there shall be a double portion" (Isa 61:7); "I will change their shame into praise and renown" (Zep 3:19); shame and honour are the opposing poles throughout the royal clothing metaphors (enemies clothed with shame vs. the king's crown shining, Psa 132:18). The M07-C evidence (VCG-02) identifies trust in God as the present experiential opposite of shame — the inner act that protects against shame's collapse. The evidence also identifies innocence (M07-H, niq.qa.von) as the structural inner-being counterpart — the blameless conscience that shields against guilt-shame. At the deepest level, the structural opposite of shame is the inner confidence that one's standing is secure — before God, before community, within oneself.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The structural opposite is exaltation — the upward movement that CHAR-2 reverses. The sha.phel evidence pairs them explicitly: "he brings low and he exalts" (1Sa 2:7); "putting down one and lifting up another" (Psa 75:7); "bring low that which is exalted, exalt that which is low" (Eze 21:26, vc=21185). 1Cor 15:43 (sown in dishonor, raised in glory) is the eschatological statement of the structural opposite.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The structural opposite of CHAR-3 is honour — the active acknowledgment of another's worth. The evidence pairs dishonour and honour explicitly: "I honor my Father, and you dishonor me" (Joh 8:49); "some for honorable use, some for dishonorable" (Rom 9:21; 2Ti 2:20).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The structural opposite of CHAR-4 is the honourable, the proper, the decent — conduct and objects that can bear scrutiny before God and community. The evidence pairs these: "we refuse to practice cunning or to tamper with God's word, but by the open statement of the truth we would commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" (2Cor 4:2) — the honourable opposite of shameful underhanded ways is open, truthful conduct that commends itself to the conscience.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The structural opposite of CHAR-5 is acceptance and worth-recognition — the act of receiving another as of genuine value. Gal 4:14 (vc=54647) names the positive opposite directly: "you did not scorn or despise me, but received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus." The Galatians' acceptance of Paul despite his weakness is the structural opposite of contempt-producing-shame.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The structural opposite of CHAR-6 is guilt — the inner moral condition that produces guilt-shame and bars approach to God. The evidence names this opposite indirectly: Hos 8:5 — incapacity for innocence — names the state that is CHAR-6's absence, which is sustained in idolatry and sin. Psa 73:13's maintained innocence that seems futile would, if abandoned, produce the guilt-condition that would make guilt-shame appropriate.

---

##### T1.3.2 — What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame in its acute form excludes the upright face, bold speech, confident self-presentation, and the capacity to approach. The covering of the face (Jer 14:3; Eze 7:18), the inability to lift the face toward God (Ezr 9:6), the shutting of the mouth (Eze 16:63 — "never open your mouth again because of your shame"), the backward turning (Psa 35:4; 129:5) — all evidence what shame excludes. In the M07-B seared-conscience register, the absence of shame is what the wicked person has achieved — they have excluded shame from their inner repertoire, which is not a positive attainment but a moral collapse. Shame also resists the fraudulent: blameless conduct produces opponents' shame precisely because it refuses to give them grounds for accusation (Tit 2:8; 1Pe 3:16).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 excludes the continued self-elevation of pride. The VCG-03 evidence (Isa 2 series; 5:15; 13:11) shows God's enforced abasement targeting every form of proud self-positioning — haughty looks, pompous display, confident ability (Isa 25:11). Military defeat (VCG-02) excludes confident national power. Social demotion (VCG-01) excludes the assumption that social position is permanent.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 excludes the recognition of the other's worth. In VCG-01, what is excluded is the inner movement of regard (entrepō) — the judge who lacks inner deference toward God and persons has excluded the worth-recognition act from his inner repertoire.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 excludes conduct that can bear open scrutiny (2Cor 4:2 — "shameful, underhanded ways" are the opposite of openness). CHAR-4 excludes proper appetitive ordering (VCG-02 — "dishonorable passions" are the corruption of natural relations). CHAR-4 excludes genuine moral seriousness: "it is shameful even to speak of the things that they do in secret" (Eph 5:12) — shameful conduct excludes the possibility of open acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 excludes the genuine worth-recognition that should accompany the person. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3 — "do not despise the one who abstains"; 1Cor 16:11 — "let no one despise him"; 1Th 5:20 — "do not despise prophecies") reveal what CHAR-5 excludes: the recognition that what is being dismissed has genuine worth that the contemptuous attitude cancels.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 explicitly excludes the deliberate moral failure that produces guilt. The "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" (Gen 20:5) excludes intentional sin of the heart and willful wrongdoing of the hands. The "I wash my hands in innocence" (Psa 26:6) excludes participation in the conduct of the wicked — Psa 26:4-5 (contextually) shows that innocence is maintained by refusing association with deceitful, hypocritical, and evil persons.

---

##### T1.3.3 — What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 is not M07-D (humiliation as enforced abasement), which concerns the external, social, downward movement of standing rather than the inner felt state. CHAR-1 is not M07-F (shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment), which concerns the qualitative assessment of what is shameful rather than the experience of being ashamed. CHAR-1 is not guilt per se (M12 territory) — guilt is the fact of moral failure, shame is the felt inner response to it. Shame can exist without guilt (M07-A — unjust wound) and guilt can exist without felt shame (M07-B seared conscience). CHAR-1 is not contempt-produced shame (M07-G), though contempt can trigger shame. The boundary with M07-C (shame before God) is within CHAR-1 itself by the volume-split; the boundary with M07-D is that humiliation can happen without shame being experienced (you can be publicly demoted without feeling the inner collapse).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is not CHAR-1 (the felt inner experience). CHAR-2 is not CHAR-4 (shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment). CHAR-2 is not voluntary lowliness — the sha.phel verses of Pro 16:19 and 29:23 were set aside precisely because the voluntary-lowliness register belongs to M09, not CHAR-2's enforced mechanism.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is not CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing): dishonour as worth-denial is a relational judgment that can be made without the external enforcement mechanism of CHAR-2. CHAR-3 is not CHAR-1 (the felt inner shame-experience of the one dishonoured): dishonour-as-worth-denial is the act directed at the person, not the inner experience of the person receiving it. CHAR-3 is not CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): contempt is the attitudinal-mechanism of dismissal; dishonour-as-worth-denial names the relational verdict.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is not CHAR-1 (the felt experience of shame): CHAR-4 is the conscience's assessment of what is shameful, not the felt collapse of dignity in the person who experiences shame. CHAR-4 is not CHAR-2 (enforced humiliation of standing): shamefulness as a quality of conduct is a moral-evaluative determination, not a social-enforced downward movement. CHAR-4 is not CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial): dishonour is what one does to another; shamefulness is the quality of conduct assessed by conscience against a standard.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is not CHAR-2 (enforced humiliation of standing): contempt-produced shame is the received experience of worth-cancellation, not a socially enacted downward movement of standing (though contempt can produce both simultaneously). CHAR-5 is not CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial): contempt is a specific form of worth-denial; CHAR-3's worth-denial can arise from other causes (favoritism, sovereign assignment). CHAR-5 is the received shame, not the contempt itself (that is M06).

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)
