CHAR-6 is not CHAR-4 (shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment): CHAR-4 is the conscience's evaluative assessment of what is shameful in conduct or objects; CHAR-6 is the positive moral condition that protects the person against guilt-shame. CHAR-6 is not CHAR-1 (the felt experience of shame): CHAR-6 is the inner condition that, when present, prevents the felt shame-experience that CHAR-1 describes. CHAR-6 is related to but not identical with M12 (purity/holiness): M12's primary register is cultic and ritual purity; CHAR-6's specific function is the inner moral purity that protects against guilt-shame in the M07 context.

---

#### T1.4 — Modes of Operation

##### T1.4.1 — In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Four distinct operational modes emerge: (1) **Passive reception** — shame falls upon the person from outside (enemies, circumstances, misplaced trust collapsing; M07-A-VCG-01, -02). The person does not choose it; it arrives as the inner impact of what is done to them. (2) **Guilt-collapse** — shame arises from within, produced by the person's own moral failure as it stands before their conscience and before God; the "face that cannot be lifted" mode (M07-C-VCG-01; Ezr 9:6). (3) **Corrective induction** — shame is deployed instrumentally by another (Paul: 1Cor 6:5; community discipline: 2Th 3:14) or activated by encounter (Eze 43:10-11 — the temple's perfection producing shame). (4) **Voluntary acceptance** — shame is consciously borne for a greater purpose; the servant not hiding the face from spitting (Isa 50:6); the apostles rejoicing in dishonour for Christ (Act 5:41); Jesus despising the cross's shame (Heb 12:2). These four modes operate differently on the person's faculties, especially volition (see T3.6).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Four operational modes: (1) Social/bodily demotion (VCG-01): enacted through bodily signs (shaved beard, stripped crown, forced lowly seat) or speechlessness (Mat 22:12, vc=30397). (2) Military-national collapse (VCG-02): enacted through military defeat, cities broken, national identity stripped. (3) Divine sovereign abasement (VCG-03): God's judicial act against the proud inner disposition — the Day of the Lord targeting everything self-exalted. (4) Enduring carried burden (VCG-04): humiliation persisting beyond the immediate event — carried into death (Eze 32), restricting priestly access indefinitely (Eze 44:13, vc=37496).

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Two operational modes: (1) Active willful dishonour (VCG-01): the inner disposition of refused-acknowledgment enacted toward specific persons — Jesus, the poor man, the Lawgiver, apostolic authority-bearers. (2) Structural or assigned dishonour (VCG-02): dishonour as an objective condition assigned by sovereign authority, created order, or received social treatment.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Three operational modes corresponding to the three VCGs: (1) Conscience identifying shameful conduct and objects (VCG-01): the moral-recognitive operation of the conscience that names specific conduct-types or objects as shameful — deeds in secret are so degraded that speaking of them is shameful (Eph 5:12). (2) Conscience identifying shameful inner desires (VCG-02): the moral-recognitive operation identifying certain appetites as the inner driving force of moral disorder — dishonorable passions (Rom 1:26). (3) Inverted conscience (VCG-03): the corruption of the evaluative faculty itself — glorying in shame (Phili 3:19), loving dishonour (Hos 4:18).

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Three operational modes (VCGs 01-03): (1) Dismissive inner attitude (VCG-01): the inner disposition of treating others as of no account — self-righteous contempt (Luk 18:9), contempt toward fellow believers over food practices (Rom 14:3; 14:10), contemptuous low regard for certain members (1Cor 6:4). (2) Active contempt through violence and mockery (VCG-02): the contempt is enacted physically — servants beaten (Mar 12:4; Luk 20:11), Jesus mocked (Luk 23:11), Jesus rejected by the builders (Act 4:11), Bartimaeus's beggar-identity formed by contempt (Mar 10:50). (3) Verbal contempt (VCG-03): reputation-destroying speech — reviling (1Ti 5:14; 1Pe 3:9), hostile verbal contempt (Act 19:9), the scoffer's verbal dishonour (Pro 22:10).

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Two operational modes (VCGs 01-02): (1) Active inner defence (VCG-01): innocence functioning as the enabling condition for approach to God (Psa 26:6 — "I wash my hands in innocence and go around your altar") and as the basis for vindication before God (Gen 20:5 — Abimelech's appeal to innocence is accepted by God). (2) Questioned or lost capacity (VCG-02): innocence whose protective function seems to fail (Psa 73:13 — maintained innocence appearing futile), or whose capacity is entirely lost through sustained idolatry (Hos 8:5 — incapacity for innocence).

---

##### T1.4.2 — Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, the three sub-group registers evidence three contextual modes. M07-A (unjust wound): shame operates as a received wound — the inner impact is felt as injustice, and the resolution is divine vindication. M07-B (moral consequence): shame operates as deserved outcome — the inner experience registers moral reality accurately. M07-C (divine encounter): shame operates at the vertical level — it is the inner posture of the creature before the holy, with the specific quality that it can be the gateway to renewed relationship (Eze 43:11). The M07-C mode is constitutionally deeper: it engages the person's standing before God rather than their standing before community or circumstance. The moral-consequence mode (M07-B) is the most cognitively engaged — it involves moral self-assessment. The unjust-wound mode (M07-A) is the most affectively prominent — the pain of undeserved exposure.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

In VCG-01, CHAR-2 operates at the body-community interface — the body bears the sign; community recognises it. In VCG-02, it operates at the collective/political level. In VCG-03, it operates at the spirit/will level — God targets the inner disposition of pride (haughty eyes, inner orientation of self-exaltation) and brings it down. Constitutional depth varies: VCG-01 is most body-proximate; VCG-03 is most spirit-proximate.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 operates differently depending on whether the worth-denial is directed at God (Joh 8:49; Rom 2:23), at humans (Jam 2:6; Luk 18:2/4), or at divinely ordered authority structures (1Cor 11:4-5, vc=35009/35010). The God-directed mode carries the highest moral weight; the human-directed mode carries strong relational consequence; the authority-structure mode is mediated through symbolic bodily acts.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 operates differently depending on the object of the evaluative judgment. When the conscience evaluates external conduct (VCG-01), it is assessing what actions or objects are shameful in relation to community norms and God's standard. When it evaluates inner desires (VCG-02), it is assessing the quality of the appetitive faculty itself. When it inverts (VCG-03), the evaluative faculty itself is the subject of concern rather than any specific conduct or desire.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 operates differently in each VCG. In VCG-01, the shame is produced through gradual social devaluation — the cumulative effect of being treated as of no account over time. In VCG-02, the shame arrives suddenly through violent or dramatic public contempt — these are acute events. In VCG-03, the shame is produced through speech and its effect on reputation — a more sustained, public, and socially mediated form.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 operates differently in the two VCGs. In VCG-01, it operates as the active shield — the functioning inner moral condition that enables approach and protects against guilt-shame. In VCG-02, it operates as the questioned or absent shield — the innocence that either seems not to protect (Psa 73:13) or is no longer accessible (Hos 8:5). The two modes together reveal the full range of CHAR-6's operation: its positive functioning and its failure-modes.

---

##### T1.4.3 — Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, with a striking characteristic: shame's primary communicative expression is *silence*. Eze 16:63 (vc=65575) — "never open your mouth again because of your shame" — names this directly. The sinner before atonement is silenced by shame. Job 10:15 (vc=37502) — "I cannot lift up my head" — evidences the non-verbal, postural form of shame's expression. The head-covering gestures (Jer 14:3; Eze 7:18) are communicative but nonverbal. The M07-A-VCG-03 evidence (Act 8:32, vc=28925) — the lamb silent before the shearer — presents silence as the appropriate inner-outer expression of bearing unjust shame with willed stillness. Conversely, bold speech is what shame suppresses: the psalmist who speaks of God's testimonies before kings "shall not be put to shame" (Psa 119:46) — trust enables speech; shame removes it.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, through silencing. The fimoō evidence (Mat 22:12 — man rendered speechless; Mat 22:34 — Sadducees publicly silenced) shows humiliation enacted through the withdrawal of the capacity to speak. The humiliated nation becomes the object of others' speech (Jer 48:39 — "Moab has become a derision") while losing its own voice.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 has a communicative mode through symbolic bodily acts (1Cor 11:4-5 — the covered and uncovered heads carrying messages of disrespect toward divinely ordered authority) and through explicit verbal declaration (Joh 8:49 — "you dishonor me" — the accusers' verbal engagement being itself the dishonouring act).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 has a communicative mode: the conscience that has recognised shamefulness can articulate it. 1Cor 14:35 ("it is shameful for a woman to speak in church") is the articulated moral evaluation. 2Cor 4:2's renunciation of shameful ways is the public declaration of the conscience's finding. The inverted conscience of Phili 3:19 "glories in their shame" — it communicates its corrupted evaluation as honour.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 has a specific speech-based mode: VCG-03 is constituted by verbal contempt. The reviling (loidoria) is the speech-act; the reputation-attack is the effect. 1Pe 3:9 (vc=37632) — "do not repay evil for evil or reviling for reviling, but on the contrary bless" — shows the speech-based form of CHAR-5 and the appropriate speech-based counter-response. The inner will is directed away from retaliatory verbal attack toward blessing.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 has a communicative mode through the gesture of hand-washing (Psa 26:6): the ritual washing of hands before approaching God's altar is the public declaration of the conscience's claim to innocence. This is CHAR-6 communicated symbolically through a bodily act that the community and God can observe. Abimelech's verbal declaration (Gen 20:5) is CHAR-6 communicated through direct speech — the person states their innocence explicitly before God.

---

#### T1.5 — Immediate Response

##### T1.5.1 — What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The evidence points to three closely related immediate responses: (1) **Collapse** — the inner state of confidence and standing falls. The psalmist's honour "turned into shame" (Psa 4:2, vc=37469); shame fills Job's inner being so completely that he cannot lift his head (Job 10:15, vc=37502). (2) **Concealment** — the face is covered, the head lowered: servants covering their heads (Jer 14:3, vc=38535/65555), horror covering bodies alongside shame (Eze 7:18, vc=34978), Jerusalem groaning and turning her face away (Lam 1:8, vc=21682). (3) **Turmoil** — enemies' confident opposition collapsing into "sudden, disorienting disgrace" (Psa 6:10, vc=34839 — "ashamed and greatly troubled"). These three are facets of the same immediate response: the inner collapse of standing expressed in bodily posture and inner agitation.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The most immediate response to enforced humiliation is inner collapse of standing and confidence paired with withdrawal or retreat. The shaved envoys cannot return to public life (2Sa 10:5, vc=38517). The people "stole into the city... like those ashamed of fleeing battle" (2Sa 19:3, vc=38518). The withered-grass image (2Ki 19:26, vc=65493; Isa 37:27, vc=65537) — "shorn of strength, dismayed and confounded" — captures the total-collapse quality of the immediate response.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The most immediate inner response to receiving CHAR-3 depends on the worth-denial mode. In the active-willful mode (VCG-01), the focus in most verses is on the dishonorer's inner disposition rather than the dishonoured's immediate response. Joh 8:49 — Jesus responding to dishonour by redirecting to the honoring of his Father — shows the possibility of a response that does not absorb the worth-denial but deflects it. In the structural mode (VCG-02), Paul endures dishonour "through honor and dishonor" (2Cor 6:8, vc=34963) without his inner integrity being altered.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The immediate response to genuine recognition of shamefulness (functioning CHAR-4) is recoil and renunciation: Paul renounces disgraceful, underhanded ways (2Cor 4:2). The conscience that recognises Eph 5:12's deeds as shameful will not name them — the immediate response is avoidance of speech and act. In the inverted mode (VCG-03), the immediate response is glorying — the conscience, having inverted its evaluative standard, embraces what it should recoil from.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The most immediate inner response to CHAR-5 is wounded worth — the inner experience of having one's worth cancelled. Psa 14:6 (vc=65498) — "shame the plans of the poor" — shows CHAR-5 targeting the inner confidence and hope of the poor. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) shows the accumulated inner-being effect of long-sustained contempt-shame: his identity has been formed around the shame-condition produced by society's contempt. 1Pe 3:9's call to bless rather than retaliate shows the acute immediate pull toward retaliatory speech when verbal contempt is received.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The most immediate inner response associated with functioning CHAR-6 (VCG-01) is confidence for approach — the person who has clean hands and a blameless heart can go around God's altar (Psa 26:6) without the collapse of confidence that guilt-shame would produce. The immediate response to the loss of CHAR-6 (Hos 8:5) is the inability to attain the inner purity that would enable approach — the question "how long will they be incapable?" names a state of persistent inner incapacity that bars the approach CHAR-6 would enable.

---

##### T1.5.2 — Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The collapse-concealment-turmoil cluster is consistent as the core immediate response. However, it varies by mode. In the voluntary-acceptance mode (M07-A-VCG-03), the immediate response to shame's threat is not collapse but willed steadiness: Jesus "despising the shame" (Heb 12:2); the servant setting his face like flint (Isa 50:7, vc=65546); Paul not being ashamed because his authority is genuinely from God (2Cor 10:8, vc=34830). In the corrective mode, the immediate response is moral activation — "they consecrated themselves" (2Ch 30:15, vc=38506) — shame prompting action rather than paralysis. The variation confirms that CHAR-1 is a condition with multiple operational modes (T1.4.1), not a single-track response.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Broadly consistent in the collapse-withdrawal pattern but with VCG variation. VCG-01: the body bears the sign and cannot re-enter public space until removed. VCG-02: collective wailing, flight, announcement of disgrace to neighbours. VCG-03: confusion, terror, going "in confusion together" (Isa 45:16).

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The evidence varies. Some verses focus on the dishonorer (Luk 18:2/4 — the judge's character trait); others on the dishonoured person's response (2Cor 6:8 — Paul's sustained integrity; Joh 8:49 — Jesus's redirection). No single consistent immediate response is described across the 15-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Variation exists between VCGs. VCG-01 immediate response: recoil and renunciation. VCG-02: moral-recognitive identification of disordered desire as dishonorable. VCG-03: glorying (the inverted response). The variation confirms the three distinct registers of CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The immediate response varies by VCG. In VCG-01 (dismissive inner attitude), the immediate response may be subtle — a gradual loss of confidence and standing. In VCG-02 (violent rejection), the response is acute wound. In VCG-03 (verbal attack), the immediate pull is toward retaliation, which 1Pe 3:9 specifically addresses.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The immediate response varies by VCG. VCG-01: confidence for approach (Psa 26:6), vindication-appeal to God (Gen 20:5). VCG-02: existential questioning of innocence's value (Psa 73:13), persistent incapacity and inability to approach (Hos 8:5).

---

##### T1.5.3 — Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The evidence is relatively complete on immediate response; the verse corpus is unusually rich in phenomenological detail about the experience of shame. No significant silence on this prompt.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

Judg 18:7 (vc=38529): Pass A notes the term may not be active; no clear inner-being immediate response evidenced. Mar 4:39 (vc=30401) and Mar 1:25/Luk 4:35 fimoō verses apply to demons and the storm — no human inner-being immediate response evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The evidence is substantially silent on the immediate inner-being response of the one who receives dishonour. The corpus is focused on the dishonorer's inner disposition. Silent on this specific area.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The evidence is substantially focused on the evaluator's conscience rather than the experience of those whose conduct is evaluated. Silent on an extensive immediate-response description.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The evidence is largely silent on the sustained inner-being response of the despised person — the focus is often on the contempt-er's inner disposition rather than the recipient's experience. The beggar-identity of Bartimaeus (Mar 10:50) is the most sustained description of how contempt-shaped shame forms a person's inner self-understanding over time. Silent on many verses' depiction of the recipient's full inner response.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse corpus is compact and does not provide extensive description of the range of immediate responses to CHAR-6's presence or absence. Silent on more extensive immediate-response description.

---

#### T1.6 — Sustained Effect

##### T1.6.1 — What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Three long-term patterns emerge from the evidence. (1) **Sustained inner wound** — Psa 44:15 (vc=37310/37473): "all day long my disgrace is before me, and shame has covered my face" — shame as perpetual condition. Jer 20:18 (vc=37316): "spend my days in shame" — shame as the chronic condition of Jeremiah's existence. The ke.lim.mah passages in Eze 32:24-30 (shame "carried into death") show shame persisting as an inner-social verdict even beyond life. (2) **Moral desensitisation** — sustained absence of appropriate shame produces the seared conscience (Jer 6:15; 8:12). The long-term effect of refusing corrective shame is hardening: "brazen forehead, refuses to be ashamed" (Jer 3:3, vc=38501). (3) **Identity formation** — Jeremiah's chronic shame becomes part of his identity (Jer 20:18); Israel's shame is carried generationally (Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers to this day"). Sustained shame either wounds identity (chronic inner burden) or is consciously borne (VCG-03 register) or is resolved by divine act.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

In the enduring-burden mode (VCG-04), CHAR-2 produces an identity-constituting shame-condition that outlasts the immediate humiliation event. Eze 32's warriors "bearing their shame" into death — the humiliation becomes permanently attached to their identity-record. Eze 44:13 — Levites bearing their shame as a permanent structural restriction on their access to God's presence. Jer 23:40 (vc=37498) — "everlasting reproach and perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — names the deposit as permanent identity-marking.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In the active-dishonour mode (VCG-01), the sustained effect on the dishonorer is the deepening of the moral failure that dishonour represents: Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — is a self-contradicting inner stance that, sustained, produces the very judgment the person sought to escape. In the structural mode (VCG-02), the sustained effect on the dishonoured is the identity-condition of diminished standing — 2Ti 2:20's vessel for dishonorable use.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

For the functioning conscience: sustained CHAR-4 produces moral discipline — the person who recognises shamefulness and renounces it builds a pattern of conduct that "commends itself to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" (2Cor 4:2). For the inverted conscience: sustained CHAR-4 inversion produces the deepening of moral perversion — "their end is destruction" (Phili 3:19). The Hos 4:18 rulers' "deep affection for dishonour" shows sustained perversion establishing a stable disposition of shameful-love.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Sustained CHAR-5 produces identity-formation around contempt-derived shame: Bartimaeus's "beggar identity" (Mar 10:50, vc=37238) — the cloak is the symbol of an identity shaped by sustained social contempt. The commands against sustained contempt (1Cor 16:11 — guarding Timothy against dismissive contempt; 1Th 5:20 — not despising prophetic speech) reveal that sustained contempt damages the standing and functioning capacity of the person or ministry being despised.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Sustained CHAR-6 (VCG-01's maintained innocence) produces the long-term condition of unhindered access to God — the person whose moral integrity is sustained can continue to "go around the altar" (Psa 26:6) without the interruption that guilt would produce. Sustained incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) produces the long-term condition of blocked access to God — the idolatrous people cannot attain innocence and therefore cannot approach God without the barrier of guilt-shame.

---

##### T1.6.2 — What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In the unjust-wound register (M07-A), sustained shame establishes vulnerability and isolation — Psa 127:5, the man without sons "put to shame when he speaks with his enemies" — chronic social exposure. In the moral-consequence register (M07-B), sustained appropriate shame ought to produce contrition and return; but where it is resisted, it establishes moral hardening (Jer 3:3; 6:15; 8:12). In the divine-encounter register (M07-C), sustained appropriate shame before God establishes the foundation for renewed relationship — Eze 43:11: shame is the precondition for receiving the temple's full design, meaning shame functions as an ongoing gateway posture before God, not merely a one-time event. The corrective-shame passages (entropē — 1Cor 6:5; 15:34) show shame intended to establish heightened moral sensitivity and community accountability.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Sustained CHAR-2 produces two trajectories: (1) Permanent exclusion from former standing (Eze 44:13 — Levites permanently barred; Sennacherib's disgrace following him into his own temple, 2Ch 32:21, vc=37326). (2) Eschatological orientation: 1Cor 15:43's sustained state of bodily humiliation (mortal existence in dishonor) is the condition that anticipates the eschatological transformation to glory — sustained dishonor is not the final word.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

For the dishonorer: sustained CHAR-3 toward God or persons establishes moral self-contradiction (Rom 2:23), the erosion of the worth-recognition capacity (Luk 18:2/4 — the judge whose lack of regard is a recognized character trait), and exposure to the same dishonour one inflicts (Heb 6:6). For the dishonoured: sustained received dishonour either establishes identity-in-diminished-standing (VCG-02) or, in Paul's case, demonstrates that inner integrity can be sustained despite external dishonour (2Cor 6:8).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 sustained: habituated moral discernment — the established capacity to recognise and renounce the shameful. Inverted CHAR-4 sustained: moral blindness — the established incapacity to see what is actually shameful, and the established love of what disgraces (Hos 4:18). These deposits shape the person's long-term moral trajectory.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Sustained CHAR-5 can establish: (1) Identity-in-contempt (the beggar-identity): the person's self-understanding is formed around the shame the world has assigned them. (2) Ministry incapacity: sustained contempt toward a person's role or ministry undermines the relational authority needed for that ministry to function. (3) Retaliatory disposition (VCG-03): sustained verbal contempt can produce the pull toward retaliatory reviling that 1Pe 3:9 addresses.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Sustained CHAR-6 establishes the orientation toward God that approach and worship require. Psa 73:13's lament — "all in vain have I kept my heart clean" — shows that the sustained maintenance of CHAR-6 even under suffering is itself a formative practice that, when vindicated by God, produces deepened trust. The sustained loss of CHAR-6's capacity (Hos 8:5) establishes the alienated condition that bars the covenant relationship from functioning.

---

##### T1.6.3 — Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, markedly. The immediate response is acute — the collapse, the covering, the turmoil. The sustained effect is more varied. Where shame is unjust and unresolved, the sustained effect is chronic inner burden — Jer 20:18 ("spend my days in shame"), Psa 44:15 ("all day long"). Where shame is the appropriate response to sin and is received as such, the sustained effect is the opening of the moral gateway — contrition, restored relationship, renewed obedience. Where shame is refused, the sustained effect is moral hardening. Where shame is voluntarily borne, the sustained effect is vindication — the servant's face like flint (Isa 50:7), the apostles rejoicing (Act 5:41). The asymmetry between immediate collapse and sustained transformation is characteristic of CHAR-1's complexity.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. The immediate response is acute collapse and withdrawal; the sustained effect is either permanent identity-marking (warriors bearing shame into death) or eschatological transition point (the mortal body's dishonor as the staging ground for resurrection glory). The difference is temporal depth.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The sustained effect for the dishonorer differs from the immediate: the immediate is the specific act of worth-denial; the sustained is the character formation in the direction of the failed worth-recognition capacity.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The sustained effect differs from the immediate. The immediate is the specific evaluative act (recognising shamefulness or glorying in it); the sustained is the character formation in the direction of the conscience's habituated orientation — either toward moral discernment or toward moral blindness.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The sustained effect differs from the immediate: the immediate is the acute wound of being treated as of no account; the sustained is the formation of a shame-shaped identity or the erosion of ministry capacity. The resolution of the sustained effect requires a re-worth-assignment from outside (Jesus calling Bartimaeus — Act 4:11's cornerstone vindication) that overrides the contempt-system's accumulated verdict.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The sustained effect differs from the immediate: the immediate is the specific moment of approach (enabled or blocked) or vindication (granted or withheld); the sustained is the long-term pattern of relational capacity with God — either maintained through moral integrity or eroded through the accumulation of moral failure that makes innocence-capacity impossible.

---

#### T1.7 — Conditions of Reception

##### T1.7.1 — What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The M07-C evidence is most direct: (1) **Conscience remaining operative** — those who "know how to blush" (the positive state behind Jer 6:15's negation) have the inner faculty intact. The priests whose conscience-shame moved them to consecration (2Ch 30:15, vc=38506) had a functional conscience that could receive shame's signal. (2) **Moral self-awareness** — Jer 31:19 (vc=38509/65562): "after I was instructed, I struck my thigh; I was ashamed" — instruction activates shame, meaning the cognitive faculty must be engaged to produce the shame response. (3) **Willingness to face what is true** — Eze 43:10: the house of Israel must be willing to "measure the plan" after shame — shame produces constructive response only when the will cooperates.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The inner condition enabling CHAR-2 to function correctively (rather than merely destructively) is openness to recognising proper standing. The entrepō evidence (Mat 21:37; Mar 12:6; Luk 20:13 — the son whose presence should produce respect) shows that the expected inner disposition of regard would have made CHAR-2's corrective impact possible. Where the person remains open to recognising their proper standing before God, CHAR-2 can fulfil its purpose.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The inner condition enabling CHAR-3's avoidance is the inner faculty of regard (entrepō): "fearing God and respecting man" (Luk 18:2) — the worth-recognition capacity operating properly. For the dishonoured, grounded knowledge of one's standing before God enables receiving external dishonour without inner displacement (2Cor 6:8 — Paul's sustained integrity).

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The inner condition enabling CHAR-4's functioning is the conscience calibrated to God's standard: the person whose conscience operates by the reference to "everyone's conscience in the sight of God" (2Cor 4:2) will recognise the shameful. The condition blocking proper CHAR-4 functioning is the conscience's inversion: when the evaluative standard is "earthly things" (Phili 3:19) rather than God's holiness, the faculty inverts and identifies the shameful as honourable.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The inner condition enabling the person who receives CHAR-5 to respond rightly (without retaliation, with blessing instead of reviling) is grounded confidence in God's worth-assignment. 1Pe 3:9 — not returning reviling with reviling — requires the will's orientation toward the calling ("you were called to this, that you may obtain a blessing"). The Galatians' non-contemptuous reception of Paul (Gal 4:14) — "received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus" — shows what enables reception of worth-denied persons: the theological vision that sees God's messenger regardless of physical weakness.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The inner condition enabling CHAR-6's functioning is the freely exercised moral will that avoids deliberate wrongdoing. Gen 20:5's "integrity of my heart" — the heart not divided between God and deliberate sin — is the enabling condition. Psa 26:6's hand-washing implies that moral maintenance requires ongoing choice: the psalmist actively maintains innocence by choosing not to participate in the conduct of the wicked (Psa 26:4-5 context).

---

##### T1.7.2 — What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The M07-B seared-conscience evidence (VCG-04) identifies the primary blocking condition: the hardened inner conscience that "refuses to be ashamed" (Jer 3:3, vc=38501). The brazen forehead, the lost capacity to blush — these represent the destruction of the shame-receptive faculty through sustained moral resistance. The M07-B idolatry register (VCG-02) identifies a secondary blocking condition: investment in the false object (the idol) so total that the shame of its exposure cannot be received without cognitive collapse. The M07-A-VCG-02 evidence shows that misplaced trust also blocks appropriate shame: those who trusted Egypt could not receive the shame signal until Egypt visibly failed (Isa 20:5; 30:3-5).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Pride is the primary blocking condition. The same inner disposition that makes CHAR-2 necessary (pride, self-exaltation) is also what resists its message. Pro 11:2 (vc=37501): "when pride comes, then comes disgrace" — pride does not anticipate the humiliation it invites. Nations whose pride was total receive CHAR-2 as external shock because they could not self-correct.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The inner condition that generates CHAR-3 is the inner disposition of self-sufficiency or self-deception: the self-contradicting inner stance of Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — shows how self-deception blocks genuine moral perception of others' worth.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The inner condition that blocks proper CHAR-4 functioning is the replacement of God's standard with an earthly one — "their god is their belly" (Phili 3:19) is the substitute-standard that inverts the evaluation. Once the standard is corrupted, the evaluative act produces inverted results.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The inner condition blocking proper response to received CHAR-5 is the retaliatory-contempt disposition — the tendency to respond to being despised by despising back. 1Pe 3:9 addresses precisely this blocking condition. On the contempt-er's side, what blocks the person from recognising their contempt as wrong is self-righteousness (Luk 18:9 — trusting in themselves that they were righteous produces contempt toward others).

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The inner condition blocking CHAR-6's functioning is sustained idolatry and the moral distortion it produces. Hos 8:5 — "how long will they be incapable of innocence?" — names the blocking condition: the sustained worship of the golden calf of Samaria has so distorted the inner moral faculty that the capacity for innocence is no longer accessible. Idolatry replaces the true object of moral formation (God) with a false one, distorting the conscience and will until innocence-capacity is lost.

---

##### T1.7.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Two distinct non-reception states emerge. (1) **Moral hardening** — the person who refuses shame's corrective signal (Jer 3:3; 6:15) is in a state of inner desensitisation: the conscience cannot register what should register. The immediate consequence is ongoing sin without corrective friction, and the long-term consequence is divine judgment (Jer 6:15 — "therefore they shall fall among those who fall"). (2) **Willed resilience** — the person in the voluntary-acceptance register (M07-A-VCG-03; Heb 12:2; Isa 50:7) does not receive shame's collapse-signal not through hardening but through the stronger orientation of will toward a greater object. Jesus "despising the shame" is not moral hardening — it is the engagement of a greater joy. Paul "will not be ashamed" because his authority is genuinely from God — not denial of the shame-pressure but its resolution through grounded confidence. These two non-reception states are analytically distinct: the first is pathological (inner death), the second is volitionally mature (inner strength).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Two possibilities: (1) Hardened defiance — the person undergoes humiliation and either doubles down on pride or cannot integrate the corrective signal. (2) Dissolved without transformation — the nations "shorn of strength" (Isa 37:27) are "reduced to withered plants" — CHAR-2 has collapsed them without producing the corrective reorientation.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The evidence does not extensively describe the inner state of the person who encounters worth-denial directed at them but does not receive it as a blow to their standing. Silent on this specific prompt.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The person who cannot receive CHAR-4's corrective is the one whose evaluative standard has been replaced by self-worship or earthly orientation. Phili 3:19's "their end is destruction" names this person's trajectory. The inverted conscience does not receive CHAR-4's corrective signal because the signal itself has been reinterpreted by the corrupted standard.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The corpus does not extensively describe the inner state of the person who encounters CHAR-5 directed at them but does not receive it as damaging to their standing. The Pauline evidence (2Cor 10:10 — critics dismissing Paul's presence as of no account) shows Paul bearing this without apparent inner displacement, but the inner mechanics of this resilience are not elaborated in the CHAR-5 corpus. Silent.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Psa 73:13's psalmist — who has maintained innocence but doubts its value — is the person who encounters CHAR-6's protective function but finds it apparently failing (enemies are prospering while he maintains moral integrity). The inner state is a crisis of moral confidence: the innocence is real but its protective benefit seems invisible. This is not a loss of innocence but a loss of confidence in innocence's protective value — a faith crisis about whether God vindicates moral integrity.

---

#### T1.8 — Dimension Classification

##### T1.8.1 — What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The primary dimension is **emotion/affect** — shame as experienced inner state is fundamentally a felt reality, the collapse of inner dignity and standing as an experienced event. The bosh corpus, the ke.lim.mah corpus, the aischunē corpus all centre on the phenomenology of the experience. However, the evidence also warrants classification of strong **moral dimension**: shame in the M07-B and M07-C registers is always morally weighted — it either signals accurate moral reality (deserved shame) or is produced in the absence of moral reality (unjust wound). And there is a **volitional dimension**: the capacity to refuse, accept, or deploy shame shows that the will is deeply engaged.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Primary dimension is social/relational — CHAR-2 operates at the level of a person's standing within their community, their political order, and before God. It is primarily a relational-status phenomenon. The bodily-visibility of CHAR-2 (shaved beards, stripped crowns, nakedness exposed) confirms the social-dimension primacy.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The primary dimension is relational — CHAR-3 is constituted by the relation between persons and specifically by the misassignment of worth within that relation. It is not primarily affective, cognitive, or volitional — though it engages all of these — but relational: it is what one person does to another in the space between them.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Primary dimension: moral-evaluative — CHAR-4 is specifically the conscience's evaluative operation, making it the most directly moral-dimension characteristic in M07. Secondary dimension: volitional (VCG-03 — the perverted will that loves dishonour). The moral-evaluative primary is distinctive to CHAR-4 within M07 and marks it as the characteristic most directly about the conscience's functioning.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The primary dimension is relational — CHAR-5 is constituted by the contempt-relation between persons, and its damage is in the relational field. The strong secondary dimension is affective: the shame produced by contempt is felt (it wounds the person's sense of worth). A volitional dimension is also present: the pull toward retaliation (1Pe 3:9) shows that the will is engaged when CHAR-5 is received.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The primary dimension is moral — CHAR-6 is specifically the inner moral condition of blameless conscience and clean will. It is the moral dimension characteristic most directly positive in M07: it names what the image-bearer should be (innocent, morally clean) rather than what goes wrong (shame, humiliation, dishonour). The moral dimension of CHAR-6 is primary because innocence is constituted by the moral choices and moral condition of the person.

---

##### T1.8.2 — What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

For the emotional primary: Psa 44:15 (vc=37310) — "shame has covered my face" — the experiential, covering quality. Job 10:15 (vc=37502) — "I am filled with disgrace" — the inner saturation. Jer 20:18 (vc=37316) — "spend my days in shame" — the chronic felt condition. For the moral dimension: Jer 6:15 (vc=65551) — the absence of shame following abomination identifies shame as the morally appropriate response that is missing. Eze 43:11 — shame as the precondition for knowledge of God's order — places shame within a moral-relational framework. For the volitional: Heb 12:2 (vc=34970) — Jesus "despising the shame" — an act of the will over against the felt shame-pressure. 1Pe 4:16 — "let him not be ashamed, but let him glorify God" — an imperative directed at the will.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

2Sa 10:5 (vc=38517): "cannot return to public life until their beards have grown" — shame constituted by social recognition of the bodily sign. Jer 46:12 (vc=37512): "nations have heard of your shame, and the earth is full of your cry" — humiliation is public, heard, announced. Eze 44:13 (vc=37496): shame restricts relational access to God's presence. All confirm the social-relational dimension as primary.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Joh 8:49 — "you dishonor me" — is relational: the dishonour is directed at Jesus personally in a relational exchange. Jam 2:6 — "you have dishonored the poor man" — is relational: the poor man's worth is being violated in the relational field of the community. The entrepō evidence (Luk 18:2/4) is relational: the judge's absent-regard fails the relational obligation toward God and persons.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" — names the conscience as both CHAR-4's location and its relational field of operation. Eph 5:12 — "it is shameful even to speak" — shows the conscience recognising a threshold of moral degradation that identifies certain conduct as unspeakable. These confirm the moral-evaluative dimension as primary.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The relational primary: exoutheneō (VCG-01) is entirely about the relational attitude toward others — the inner disposition of the contempt-er toward the contempt-ed expressed in how the person is treated. The shame produced (in VCG-01's case: exclusion from proper regard, devaluation of ministry) is relational in its operation.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Gen 20:5 — "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" — names the moral primary directly: the heart's moral integrity and the hands' moral cleanness are both moral conditions, not relational or social states. Psa 26:6's approach to God's altar based on moral innocence confirms the moral dimension as what enables or blocks the relational outcome (approach to God).

---

##### T1.8.3 — Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The secondary dimensions (moral and volitional) do not compete with the emotional primary but qualify it. The evidence shows that shame's emotional register is never purely physiological or psychological — it is always morally weighted (the shame is either deserved or unjust, appropriate or seared). The volitional dimension qualifies how the emotional register is received and expressed. The three dimensions work as a system: the emotional (felt collapse), the moral (appropriate or not), and the volitional (received, borne, resisted, deployed) together constitute CHAR-1's full inner anatomy.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) Affective — inner turmoil, dismay, confusion accompanying CHAR-2 (Jer 49:23 — "melt in fear, troubled like the sea"). (2) Moral — VCG-03 grounds CHAR-2 in moral cause (pride -> disgrace). These do not compete with the social-relational primary but accompany it.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) Moral-evaluative — the dishonoring of persons presupposes and corrupts a moral-evaluative faculty. (2) Volitional — the active-dishonour mode (VCG-01) is willful — it requires a volitional act of refused-acknowledgment. These secondary dimensions accompany the relational primary without competing with it.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Secondary dimensions: volitional (VCG-03 — the rulers "dearly love shame," Hos 4:18 — the will has chosen dishonour as its object) and affective (VCG-03 — glorying in shame, Phili 3:19 — the affective response to shamefulness is perverted into joy). These secondary dimensions accompany the moral-evaluative primary without competing with it.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Secondary dimensions: affective (the wound of being treated as nothing), volitional (the pull toward retaliation). These accompany the relational primary without competing.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) Relational — CHAR-6 enables the relational condition of approach to God (Psa 26:6); its absence blocks the relational approach (Hos 8:5). (2) Volitional — the maintained innocence of Psa 73:13 requires active moral choice; the incapacity of Hos 8:5 is the loss of volitional capacity for moral purity. These accompany the moral primary without competing with it.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location

---

### T2

#### T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

##### T2.1.1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

No verse in the 224-verse corpus explicitly identifies shame as a spirit-level phenomenon using the Hebrew *ruach* or Greek *pneuma* terms. The evidence does not locate CHAR-1 at the spirit level explicitly.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not explicitly locate enforced humiliation at the spirit level. The sha.phel evidence targets inner orientations (pride) but does not name ruach/pneuma as the constitutional locus. Silent on spirit-level location.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse CHAR-3 corpus does not explicitly locate worth-denial at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not explicitly locate the shamefulness-evaluative judgment at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not explicitly locate contempt-produced shame at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse CHAR-6 corpus does not explicitly locate innocence at the spirit level. Silent.

---

---

##### T2.1.2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

Not evidenced. The primary constitutional location across the corpus is soul-level (the felt inner experience, the conscience, the will responding). The absence of spirit-level language in the shame corpus is itself analytically significant — shame appears to operate at the soul and body level rather than the spirit.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not explicitly locate enforced humiliation at the spirit level. The sha.phel evidence targets inner orientations (pride) but does not name ruach/pneuma as the constitutional locus. Silent on spirit-level location.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse CHAR-3 corpus does not explicitly locate worth-denial at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not explicitly locate the shamefulness-evaluative judgment at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not explicitly locate contempt-produced shame at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse CHAR-6 corpus does not explicitly locate innocence at the spirit level. Silent.

---

---

##### T2.1.3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

Not directly applicable given the absence of spirit-level location in the evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not explicitly locate enforced humiliation at the spirit level. The sha.phel evidence targets inner orientations (pride) but does not name ruach/pneuma as the constitutional locus. Silent on spirit-level location.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse CHAR-3 corpus does not explicitly locate worth-denial at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not explicitly locate the shamefulness-evaluative judgment at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not explicitly locate contempt-produced shame at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse CHAR-6 corpus does not explicitly locate innocence at the spirit level. Silent.

---

---

##### T2.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The 224-verse CHAR-1 corpus is silent on spirit-level location. This distinguishes shame from characteristics whose evidence explicitly names the spirit (ruach) as the locus.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not explicitly locate enforced humiliation at the spirit level. The sha.phel evidence targets inner orientations (pride) but does not name ruach/pneuma as the constitutional locus. Silent on spirit-level location.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse CHAR-3 corpus does not explicitly locate worth-denial at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not explicitly locate the shamefulness-evaluative judgment at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not explicitly locate contempt-produced shame at the spirit level. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse CHAR-6 corpus does not explicitly locate innocence at the spirit level. Silent.

---

---

#### T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

##### T2.2.1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, by location and language. The soul (nefesh) is the locus of the felt inner life, and shame's experience — the felt collapse of dignity — is consistently located in the inner person without explicit anatomical precision but with the language of inner state that is characteristic of soul-level phenomena. Job 10:15 (vc=37502) — "I am *filled* with disgrace" — the language of inner saturation that aligns with soul-level experience. 1Jo 2:28 (vc=34832) uses aischunō in the context of "shrinking" (literally: "shrink back from him in shame") — the recoiling of the inner self before Christ's appearing, which is a soul-level response.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced by the felt inner collapse accompanying CHAR-2 (the dismay, confusion, and inner devastation of defeated nations; Zion's cry of utter shame, Jer 9:19, vc=65554). The inner experienced dimension of enforced humiliation operates at soul level, though secondary to the social-bodily primary.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Soul-level location is implied in the inner attitude of the dishonorer (the Luk 18:2/4 judge whose lack of regard is "a recognised inner character trait"; Luk 18:9's those who "trust in themselves that they were righteous" — a soul-level self-assessment producing contemptuous treatment of others). The inner disposition of worth-misassignment operates at soul level.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 operates at soul level through the conscience — the faculty that registers the moral quality of conduct and desires against a standard. 2Cor 4:2's "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" positions CHAR-4's evaluative operation in the conscience as a soul-level faculty. Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" shows the evaluative faculty (mind/phronēma) as the location of the inversion in VCG-03.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The soul-level dimension of CHAR-5 is evidenced in the wound to the person's sense of worth. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is a soul-level condition — his inner self-understanding has been shaped by the accumulated contempt of his social context.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is a soul-level characteristic: the moral conscience and the will are both soul-level faculties, and it is their condition (clean, blameless, free from deliberate wrongdoing) that constitutes CHAR-6. The "integrity of my heart" (Gen 20:5) names the soul-level location explicitly: the heart as the integrating moral centre is the primary location of CHAR-6.

---

---

##### T2.2.2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Soul-level location confirms that CHAR-1 is an experience of the whole inner person, not merely a cognitive judgment or physical reaction. Shame penetrates to the sense of personal identity and worth — it is not a belief about oneself but a felt state of being. The M07-A language of shame as "rottenness in the bones" (Pro 12:4, vc=65525) — an inward destructive force — and the ke.lim.mah language of shame as "carried" (Eze 34:29; 36:6; 39:26) confirm the weight and penetration of shame as a soul-level burden. The person who bears shame bears it as themselves, not merely as a label attached to them.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced by the felt inner collapse accompanying CHAR-2 (the dismay, confusion, and inner devastation of defeated nations; Zion's cry of utter shame, Jer 9:19, vc=65554). The inner experienced dimension of enforced humiliation operates at soul level, though secondary to the social-bodily primary.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Soul-level location is implied in the inner attitude of the dishonorer (the Luk 18:2/4 judge whose lack of regard is "a recognised inner character trait"; Luk 18:9's those who "trust in themselves that they were righteous" — a soul-level self-assessment producing contemptuous treatment of others). The inner disposition of worth-misassignment operates at soul level.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 operates at soul level through the conscience — the faculty that registers the moral quality of conduct and desires against a standard. 2Cor 4:2's "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" positions CHAR-4's evaluative operation in the conscience as a soul-level faculty. Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" shows the evaluative faculty (mind/phronēma) as the location of the inversion in VCG-03.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The soul-level dimension of CHAR-5 is evidenced in the wound to the person's sense of worth. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is a soul-level condition — his inner self-understanding has been shaped by the accumulated contempt of his social context.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is a soul-level characteristic: the moral conscience and the will are both soul-level faculties, and it is their condition (clean, blameless, free from deliberate wrongdoing) that constitutes CHAR-6. The "integrity of my heart" (Gen 20:5) names the soul-level location explicitly: the heart as the integrating moral centre is the primary location of CHAR-6.

---

---

##### T2.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; soul-level evidence is present.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced by the felt inner collapse accompanying CHAR-2 (the dismay, confusion, and inner devastation of defeated nations; Zion's cry of utter shame, Jer 9:19, vc=65554). ---

#### T2.3 — Heart

##### T2.3.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, with specific evidence. Psa 119:80 (vc=65520): "may my heart be blameless in your statutes, that I may not be put to shame" — the blameless heart is the protective faculty, directly linking heart-integrity to shame-avoidance. The heart's blamelessness is what guards against shame's collapse. Ezr 9:6 (vc=65495) — the conscience-driven shame that prevents lifting the face toward God is a heart-level phenomenon in the biblical sense of heart as the integrating centre of moral awareness and will. The corrective-shame passages where shame activates return (2Ch 30:15; Jer 31:19) implicitly engage the heart as the faculty that receives the shame signal and responds.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

CHAR-2's evidence does not specifically locate the characteristic in the heart. The heart is implicated as the locus of the proud disposition CHAR-2 corrects, but CHAR-2 itself as enforced humiliation is not explicitly heart-located. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The self-contradicting inner stance of Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — engages the heart as the integrating centre of moral consistency (or inconsistency). The heart that boasts in the law while the will breaks it is a divided heart, and from this inner division the dishonoring of God flows. Jam 2:6's failure of moral perception — treating the poor man as if he had no worth — is a failure of the heart's integrating moral vision.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The heart is implicated in CHAR-4's VCG-03 inversion: Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" and "their god is their belly" suggest a heart-level orientation that corrupts the evaluative faculty. The heart as the integrating moral centre is the location from which the evaluative faculty operates and from which its inversion flows.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's heart is engaged: Luk 18:9 — "trusted in themselves that they were righteous" — is a heart-disposition of self-sufficiency that generates contempt. The heart as the integrating centre of self-assessment is the location from which the contemptuous dismissal of others flows. For the recipient, the heart as the worth-sensing faculty is the target of CHAR-5's damage.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The heart is CHAR-6's primary explicit constitutional location: "integrity of my heart" (Gen 20:5, vc=22817/22821). The heart as the integrating centre of moral knowing, willing, and feeling is the location from which CHAR-6 operates. Psa 73:13's "I have kept my heart clean" names the heart as the specific locus of the moral purity that CHAR-6 describes. The heart-location confirms CHAR-6 as a heart-level moral characteristic — it is the condition of the heart's moral integrity.

---

---

##### T2.3.2 — What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Heart-location reveals that shame engages the integrating centre of the inner person — the faculty of moral knowing, feeling, and willing simultaneously. Psa 119:80's "blameless heart" as the shame-shield means that what protects against shame is not merely righteous behaviour but the inner orientation of the heart's full faculty. This places shame within the heart's moral-evaluative and volitional system: shame is what the heart experiences when its moral integrity is compromised or threatened, and a heart that is whole is the inner condition that protects against it.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

CHAR-2's evidence does not specifically locate the characteristic in the heart. The heart is implicated as the locus of the proud disposition CHAR-2 corrects, but CHAR-2 itself as enforced humiliation is not explicitly heart-located. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The self-contradicting inner stance of Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — engages the heart as the integrating centre of moral consistency (or inconsistency). The heart that boasts in the law while the will breaks it is a divided heart, and from this inner division the dishonoring of God flows. Jam 2:6's failure of moral perception — treating the poor man as if he had no worth — is a failure of the heart's integrating moral vision.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The heart is implicated in CHAR-4's VCG-03 inversion: Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" and "their god is their belly" suggest a heart-level orientation that corrupts the evaluative faculty. The heart as the integrating moral centre is the location from which the evaluative faculty operates and from which its inversion flows.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's heart is engaged: Luk 18:9 — "trusted in themselves that they were righteous" — is a heart-disposition of self-sufficiency that generates contempt. The heart as the integrating centre of self-assessment is the location from which the contemptuous dismissal of others flows. For the recipient, the heart as the worth-sensing faculty is the target of CHAR-5's damage.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The heart is CHAR-6's primary explicit constitutional location: "integrity of my heart" (Gen 20:5, vc=22817/22821). The heart as the integrating centre of moral knowing, willing, and feeling is the location from which CHAR-6 operates. Psa 73:13's "I have kept my heart clean" names the heart as the specific locus of the moral purity that CHAR-6 describes. The heart-location confirms CHAR-6 as a heart-level moral characteristic — it is the condition of the heart's moral integrity.

---

---

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

---

#### T2.4 — Mind

##### T2.4.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The cognitive dimension of CHAR-1 is present in several registers. The M07-B idolatry register shows shame produced by cognitive exposure — the inner disorientation (confusion, bewilderment) when the idol's worthlessness is revealed (Isa 45:16; Jer 51:17). This is a cognitive collapse: what was believed (the idol has power) is exposed as false, and the cognitive crash produces shame. Jer 31:19 (vc=38509) — "after I was instructed... I was ashamed" — instruction (cognitive engagement) triggering shame confirms the mind's role in the shame-producing sequence. The wisdom literature pattern (Pro 13:18; 18:13) locates shame as the consequence of failures of the mind — ignoring instruction, answering before listening.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The cognitive dimension is evidenced in the confusion/disorientation register: the defeated and humiliated "go in confusion" (Isa 45:16), are "dismayed and confounded" (2Ki 19:26; Isa 37:27). The cognitive faculty of confident orientation collapses under enforced humiliation — the person loses their bearings. This is a mind-level effect of CHAR-2.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 engages the cognitive faculty in the worth-assessment process: to dishonour another is to make a cognitive judgment about their worth (assigning them less worth than they have). The Luk 18:4 judge "acknowledges to himself" that he lacks fear and regard — the cognitive self-recognition of the absent-faculty.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The mind (nous/dianoia) is CHAR-4's primary constitutional location: the moral-evaluative judgment is a cognitive act, assessing conduct against a standard. Phili 3:19 — "minds set on earthly things" — names the mind as the site of the evaluative inversion. Rom 1:26-27's "dishonorable passions" engage the cognitive faculty in assessing whether desires are properly ordered.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment (this person is of no account) is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4 — "those who have no standing in the church" — is a cognitive assessment about standing. Rom 14:3/10 — despising a brother who eats or abstains — is a cognitive-evaluative judgment about the other person's worth or standing before God.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 does not specifically engage the mind (nous/dianoia) as its primary constitutional location — the emphasis throughout is on the heart and the hands rather than cognitive operations. Silent on mind as the specific locus of CHAR-6.

---

---

##### T2.4.2 — What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Mind-location reveals that shame is not merely emotional — it involves cognitive assessment of one's standing and the cognitive crash when false beliefs are exposed. The idolatry-shame passages evidence a specific cognitive pattern: when the mind's confident belief in a false object is suddenly exposed as groundless, the cognitive disorientation (confusion, bewilderment) is the shame-experience. This means shame can be the cognitive-emotional response to cognitive failure — the inner collapse of a worldview that cannot sustain the weight of reality.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The cognitive dimension is evidenced in the confusion/disorientation register: the defeated and humiliated "go in confusion" (Isa 45:16), are "dismayed and confounded" (2Ki 19:26; Isa 37:27). The cognitive faculty of confident orientation collapses under enforced humiliation — the person loses their bearings. This is a mind-level effect of CHAR-2.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 engages the cognitive faculty in the worth-assessment process: to dishonour another is to make a cognitive judgment about their worth (assigning them less worth than they have). The Luk 18:4 judge "acknowledges to himself" that he lacks fear and regard — the cognitive self-recognition of the absent-faculty.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The mind (nous/dianoia) is CHAR-4's primary constitutional location: the moral-evaluative judgment is a cognitive act, assessing conduct against a standard. Phili 3:19 — "minds set on earthly things" — names the mind as the site of the evaluative inversion. Rom 1:26-27's "dishonorable passions" engage the cognitive faculty in assessing whether desires are properly ordered.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment (this person is of no account) is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4 — "those who have no standing in the church" — is a cognitive assessment about standing. Rom 14:3/10 — despising a brother who eats or abstains — is a cognitive-evaluative judgment about the other person's worth or standing before God.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 does not specifically engage the mind (nous/dianoia) as its primary constitutional location — the emphasis throughout is on the heart and the hands rather than cognitive operations. Silent on mind as the specific locus of CHAR-6.

---

---

##### T2.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; mind-location is evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment (this person is of no account) is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4 — "those who have no standing in the church" — is a cognitive assessment about standing. Rom 14:3/10 — despising a brother who eats or abstains — is a cognitive-evaluative judgment about the other person's worth or standing before God.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 does not specifically engage the mind (nous/dianoia) as its primary constitutional location — the emphasis throughout is on the heart and the hands rather than cognitive operations. Silent on mind as the specific locus of CHAR-6.

---

---

#### T2.5 — Other Soul Subsets

##### T2.5.1 — Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Conscience is the most prominent additional soul-location for CHAR-1. The M07-B seared-conscience register (VCG-04) is entirely about the conscience's relation to shame: "they did not know how to blush" — the loss of the shame-registering conscience. The M07-C-VCG-03 material (entropē — 1Cor 6:5; 15:34) presents shame as directly awakening the conscience toward God. 2Ch 30:15 (vc=38506) — the priests' shame moving them to consecration — is a conscience-activated response. Conscience is the specific inner faculty that receives the moral signal that shame carries; when it is functional, shame can be received; when seared, it cannot.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the general soul and the cognitive/affective dimensions is evidenced in the 72-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the above is evidenced in the 15-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Conscience (suneidēsis, implied in 2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience") is the specific soul-subset location of CHAR-4. The conscience is the moral-recognitive faculty that specifically identifies the shameful as shameful. CHAR-4 is conscience's primary output in its evaluative mode.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the above is clearly evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscience is the additional soul-subset location of CHAR-6: the clean conscience is what CHAR-6's innocence produces and what blameless hands reflect. The conscience is the faculty that registers the presence or absence of guilt — and CHAR-6 is the condition in which the conscience registers no guilt because no deliberate wrongdoing has occurred. The conscience and CHAR-6 are functionally linked: functioning conscience + no deliberate wrongdoing = CHAR-6's inner condition.

---

---

##### T2.5.2 — If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Conscience as the additional soul-subset location reveals that CHAR-1 has a specific moral-registration function beyond the general heart/mind framework. Shame is the primary experiential output of the conscience when it registers moral failure or exposure. The functional conscience = shame-capable; the non-functional (seared) conscience = shame-incapable. This means CHAR-1 and the conscience are structurally linked: shame is what the conscience feels when it registers failure, and the loss of shame is the sign that the conscience has ceased to function. The conscience is both the faculty that receives the shame signal and the faculty through which shame can be deployed correctively (1Cor 6:5).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the general soul and the cognitive/affective dimensions is evidenced in the 72-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the above is evidenced in the 15-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Conscience (suneidēsis, implied in 2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience") is the specific soul-subset location of CHAR-4. The conscience is the moral-recognitive faculty that specifically identifies the shameful as shameful. CHAR-4 is conscience's primary output in its evaluative mode.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the above is clearly evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscience is the additional soul-subset location of CHAR-6: the clean conscience is what CHAR-6's innocence produces and what blameless hands reflect. The conscience is the faculty that registers the presence or absence of guilt — and CHAR-6 is the condition in which the conscience registers no guilt because no deliberate wrongdoing has occurred. The conscience and CHAR-6 are functionally linked: functioning conscience + no deliberate wrongdoing = CHAR-6's inner condition.

---

---

##### T2.5.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; conscience as an additional soul-subset is evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

No additional soul-subset location beyond the general soul and the cognitive/affective dimensions is evidenced in the 72-verse corpus. Silent.
