---

---

#### T2.6 — Body — Significance

##### T2.6.1 — Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, with multiple body-part links evidenced. (1) **The face** — the most prominent body-part link: "shame has covered my face" (Psa 44:15); "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face" (Ezr 9:6); "dishonor has covered my face" (Psa 69:7); "shame is on all faces" (Eze 7:18); "groans and turns her face away" (Lam 1:8). (2) **The head** — covering the head as the bodily expression of shame (Jer 14:3; 14:4); "I cannot lift up my head" (Job 10:15). (3) **The eyes** — "their faces shall never be ashamed" / "those who look to him are radiant" (Psa 34:5) — the eyes' orientation toward God as the protective posture. (4) **Blushing** — "blush to lift my face" (Ezr 9:6); "they did not know how to blush" (Jer 6:15; 8:12) — the physiological blush as shame's most immediate bodily expression.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Multiple prominent body-part links: (1) The beard (2Sa 10:5; 1Ch 19:5) — shaving as the enacted sign of humiliation. (2) The face (2Ch 32:21 — "shame of face"; Mic 3:7 — "cover their lips"). (3) The crown and turban (Eze 21:26 — "remove the turban and take off the crown"). (4) The back (Jer 48:39 — "turned his back in shame"). (5) The eyes (Isa 2:11; 5:15; Psa 18:27 — haughty eyes brought down). The links are indicative, expressive, and juridical.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The head-covering symbolic-disrespect register (1Cor 11:4-5, vc=35009/35010) is CHAR-3's most prominent body-part link: the covered or uncovered head is the bodily sign through which the symbolic disrespect of divinely ordered authority is communicated. The body-part link here is symbolic and communicative — the head functions as the sign of relational honour/dishonour.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The body-part link is present in VCG-01 and VCG-02. 1Cor 11:6 (vc=34983) — the wife's cut or shaved hair is disgraceful — links shamefulness to hair as the bodily sign of social-moral propriety. Rom 1:27 (vc=34966) — "shameless acts with men" — links shamefulness to specific bodily conduct. Rev 16:15 (vc=34967) — naked exposure — links shamefulness to the body's unguarded state. The body-part links in CHAR-4 are indicative (the body reveals the inner moral-disorder) and symbolic (hair as the sign of propriety).

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

VCG-02's violent-contempt register (Mar 12:4 — "struck him on the head and treated him shamefully"; Luk 20:11 — "beat and treated him shamefully") links CHAR-5 to the body through physical violence as the enactment of contemptuous dismissal. The body is the site where contemptuous rejection is enacted against the person — the body receives the contempt physically. Bartimaeus's cloak (Mar 10:50) is a bodily-item carrying the identity of contempt-shaped shame; throwing it off is a bodily act of shame-identity abandonment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The hands are CHAR-6's most prominent body-part link: "the innocence of my hands" (Gen 20:5); "I wash my hands in innocence" (Psa 26:6). The hands function as the external expression of the internal moral condition: hand-cleanness is the outward evidence of the inner moral integrity. The hand-washing gesture (Psa 26:6) is both the ritual enactment of CHAR-6's claim and the symbolic communication of the inner state to God and community. The body-part link is indicative (the hands show the moral condition), ritual (hand-washing enacts the moral claim), and communicative (the gesture declares innocence).

---

---

##### T2.6.2 — If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The face-link is both *indicative* (showing shame's outward visibility — it is seen in the face) and *expressive* (the covering of the face is the body acting out the inner shame). The head-link is primarily *postural* — the head-down posture is the body enacting the inner collapse of dignity. The blush-link is *physiological* — it names the involuntary body-response that indicates the inner state. The face/head/blush links together reveal that shame's inner state is not hidden — it expresses itself through the body even when the person tries to conceal it (covering the face is itself a shame-expression). Scripture is showing that shame is a whole-person event: the inner collapse has a necessary bodily expression that cannot be fully suppressed.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Multiple prominent body-part links: (1) The beard (2Sa 10:5; 1Ch 19:5) — shaving as the enacted sign of humiliation. (2) The face (2Ch 32:21 — "shame of face"; Mic 3:7 — "cover their lips"). (3) The crown and turban (Eze 21:26 — "remove the turban and take off the crown"). (4) The back (Jer 48:39 — "turned his back in shame"). (5) The eyes (Isa 2:11; 5:15; Psa 18:27 — haughty eyes brought down). The links are indicative, expressive, and juridical.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The head-covering symbolic-disrespect register (1Cor 11:4-5, vc=35009/35010) is CHAR-3's most prominent body-part link: the covered or uncovered head is the bodily sign through which the symbolic disrespect of divinely ordered authority is communicated. The body-part link here is symbolic and communicative — the head functions as the sign of relational honour/dishonour.

---

---

---

---

##### T2.6.3 — If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; multiple body-part links are evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Multiple prominent body-part links: (1) The beard (2Sa 10:5; 1Ch 19:5) — shaving as the enacted sign of humiliation. (2) The face (2Ch 32:21 — "shame of face"; Mic 3:7 — "cover their lips"). ---

---

#### T2.7 — Body — Direction

##### T2.7.1 — Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to the soul, or does it run in both directions?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Primarily **inner → body**: the felt inner shame produces the bodily expression (face-covering, blushing, head-lowering, withdrawal). But there is also a **body → inner** feedback: the bodily expression of shame can reinforce and deepen the inner state, and the bodily posture of trust (looking to God, Psa 34:5) produces the inner radiance that shame would have destroyed. The blushing-refusal of Jer 6:15 ("they did not know how to blush") shows that the bodily signal has been disconnected from the inner state — the body no longer reflects the inner reality that should be present. In the M07-C mode (face not lifted, Ezr 9:6), the bodily posture carries the inner moral reality outward into a relational context (before God) — this is bidirectional: inner shame → bodily posture → relational stance before God.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Bidirectional. External to body to inner: military defeat strips armour and forces retreat; social community strips the beard; divine act removes crown — the outer act produces inner collapse. Inner to body: haughty eyes (inner pride-disposition) are specifically targeted and brought low.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Inner to body: the inner disposition of disrespect toward divinely ordered authority is expressed through the bodily act (the covered or uncovered head). The body is the medium through which the inner worth-denial is communicated to the relational community.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

In VCG-02, the direction is inner to body: disordered inner desire (dishonorable passions, Rom 1:26) produces the shameful bodily acts (Rom 1:27). The body enacts the inner disorder. In VCG-01's hair register (1Cor 11:6), the body-sign is both indicative of inner moral propriety and constitutive of the social-moral statement.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

In VCG-02, the direction is outer to inner: the physical blow and shameful treatment produce the inner experience of CHAR-5 in the person being treated. In Mar 10:50, the direction is inner to body: the decision to abandon the shame-identity is expressed through the bodily act of throwing off the cloak.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The direction is inner to body to relational: heart-integrity (inner) -> hand-cleanness (body) -> approach to God's altar (relational). The hands express and enact the inner moral condition; the relational access to God is the outcome of the inner-to-body expression. This is a consistently inner-to-outer direction: CHAR-6 originates in the heart and expresses through the hands toward the relational encounter with God.

---

---

##### T2.7.2 — What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The primarily inner → body direction confirms that CHAR-1 is first an inner phenomenon whose bodily expression is the consequence, not the cause. This distinguishes shame from purely social performances of shame (which would be body → inner). However, the bidirectionality in the M07-C mode (bodily posture mediating the relational stance before God) reveals that shame is not merely private — it finds its completion in a relational posture. The person who bears shame before God completes the experience in the downward posture of the face not lifted; the person who trusts God completes their trust in the radiant face that looks toward him. Body and inner state constitute the whole shame-experience.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Bidirectional. External to body to inner: military defeat strips armour and forces retreat; social community strips the beard; divine act removes crown — the outer act produces inner collapse. Inner to body: haughty eyes (inner pride-disposition) are specifically targeted and brought low.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Inner to body: the inner disposition of disrespect toward divinely ordered authority is expressed through the bodily act (the covered or uncovered head). The body is the medium through which the inner worth-denial is communicated to the relational community.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

In VCG-02, the direction is inner to body: disordered inner desire (dishonorable passions, Rom 1:26) produces the shameful bodily acts (Rom 1:27). The body enacts the inner disorder. In VCG-01's hair register (1Cor 11:6), the body-sign is both indicative of inner moral propriety and constitutive of the social-moral statement.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

In VCG-02, the direction is outer to inner: the physical blow and shameful treatment produce the inner experience of CHAR-5 in the person being treated. In Mar 10:50, the direction is inner to body: the decision to abandon the shame-identity is expressed through the bodily act of throwing off the cloak.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The direction is inner to body to relational: heart-integrity (inner) -> hand-cleanness (body) -> approach to God's altar (relational). The hands express and enact the inner moral condition; the relational access to God is the outcome of the inner-to-body expression. This is a consistently inner-to-outer direction: CHAR-6 originates in the heart and expresses through the hands toward the relational encounter with God.

---

---

##### T2.7.3 — If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Bidirectional. External to body to inner: military defeat strips armour and forces retreat; social community strips the beard; divine act removes crown — the outer act produces inner collapse. Inner to body: haughty eyes (inner pride-disposition) are specifically targeted and brought low.

---

---

#### T2.8 — Body — Deposit

##### T2.8.1 — Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The evidence suggests a functional deposit but not a biological/genetic one. Pro 12:4 (vc=65525) — shame as "rottenness in the bones" — uses the bones as the metaphorical locus of deep inner damage, suggesting that sustained shame-experience leaves a structural deposit in the person's core. Eze 32:24-30 (the Elam warriors carrying their shame into the pit) suggests a deposit that persists beyond death — the shame is constitutionally part of the person's identity-record. However, the evidence does not explicitly name genetic or DNA-level deposit. The deposit appears to be at the level of the person's inner record and identity rather than biological inheritance.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32:24-30; 44:13) shows CHAR-2 leaving a permanent deposit: shame carried into death (identity-record), priestly access permanently restricted (structural consequence). Jer 23:40 — "everlasting reproach and perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — names the deposit as permanent identity-marking. The deposit is social-relational.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In VCG-02, the potter's assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) and the household of God with vessels for both honourable and dishonorable use (2Ti 2:20) suggest that dishonour can be a structural/constitutional condition. The Pass A meaning of 2Ti 2:20 notes "the inner person's moral condition determines their standing" — suggesting the deposit is produced by moral condition rather than arbitrary assignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03's sustained inverted conscience establishes a deposit: Hos 4:18's "deep affection for dishonour" — the rulers have moved from occasional wrong evaluation to constitutionally-structured love of what disgraces them. Phili 3:19's "their end is destruction" implies the deposit of the inverted conscience is eschatologically irreversible in its current trajectory. The functional conscience (VCG-01) produces the deposit of habituated moral discernment.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Mar 10:50's Bartimaeus evidences the deposit: a life lived under sustained social contempt produces a settled beggar-identity — the contempt-shame has deposited itself as a structural element of the person's inner self-understanding. The willingness to throw off the cloak in response to Jesus's call suggests the deposit can be overcome by a re-worth-assignment from a higher authority (Jesus's call overriding the social contempt-verdict).

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Hos 8:5's incapacity for innocence evidences the deposit of its loss: sustained idolatry has so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity is no longer accessible. This is a negative-deposit: the accumulation of idolatrous compromise has deposited into the inner person as an incapacity rather than a capacity. The deposit's consequence is the permanent blocking of the relational access to God that CHAR-6 would enable.

---

---

##### T2.8.2 — What evidence supports or contradicts this?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Supporting: Pro 12:4 ("rottenness in the bones"), Eze 32:24-30 (shame carried into death), Ezr 9:7 ("from the days of our fathers to this day we have been in great guilt" — generational shame-condition). Moderating: the M07-A-VCG-04 promises (Isa 54:4 — "you will forget the shame of your youth") show that shame's deposit is not irreversible; divine action can dissolve it. The evidence does not clearly contradict a functional-deposit reading but does show the deposit is transformable.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32:24-30; 44:13) shows CHAR-2 leaving a permanent deposit: shame carried into death (identity-record), priestly access permanently restricted (structural consequence). Jer 23:40 — "everlasting reproach and perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — names the deposit as permanent identity-marking. The deposit is social-relational.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In VCG-02, the potter's assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) and the household of God with vessels for both honourable and dishonorable use (2Ti 2:20) suggest that dishonour can be a structural/constitutional condition. The Pass A meaning of 2Ti 2:20 notes "the inner person's moral condition determines their standing" — suggesting the deposit is produced by moral condition rather than arbitrary assignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03's sustained inverted conscience establishes a deposit: Hos 4:18's "deep affection for dishonour" — the rulers have moved from occasional wrong evaluation to constitutionally-structured love of what disgraces them. Phili 3:19's "their end is destruction" implies the deposit of the inverted conscience is eschatologically irreversible in its current trajectory. The functional conscience (VCG-01) produces the deposit of habituated moral discernment.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Mar 10:50's Bartimaeus evidences the deposit: a life lived under sustained social contempt produces a settled beggar-identity — the contempt-shame has deposited itself as a structural element of the person's inner self-understanding. The willingness to throw off the cloak in response to Jesus's call suggests the deposit can be overcome by a re-worth-assignment from a higher authority (Jesus's call overriding the social contempt-verdict).

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Hos 8:5's incapacity for innocence evidences the deposit of its loss: sustained idolatry has so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity is no longer accessible. This is a negative-deposit: the accumulation of idolatrous compromise has deposited into the inner person as an incapacity rather than a capacity. The deposit's consequence is the permanent blocking of the relational access to God that CHAR-6 would enable.

---

---

##### T2.8.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not silent; the "rottenness in the bones" and shame-carried-to-death material provides the evidence for a functional deposit finding.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes. VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32:24-30; 44:13) shows CHAR-2 leaving a permanent deposit: shame carried into death (identity-record), priestly access permanently restricted (structural consequence). Jer 23:40 — "everlasting reproach and perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — names the deposit as permanent identity-marking. The deposit is social-relational.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In VCG-02, the potter's assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) and the household of God with vessels for both honourable and dishonorable use (2Ti 2:20) suggest that dishonour can be a structural/constitutional condition. The Pass A meaning of 2Ti 2:20 notes "the inner person's moral condition determines their standing" — suggesting the deposit is produced by moral condition rather than arbitrary assignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03's sustained inverted conscience establishes a deposit: Hos 4:18's "deep affection for dishonour" — the rulers have moved from occasional wrong evaluation to constitutionally-structured love of what disgraces them. Phili 3:19's "their end is destruction" implies the deposit of the inverted conscience is eschatologically irreversible in its current trajectory. The functional conscience (VCG-01) produces the deposit of habituated moral discernment.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Mar 10:50's Bartimaeus evidences the deposit: a life lived under sustained social contempt produces a settled beggar-identity — the contempt-shame has deposited itself as a structural element of the person's inner self-understanding. The willingness to throw off the cloak in response to Jesus's call suggests the deposit can be overcome by a re-worth-assignment from a higher authority (Jesus's call overriding the social contempt-verdict).

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Hos 8:5's incapacity for innocence evidences the deposit of its loss: sustained idolatry has so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity is no longer accessible. This is a negative-deposit: the accumulation of idolatrous compromise has deposited into the inner person as an incapacity rather than a capacity. The deposit's consequence is the permanent blocking of the relational access to God that CHAR-6 would enable.

---

---

#### T2.9 — Origin and Source

##### T2.9.1 — Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Multiple origins are evidenced, corresponding to the three sub-group registers. (1) **Received from outside** (M07-A): shame arrives from enemy aggression, circumstantial collapse, misplaced trust — it originates in what is done to the person. (2) **Generated from within** (M07-B guilt-shame and M07-C guilt-shame): shame arises from one's own moral failure registered by the conscience — it originates in the inner moral-evaluative faculty. (3) **Bestowed by God** (M07-B judgment): God "puts enemies to shame" — a divine judicial act initiating shame in the opponent. (4) **Accumulated generationally** (M07-C: Ezr 9:7; Dan 9:7-8): the shame of corporate sin is inherited — it originates in a collective generational history.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Multiple origins matching the four VCGs: (1) Social community acting (VCG-01 — Ammonites shaving David's envoys). (2) Military conquest (VCG-02 — Assyria, Babylon). (3) Divine judicial action (VCG-03 — God bringing down the proud). (4) Past moral failure accumulating as carried burden (VCG-04). The origin in all cases is external to the recipient. Multiple rather than singular.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 originates in two ways: (1) From the inner disposition of the dishonorer (VCG-01): absent-regard, willful refusal to acknowledge worth, self-righteous contempt — generated from within the dishonorer's own inner-being condition. (2) From sovereign assignment (VCG-02): the potter's right, created order, received social treatment — external sources that assign dishonour-standings without the agency of either party being the primary origin.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 originates from within the conscience's evaluative operation: it is the conscience assessing conduct and desires against God's standard. In the functioning mode (VCG-01), the origin is the conscience's proper operation with God's standard as the reference. In the disordered-desire mode (VCG-02), the origin is within the appetitive faculty. In the inverted mode (VCG-03), the origin of the inversion is the choice of an earthly standard as the evaluative reference replacing God's standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 originates from outside the recipient: the contempt of others is the source (VCG-01 — the inner dismissive attitude of others; VCG-02 — the violent rejection by others; VCG-03 — the verbal assault by others). The origin is consistently external. Multiple rather than singular origins (dismissal, violence, speech) all producing the same received condition of contempt-shame.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 originates from within the person through the exercise of the moral will: the person who chooses not to engage in deliberate wrongdoing maintains the inner moral condition that CHAR-6 names. In Gen 20:5, Abimelech's innocence originated from his genuine not-knowing (he took Sarah believing she was Abraham's sister, not his wife) — it is innocence grounded in both ignorance and moral intention. In Psa 26:6, innocence is maintained through active moral choice. In Hos 8:5, the incapacity for innocence results from the accumulated moral choices of sustained idolatry — the origin of the loss is internal to the moral choices the people have been making.

---

---

##### T2.9.2 — What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Definitively multiple. CHAR-1 cannot be reduced to a single originating source. The volume-split into three sub-groups (unjust wound, moral consequence, divine encounter) was designed precisely because the evidence shows three distinct originating dynamics — all producing the same fundamental inner experience of shame. This multiplicity of origin is one of CHAR-1's analytically significant features: the same felt inner state can be produced by unjust external wounding, by one's own moral failure, by divine judgment, or by the encounter with the holy.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Multiple origins matching the four VCGs: (1) Social community acting (VCG-01 — Ammonites shaving David's envoys). (2) Military conquest (VCG-02 — Assyria, Babylon). (3) Divine judicial action (VCG-03 — God bringing down the proud). (4) Past moral failure accumulating as carried burden (VCG-04). The origin in all cases is external to the recipient. Multiple rather than singular.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 originates in two ways: (1) From the inner disposition of the dishonorer (VCG-01): absent-regard, willful refusal to acknowledge worth, self-righteous contempt — generated from within the dishonorer's own inner-being condition. (2) From sovereign assignment (VCG-02): the potter's right, created order, received social treatment — external sources that assign dishonour-standings without the agency of either party being the primary origin.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 originates from within the conscience's evaluative operation: it is the conscience assessing conduct and desires against God's standard. In the functioning mode (VCG-01), the origin is the conscience's proper operation with God's standard as the reference. In the disordered-desire mode (VCG-02), the origin is within the appetitive faculty. In the inverted mode (VCG-03), the origin of the inversion is the choice of an earthly standard as the evaluative reference replacing God's standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 originates from outside the recipient: the contempt of others is the source (VCG-01 — the inner dismissive attitude of others; VCG-02 — the violent rejection by others; VCG-03 — the verbal assault by others). The origin is consistently external. Multiple rather than singular origins (dismissal, violence, speech) all producing the same received condition of contempt-shame.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 originates from within the person through the exercise of the moral will: the person who chooses not to engage in deliberate wrongdoing maintains the inner moral condition that CHAR-6 names. In Gen 20:5, Abimelech's innocence originated from his genuine not-knowing (he took Sarah believing she was Abraham's sister, not his wife) — it is innocence grounded in both ignorance and moral intention. In Psa 26:6, innocence is maintained through active moral choice. In Hos 8:5, the incapacity for innocence results from the accumulated moral choices of sustained idolatry — the origin of the loss is internal to the moral choices the people have been making.

---

---

##### T2.9.3 — Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. In the psalmist's lament context (M07-A-VCG-01), origin is external (enemy) and unjust. In the wisdom-literature context (M07-B-VCG-03), origin is internal (moral failure) and deserved. In the prophetic-penitential context (M07-C-VCG-01), origin is internal (sin's weight) before divine holiness. In the eschatological context (M07-B-VCG-02), origin is theological (God as judge). The contextual variation confirms that CHAR-1's originating source is not fixed by the characteristic itself but by the relational and moral situation of the person.

---

Multiple origins matching the four VCGs: (1) Social community acting (VCG-01 — Ammonites shaving David's envoys). (2) Military conquest (VCG-02 — Assyria, Babylon). (3) Divine judicial action (VCG-03 — God bringing down the proud). (4) Past moral failure accumulating as carried burden (VCG-04). The origin in all cases is external to the recipient. ## T3 — Inner Faculties

---

#### T2.10 — Constitutional Movement

##### T2.10.1 — Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows shame moving from inner to outer consistently. The direction is inner → body → social: the felt inner collapse (soul level) produces the bodily expression (head-covering, face-hiding, downward posture) which then has social consequences (withdrawal from public life, inability to speak). Jer 14:3 (vc=38535/65555) — inner shame expressed in the bodily gesture of covering the head. Eze 7:18 (vc=34978) — "shame is on all faces" — the inner-outer interface. Ezr 9:6 (vc=38500/65495) — "blush to lift my face" — the inner guilt-shame expressed through the bodily posture of not lifting the face. There is also an outer → inner direction in the M07-A mode: the outer wound of enemy aggression or circumstantial collapse arrives and produces the inner shame-state.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Primarily outer to inner: enforced humiliation arrives externally (military defeat, divine act, social community) then moves inward — the shaved envoys experience the inner collapse preventing re-entry to public life (2Sa 10:5). A secondary inner to outer movement occurs when the proud inner disposition produces the outer shame of CHAR-2 as its consequence (Pro 11:2). Primary sequence: external enforcing event -> inner collapse of standing -> bodily retreat/withdrawal/exclusion.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In VCG-01, CHAR-3 moves from the inner disposition of the dishonorer (absent regard, refused acknowledgment) outward through their conduct and speech toward the relational standing of the dishonoured. The Luk 18:2/4 judge: inner disposition (no fear of God, no respect for persons) -> outer conduct (unjust judicial decisions) -> relational effect (the widow's worth is denied in her legal case). In VCG-02, CHAR-3 arrives from outside (sovereign assignment, created order, social treatment) -> inner standing of the recipient.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 primarily operates inward-to-outward: the conscience evaluates -> the evaluation produces conduct-renunciation or conduct-embrace -> the conduct is visible externally. 2Cor 4:2: conscience assessment of shameful conduct -> renunciation -> open statement of truth (the outward expression of the inward evaluation). The inverted conscience (VCG-03) reverses this: corrupted inner evaluation -> glorying in what is shameful -> outward expression of the inversion.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 moves from the contempt-er's inner disposition (self-righteous, dismissive, devaluing) outward through their conduct or speech toward the recipient, where it produces the inner shame-condition. The direction is primarily outer-to-inner for the recipient: the contempt arrives from outside and produces inner shame. For the contempt-er, the movement is inner-to-outer: the inner dismissive attitude expresses outward in the conduct of exclusion and devaluation.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 moves from the inner will (the faculty of moral choice) through the hands (the outward action-faculty) toward the relational outcome of approach to God. Gen 20:5's "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" describes both the inner location (heart) and the outer expression (hands). The movement is inner-to-outer: the heart's moral integrity expresses through the hands' clean action; together these enable the relational approach (Psa 26:6 — going around the altar). The constitutional movement is: inner will -> outward action -> relational access.

---

---

##### T2.10.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The primary pattern is: *trigger event → inner collapse → bodily expression → social withdrawal/silence*. In the M07-C guilt-shame mode: *sin → awareness of standing before God → inner shame → physical posture (face not lifted, blushing) → corrective action or corrective silence*. In the M07-A unjust-wound mode: *enemy aggression or circumstance → inner wound felt → face covering or withdrawal → prayer for divine vindication*. The corrective sub-mode reverses the last step: *shame → corrective action (2Ch 30:15 — "they consecrated themselves") or gateway opening (Eze 43:11)*.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Primarily outer to inner: enforced humiliation arrives externally (military defeat, divine act, social community) then moves inward — the shaved envoys experience the inner collapse preventing re-entry to public life (2Sa 10:5). A secondary inner to outer movement occurs when the proud inner disposition produces the outer shame of CHAR-2 as its consequence (Pro 11:2). Primary sequence: external enforcing event -> inner collapse of standing -> bodily retreat/withdrawal/exclusion.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

In VCG-01, CHAR-3 moves from the inner disposition of the dishonorer (absent regard, refused acknowledgment) outward through their conduct and speech toward the relational standing of the dishonoured. The Luk 18:2/4 judge: inner disposition (no fear of God, no respect for persons) -> outer conduct (unjust judicial decisions) -> relational effect (the widow's worth is denied in her legal case). In VCG-02, CHAR-3 arrives from outside (sovereign assignment, created order, social treatment) -> inner standing of the recipient.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 primarily operates inward-to-outward: the conscience evaluates -> the evaluation produces conduct-renunciation or conduct-embrace -> the conduct is visible externally. 2Cor 4:2: conscience assessment of shameful conduct -> renunciation -> open statement of truth (the outward expression of the inward evaluation). The inverted conscience (VCG-03) reverses this: corrupted inner evaluation -> glorying in what is shameful -> outward expression of the inversion.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 moves from the contempt-er's inner disposition (self-righteous, dismissive, devaluing) outward through their conduct or speech toward the recipient, where it produces the inner shame-condition. The direction is primarily outer-to-inner for the recipient: the contempt arrives from outside and produces inner shame. For the contempt-er, the movement is inner-to-outer: the inner dismissive attitude expresses outward in the conduct of exclusion and devaluation.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 moves from the inner will (the faculty of moral choice) through the hands (the outward action-faculty) toward the relational outcome of approach to God. Gen 20:5's "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" describes both the inner location (heart) and the outer expression (hands). The movement is inner-to-outer: the heart's moral integrity expresses through the hands' clean action; together these enable the relational approach (Psa 26:6 — going around the altar). The constitutional movement is: inner will -> outward action -> relational access.

---

---

##### T2.10.3 — If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; constitutional movement is evidenced above.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Primarily outer to inner: enforced humiliation arrives externally (military defeat, divine act, social community) then moves inward — the shaved envoys experience the inner collapse preventing re-entry to public life (2Sa 10:5). A secondary inner to outer movement occurs when the proud inner disposition produces the outer shame of CHAR-2 as its consequence (Pro 11:2). ---

In VCG-02, CHAR-3 arrives from outside (sovereign assignment, created order, social treatment) -> inner standing of the recipient.

---

The inverted conscience (VCG-03) reverses this: corrupted inner evaluation -> glorying in what is shameful -> outward expression of the inversion.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 moves from the contempt-er's inner disposition (self-righteous, dismissive, devaluing) outward through their conduct or speech toward the recipient, where it produces the inner shame-condition. The direction is primarily outer-to-inner for the recipient: the contempt arrives from outside and produces inner shame. For the contempt-er, the movement is inner-to-outer: the inner dismissive attitude expresses outward in the conduct of exclusion and devaluation.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 moves from the inner will (the faculty of moral choice) through the hands (the outward action-faculty) toward the relational outcome of approach to God. Gen 20:5's "integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands" describes both the inner location (heart) and the outer expression (hands). The movement is inner-to-outer: the heart's moral integrity expresses through the hands' clean action; together these enable the relational approach (Psa 26:6 — going around the altar). The constitutional movement is: inner will -> outward action -> relational access.

---

---

### T3

#### T3.1 — Perception

##### T3.1.1 — Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. Sight and hearing are prominent in the shame-triggering sequences. Ezr 8:22 (vc=65494) — Ezra's anticipatory shame arises from having publicly declared God's sufficiency (his own words, heard by the king); asking for soldiers would expose the inconsistency. The shame is perceptively triggered by the anticipated gap between what has been seen and what would be seen. Psa 34:5 (vc=37340) — "those who look to him are radiant" — the direction of the perceptive faculty (toward God) determines whether shame falls. The seared-conscience passages show shame's absence being linked to failed perception: "they do not see" God's lifted hand (Isa 26:11, vc=65534). The shame of idol-worship (M07-B-VCG-02) is triggered by seeing the idols' worthlessness exposed — a perceptive event (the idol fails to act) produces the inner shame collapse.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs perception by collapsing the upward gaze: the humiliated are "dismayed and confounded." The haughty eyes targeted in Isa 5:15 and Psa 18:27 show the perceptive faculty as the site of prideful distortion. In the VCG-03 divine-abasement mode, CHAR-2 can be read as perception-correcting: the proud are forced to see what they actually are.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed perception — the judge who does not see the worth of persons (Luk 18:2/4); dishonoring God through hypocrisy while not perceiving the self-contradiction (Rom 2:23). CHAR-3 impairs the relational-perceptive faculty in the dishonorer.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 engages moral perception — the conscience that recognises "certain deeds done in secret are so morally degraded that even speaking of them is shameful" (Eph 5:12) is exercising moral-perceptive discernment. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) shows distorted moral perception: what should be seen as shameful is seen as honourable.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Perception is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's misperception of worth (they do not see the genuine worth of the person they despise) and through the recipient's perception of their own contempt-received condition. Psa 14:6 — "shame the plans of the poor" — shows how contempt targets the poor person's inner plans and confidence (their hopeful perception of their own possibilities). CHAR-5 impairs the recipient's hopeful perception by forcing them to see themselves through the contempt-er's false worth-assessment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 enables moral perception: the person with a clean conscience and blameless hands can perceive their own moral condition accurately (they know they are innocent) and can perceive God's response accurately (God confirms the innocent's claim, Gen 20:6). The loss of CHAR-6 impairs moral perception: Psa 73:13's crisis is a perceptive failure — the psalmist cannot perceive why innocent suffering exists; Hos 8:5's incapacity-for-innocence is a state in which the people cannot perceive their own moral condition accurately because it has been so long distorted by idolatry.

---

---

##### T3.1.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its acute form, shame **impairs** perception by collapsing the upward gaze: the face that cannot be lifted, the eyes that turn away. The shamed person cannot look clearly at what is before them — shame produces a kind of perceptive closing-down. However, in the M07-C corrective mode, shame **sharpens** perception: being shown the temple's design produces shame, and shame then becomes the condition for receiving clearer spiritual perception (Eze 43:10-11). Corrective shame is thus a perception-clearing event: shame removes the blindness of false confidence and opens the person to see what is actually required.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs perception by collapsing the upward gaze: the humiliated are "dismayed and confounded." The haughty eyes targeted in Isa 5:15 and Psa 18:27 show the perceptive faculty as the site of prideful distortion. In the VCG-03 divine-abasement mode, CHAR-2 can be read as perception-correcting: the proud are forced to see what they actually are.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed perception — the judge who does not see the worth of persons (Luk 18:2/4); dishonoring God through hypocrisy while not perceiving the self-contradiction (Rom 2:23). CHAR-3 impairs the relational-perceptive faculty in the dishonorer.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 engages moral perception — the conscience that recognises "certain deeds done in secret are so morally degraded that even speaking of them is shameful" (Eph 5:12) is exercising moral-perceptive discernment. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) shows distorted moral perception: what should be seen as shameful is seen as honourable.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Perception is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's misperception of worth (they do not see the genuine worth of the person they despise) and through the recipient's perception of their own contempt-received condition. Psa 14:6 — "shame the plans of the poor" — shows how contempt targets the poor person's inner plans and confidence (their hopeful perception of their own possibilities). CHAR-5 impairs the recipient's hopeful perception by forcing them to see themselves through the contempt-er's false worth-assessment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 enables moral perception: the person with a clean conscience and blameless hands can perceive their own moral condition accurately (they know they are innocent) and can perceive God's response accurately (God confirms the innocent's claim, Gen 20:6). The loss of CHAR-6 impairs moral perception: Psa 73:13's crisis is a perceptive failure — the psalmist cannot perceive why innocent suffering exists; Hos 8:5's incapacity-for-innocence is a state in which the people cannot perceive their own moral condition accurately because it has been so long distorted by idolatry.

---

---

##### T3.1.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That shame operates bidirectionally on perception: in its destructive form (unjust wound, moral paralysis) it closes perception down; in its constructive form (corrective shame before God's holiness) it opens perception to what was previously obscured. This bidirectional relation confirms that the quality of shame's perceptive effect depends on whether the person's will is engaged constructively (receiving the corrective signal) or not (paralysed by the wound or hardened against correction).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs perception by collapsing the upward gaze: the humiliated are "dismayed and confounded." The haughty eyes targeted in Isa 5:15 and Psa 18:27 show the perceptive faculty as the site of prideful distortion. In the VCG-03 divine-abasement mode, CHAR-2 can be read as perception-correcting: the proud are forced to see what they actually are.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed perception — the judge who does not see the worth of persons (Luk 18:2/4); dishonoring God through hypocrisy while not perceiving the self-contradiction (Rom 2:23). CHAR-3 impairs the relational-perceptive faculty in the dishonorer.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 engages moral perception — the conscience that recognises "certain deeds done in secret are so morally degraded that even speaking of them is shameful" (Eph 5:12) is exercising moral-perceptive discernment. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) shows distorted moral perception: what should be seen as shameful is seen as honourable.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Perception is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's misperception of worth (they do not see the genuine worth of the person they despise) and through the recipient's perception of their own contempt-received condition. Psa 14:6 — "shame the plans of the poor" — shows how contempt targets the poor person's inner plans and confidence (their hopeful perception of their own possibilities). CHAR-5 impairs the recipient's hopeful perception by forcing them to see themselves through the contempt-er's false worth-assessment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 enables moral perception: the person with a clean conscience and blameless hands can perceive their own moral condition accurately (they know they are innocent) and can perceive God's response accurately (God confirms the innocent's claim, Gen 20:6). The loss of CHAR-6 impairs moral perception: Psa 73:13's crisis is a perceptive failure — the psalmist cannot perceive why innocent suffering exists; Hos 8:5's incapacity-for-innocence is a state in which the people cannot perceive their own moral condition accurately because it has been so long distorted by idolatry.

---

---

#### T3.2 — Cognition

##### T3.2.1 — Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The idolatry-shame passages (M07-B-VCG-02) show shame as the product of cognitive collapse — when the mind's confident belief in the idol is exposed as false, the cognitive disorientation (confusion, bewilderment — Isa 45:16: "go in confusion together") is itself the shame experience. Jer 31:19 (vc=38509) — "after I was *instructed*, I struck my thigh; I was ashamed" — instruction (cognitive engagement) produces the shame recognition. The wisdom literature pattern (Pro 18:13 — answering before listening is folly and shame) shows shame as the consequence of cognitive failure (listening bypassed). Shame is cognitively engaged throughout: it requires self-assessment, comparison with a standard, and recognition of the gap.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 collapses confident cognition: the defeated "go in confusion" — their ability to think through their situation and act effectively is destroyed. Cognitive paralysis accompanies military defeat (Jer 49:23 — "melting in fear, troubled like the sea"). In VCG-03, God's abasement targets the cognitive self-assessment of the proud.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The cognitive worth-assessment process is engaged and distorted in CHAR-3: the dishonorer makes a wrong cognitive judgment about worth. The structural-dishonour mode (VCG-02) is more cognitively neutral — it is the result of sovereign assignment rather than a cognitive failure.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is a cognitive operation — the conscience assesses against a standard (God's sight, created order, community norms) and produces a judgment. The cognitive faculty is CHAR-4's primary operating mode. VCG-03 shows cognitive corruption: the evaluative judgment is produced but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment ("this person is of no account") is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4's cognitive assessment about standing; Rom 14:3/10's cognitive-evaluative judgment about a brother's worth before God — these show the cognitive faculty producing CHAR-5. For the recipient, the cognitive dimension is engaged in the ongoing self-assessment that contempt-shame distorts.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Cognition is engaged in CHAR-6 through the moral self-assessment that innocence requires. Abimelech's appeal to his innocence (Gen 20:5) involves cognitive self-assessment: he knows he acted in ignorance and moral intention. Psa 73:13's lament involves cognitive evaluation: the psalmist has cognitively assessed his own moral maintenance and found it, in his experience, to have been in vain. The cognitive faculty is engaged in CHAR-6's self-assessment and moral accounting.

---

---

##### T3.2.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its cognitive-collapse form (idolatry exposed, confident belief destroyed), shame **impairs** cognition — the shamed idol-maker "goes in confusion." In its corrective form, shame **deepens** cognition: after instruction-and-shame (Jer 31:19), the person comes to a clearer self-knowledge. The conscience-awakening passages (1Cor 6:5; 15:34) show shame *enabling* cognitive clarity: Paul directs shame at the Corinthians' failure to produce a wise person for disputes — shame is the tool for awakening cognitive wisdom. Thus shame's cognitive effect mirrors its perceptive effect: destructive in its paralysing form, constructive in its corrective form.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 collapses confident cognition: the defeated "go in confusion" — their ability to think through their situation and act effectively is destroyed. Cognitive paralysis accompanies military defeat (Jer 49:23 — "melting in fear, troubled like the sea"). In VCG-03, God's abasement targets the cognitive self-assessment of the proud.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The cognitive worth-assessment process is engaged and distorted in CHAR-3: the dishonorer makes a wrong cognitive judgment about worth. The structural-dishonour mode (VCG-02) is more cognitively neutral — it is the result of sovereign assignment rather than a cognitive failure.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is a cognitive operation — the conscience assesses against a standard (God's sight, created order, community norms) and produces a judgment. The cognitive faculty is CHAR-4's primary operating mode. VCG-03 shows cognitive corruption: the evaluative judgment is produced but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment ("this person is of no account") is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4's cognitive assessment about standing; Rom 14:3/10's cognitive-evaluative judgment about a brother's worth before God — these show the cognitive faculty producing CHAR-5. For the recipient, the cognitive dimension is engaged in the ongoing self-assessment that contempt-shame distorts.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Cognition is engaged in CHAR-6 through the moral self-assessment that innocence requires. Abimelech's appeal to his innocence (Gen 20:5) involves cognitive self-assessment: he knows he acted in ignorance and moral intention. Psa 73:13's lament involves cognitive evaluation: the psalmist has cognitively assessed his own moral maintenance and found it, in his experience, to have been in vain. The cognitive faculty is engaged in CHAR-6's self-assessment and moral accounting.

---

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That shame is cognitively engaged at both ends: it is produced by cognitive failure (misplaced trust, idolatry, folly) and it produces cognitive response (either collapse-confusion or clarity-through-correction). The cognitive dimension confirms that CHAR-1 is not a purely emotional phenomenon — it has deep cognitive roots and cognitive consequences.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 collapses confident cognition: the defeated "go in confusion" — their ability to think through their situation and act effectively is destroyed. Cognitive paralysis accompanies military defeat (Jer 49:23 — "melting in fear, troubled like the sea"). In VCG-03, God's abasement targets the cognitive self-assessment of the proud.

---

The cognitive worth-assessment process is engaged and distorted in CHAR-3: the dishonorer makes a wrong cognitive judgment about worth. The structural-dishonour mode (VCG-02) is more cognitively neutral — it is the result of sovereign assignment rather than a cognitive failure.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The cognitive faculty is CHAR-4's primary operating mode. VCG-03 shows cognitive corruption: the evaluative judgment is produced but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er's cognitive faculty is engaged: the worth-assessment judgment ("this person is of no account") is a cognitive act. 1Cor 6:4's cognitive assessment about standing; Rom 14:3/10's cognitive-evaluative judgment about a brother's worth before God — these show the cognitive faculty producing CHAR-5. For the recipient, the cognitive dimension is engaged in the ongoing self-assessment that contempt-shame distorts.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Cognition is engaged in CHAR-6 through the moral self-assessment that innocence requires. Abimelech's appeal to his innocence (Gen 20:5) involves cognitive self-assessment: he knows he acted in ignorance and moral intention. Psa 73:13's lament involves cognitive evaluation: the psalmist has cognitively assessed his own moral maintenance and found it, in his experience, to have been in vain. The cognitive faculty is engaged in CHAR-6's self-assessment and moral accounting.

---

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Eze 16:61 (vc=38511): "then you will *remember* your ways and be ashamed" — memory activating shame. Eze 16:63 (vc=65575) — "that you may *remember* and be confounded" — memory paired with the shame-silencing. The generational dimension of shame (Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers") shows shame carried in collective memory. Isa 54:4 (vc=34838) — "you will *forget* the shame of your youth" — God's promise directly addresses the memory-load of shame, promising its dissolution. Shame and memory are structurally linked: shame is partly constituted by memory (the remembered failure or wound) and is resolved when memory is reoriented (forgetting the shame, or remembering it differently under atonement).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32; Jer 23:40) shows CHAR-2 engaging memory through its persistence: "perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — the humiliation is branded into the identity-record. Warriors who bear shame into the pit carry a memory of their defeat outlasting their life. Memory in CHAR-2 operates as the vehicle for the enduring burden.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced in the 15-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 16-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Memory is engaged in CHAR-5 through the accumulated identity-formation of sustained contempt. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is a memory-constituted condition: the accumulated contempt of years has deposited into a self-understanding that the person carries as their ongoing identity. The throwing off of the cloak is a memory-renunciation act — a decisive abandonment of the shame-identity that contempt has written into the person's inner record.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Memory is engaged in CHAR-6 through the psalmist's appeal to his maintained moral record: "I have kept my heart clean" (Psa 73:13) is a memory-claim about sustained moral integrity. The psalmist's maintenance of innocence is something he remembers and can appeal to as a sustained pattern, not merely a momentary state.

---

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame **deepens** painful memory: "my days are spent in shame" (Jer 20:18) — the chronic inner condition is fed by the ongoing memory of disgrace. Eze 16:61 shows shame activating memory of past failures. But shame can also motivate memory-healing: the penitential shame of M07-C-VCG-01 leads to memory-with-contrition that opens toward renewal (Eze 43:10-11). The eschatological promise (Isa 54:4 — "you will forget") directly addresses shame's memory-bind — divine act releases the person from the memory-load of shame. Thus shame and memory are in a complex relationship: shame feeds on memory; memory of shame can be either paralyzing or corrective; only divine act or trust-in-God fully resolves the memory dimension.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32; Jer 23:40) shows CHAR-2 engaging memory through its persistence: "perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — the humiliation is branded into the identity-record. Warriors who bear shame into the pit carry a memory of their defeat outlasting their life. Memory in CHAR-2 operates as the vehicle for the enduring burden.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced in the 15-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 16-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Memory is engaged in CHAR-5 through the accumulated identity-formation of sustained contempt. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is a memory-constituted condition: the accumulated contempt of years has deposited into a self-understanding that the person carries as their ongoing identity. ---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The psalmist's maintenance of innocence is something he remembers and can appeal to as a sustained pattern, not merely a momentary state.

---

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; memory engagement is directly evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32; Jer 23:40) shows CHAR-2 engaging memory through its persistence: "perpetual shame, which shall not be forgotten" — the humiliation is branded into the identity-record. Warriors who bear shame into the pit carry a memory of their defeat outlasting their life. Memory in CHAR-2 operates as the vehicle for the enduring burden.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced in the 15-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 16-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Memory is engaged in CHAR-5 through the accumulated identity-formation of sustained contempt. Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is a memory-constituted condition: the accumulated contempt of years has deposited into a self-understanding that the person carries as their ongoing identity. The psalmist's maintenance of innocence is something he remembers and can appeal to as a sustained pattern, not merely a momentary state.

---

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame is itself primarily an affective phenomenon — the felt collapse of dignity is an affective event. The evidence is uniformly phenomenological across the corpus: "I am filled with disgrace" (Job 10:15); "shame has covered my face" (Psa 44:15); "she groans and turns her face away" (Lam 1:8); "Jonathan rose from the table in fierce anger... for he was grieved" (1Sa 20:34 — vc=38502, shame producing emotional pain in a third party). The M07-A material is particularly rich in affective texture: the mother who has "grown feeble and fainted" from shame (Jer 15:9), the farmers covering their heads in shame before drought (Jer 14:3-4). Affect is CHAR-1's primary mode.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 produces strong negative affect: dismay, confusion, wailing (Jer 48:20 — "wail and cry"), fear (Jer 49:23 — "melt in fear"), and derision in the observer. The cosmic register (Isa 24:23 — moon and sun ashamed before divine glory) extends the affective dimension. CHAR-2 impairs positive affect by stripping the inner confidence from which positive states arise.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-3 is present but secondary — in the VCG-01 active mode, the dishonorer's inner disposition of contempt or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9 in CHAR-5) carries an affective component. Paul's reception of dishonour "without altering inner integrity" (2Cor 6:8) implies the affective faculty has been stabilised against the dishonour signal.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 engages affect in the inverted mode: "they glory in their shame" (Phili 3:19) — the affective response to shamefulness is joy/pride rather than recoil. VCG-02's "dishonorable passions" (Rom 1:26) and "consumed with passion" (Rom 1:27) show affect in its disordered form as the engine of the shameful conduct. Functioning CHAR-4 produces recoil as its affective response to the shameful.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily an affective phenomenon in its received form: the shame produced by contempt is felt — it wounds the person's sense of worth and produces the inner pain of being treated as nothing. Psa 14:6's shaming of the poor's "plans" targets their inner affective confidence (their hope and aspiration). 1Pe 3:9's call to bless rather than retaliate shows the affective pull toward retaliatory anger that verbal contempt produces.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-6 is engaged in Psa 73:13's lament: the psalmist's maintained innocence is accompanied by existential suffering — the emotion of frustrated confidence in innocence's protective value. The affect here is not the joy that innocence should ideally produce (access to God, Psa 26:6) but the anguish of apparent futility. CHAR-6's affective register includes both the confidence of VCG-01 and the anguish of VCG-02's questioning.

---

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame primarily **impairs** affect in one specific direction: it collapses the positive affective range (confidence, joy, openness) while intensifying the negative range (grief, turmoil, inner pain). The enemies "overtaken by shame and inner turmoil simultaneously" (Psa 6:10) — shame produces turmoil alongside itself. However, in the voluntary-bearing register (M07-A-VCG-03), shame does not impair affect in the same way: Act 5:41 — the apostles "rejoice" while bearing dishonour. The affect of joy can coexist with borne shame when the will is oriented toward a greater object. Heb 12:2 — Jesus endures the cross "for the joy set before him" — demonstrates that the affective register can be oriented above shame's impact when the will is engaged at the level of eschatological hope.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 produces strong negative affect: dismay, confusion, wailing (Jer 48:20 — "wail and cry"), fear (Jer 49:23 — "melt in fear"), and derision in the observer. The cosmic register (Isa 24:23 — moon and sun ashamed before divine glory) extends the affective dimension. CHAR-2 impairs positive affect by stripping the inner confidence from which positive states arise.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-3 is present but secondary — in the VCG-01 active mode, the dishonorer's inner disposition of contempt or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9 in CHAR-5) carries an affective component. Paul's reception of dishonour "without altering inner integrity" (2Cor 6:8) implies the affective faculty has been stabilised against the dishonour signal.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 engages affect in the inverted mode: "they glory in their shame" (Phili 3:19) — the affective response to shamefulness is joy/pride rather than recoil. VCG-02's "dishonorable passions" (Rom 1:26) and "consumed with passion" (Rom 1:27) show affect in its disordered form as the engine of the shameful conduct. Functioning CHAR-4 produces recoil as its affective response to the shameful.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily an affective phenomenon in its received form: the shame produced by contempt is felt — it wounds the person's sense of worth and produces the inner pain of being treated as nothing. Psa 14:6's shaming of the poor's "plans" targets their inner affective confidence (their hope and aspiration). 1Pe 3:9's call to bless rather than retaliate shows the affective pull toward retaliatory anger that verbal contempt produces.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-6 is engaged in Psa 73:13's lament: the psalmist's maintained innocence is accompanied by existential suffering — the emotion of frustrated confidence in innocence's protective value. The affect here is not the joy that innocence should ideally produce (access to God, Psa 26:6) but the anguish of apparent futility. CHAR-6's affective register includes both the confidence of VCG-01 and the anguish of VCG-02's questioning.

---

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That shame's affective impact is not inevitable — it can be transcended when the will is oriented toward a greater affective reality. But this transcendence is exceptional (M07-A-VCG-03) and requires specific conditions (trust in God, eschatological joy as the motivating object). In its ordinary operation, shame is the primary affective event.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 produces strong negative affect: dismay, confusion, wailing (Jer 48:20 — "wail and cry"), fear (Jer 49:23 — "melt in fear"), and derision in the observer. The cosmic register (Isa 24:23 — moon and sun ashamed before divine glory) extends the affective dimension. CHAR-2 impairs positive affect by stripping the inner confidence from which positive states arise.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-3 is present but secondary — in the VCG-01 active mode, the dishonorer's inner disposition of contempt or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9 in CHAR-5) carries an affective component. Paul's reception of dishonour "without altering inner integrity" (2Cor 6:8) implies the affective faculty has been stabilised against the dishonour signal.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 engages affect in the inverted mode: "they glory in their shame" (Phili 3:19) — the affective response to shamefulness is joy/pride rather than recoil. VCG-02's "dishonorable passions" (Rom 1:26) and "consumed with passion" (Rom 1:27) show affect in its disordered form as the engine of the shameful conduct. Functioning CHAR-4 produces recoil as its affective response to the shameful.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily an affective phenomenon in its received form: the shame produced by contempt is felt — it wounds the person's sense of worth and produces the inner pain of being treated as nothing. Psa 14:6's shaming of the poor's "plans" targets their inner affective confidence (their hope and aspiration). 1Pe 3:9's call to bless rather than retaliate shows the affective pull toward retaliatory anger that verbal contempt produces.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The affective dimension of CHAR-6 is engaged in Psa 73:13's lament: the psalmist's maintained innocence is accompanied by existential suffering — the emotion of frustrated confidence in innocence's protective value. The affect here is not the joy that innocence should ideally produce (access to God, Psa 26:6) but the anguish of apparent futility. CHAR-6's affective register includes both the confidence of VCG-01 and the anguish of VCG-02's questioning.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The 224-verse corpus does not provide evidence of shame directly engaging or impairing the creative faculty (imagination, capacity to originate). Shame's primary engagement is with the conscience, the affect, the will, and the cognitive faculty — not with creativity. This is a noteworthy silence: shame appears not to be a creativity-engaging phenomenon in the scriptural evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

Not evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Not evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

Not evidenced in the 8-verse corpus. Silent.

---

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

Not evidenced. The evidence is silent on creativity.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. Silent.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The CHAR-1 corpus is silent on the relationship between shame and the creative faculty. No finding can be made on this prompt.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse CHAR-2 corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)
