---

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Strongly and throughout. The volitional faculty is engaged across all three sub-group registers, though differently in each. In M07-A (unjust wound), the will is engaged in how the person responds to received shame: whether they collapse into it (Pro 12:4 — "rottenness in the bones"), absorb it with inner reserve (Pro 12:16 — the prudent ignores an insult), or voluntarily bear it for God's sake (Isa 50:6-7; Heb 12:2). In M07-B (moral consequence), the will is the point at which shame's signal is either received (producing corrective action) or refused (producing the seared conscience of Jer 3:3; 6:15). In M07-C (divine encounter), the will is engaged in choosing to trust God as the shame-protecting orientation (Psa 31:1; 119:80; Rom 9:33; 10:11).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs volition: the humiliated cannot return to public life (2Sa 10:5), cannot respond (Mat 22:12), retreat rather than advance. The enforced character of CHAR-2 is the primary volitional engagement — the person's will is not operative in the humiliation; it is done to them. The absence of the proper inner disposition of regard (entrepō evidence) shows that the failure of will to recognise proper standing enables CHAR-2 to become necessary.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 active-dishonour is deeply volitional — it requires the willful act of refused-acknowledgment. "Willful inner refusal to acknowledge worth" (Pass A on Joh 8:49, vc=35000). The absent-regard of Luk 18:2/4 is a sustained volitional disposition. VCG-02 structural dishonour is less volitionally constituted — it arrives as assignment rather than choice.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 is most volitionally engaged: "rulers dearly love shame" (Hos 4:18) — the will has chosen dishonour as its object. Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" — the will has oriented the evaluative faculty toward an earthly standard. Functioning CHAR-4 (VCG-01) requires the will's cooperation to renounce shameful ways (2Cor 4:2 — "we have renounced"). The volitional dimension is significant across all three VCGs.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Volition is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's willful act of dismissal (exoutheneō is consistently presented as a volitional disposition in its VCG-01 register — Luk 18:9: "trusted in themselves that they were righteous" and "treated others with contempt"). For the recipient, the will is engaged in the response: whether they retaliate (1Pe 3:9's temptation) or bless (1Pe 3:9's call). The decision to throw off the cloak (Mar 10:50) is a decisive volitional act of shame-identity abandonment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Volition is CHAR-6's constituting faculty: the maintenance of innocence (Psa 73:13 — "I have kept my heart clean") is a volitional practice. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) is precisely a failure at the volitional level — the will's capacity for moral purity is so damaged by sustained idolatry that innocence-oriented choices are no longer possible. CHAR-6 is constituted by the will's sustained orientation toward moral cleanness and free-from-deliberate-wrongdoing choices.

---

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its acute received form, shame **impairs** volition by collapsing the person's inner resources for self-determination — the shamed person cannot act confidently, cannot lift the face, withdraws from social agency. In its corrective form, shame **enables** volition by clearing out false confidence and creating the space for genuine reorientation: 2Ch 30:15 — the shame-activated priests immediately consecrate themselves. In the voluntary-bearing mode, a strong will **overcomes** shame's impairing effect — Heb 12:2, Isa 50:7. The three possibilities (impaired by shame, enabled by corrective shame, overcoming shame through will) constitute the full volitional-shame relationship in the evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs volition: the humiliated cannot return to public life (2Sa 10:5), cannot respond (Mat 22:12), retreat rather than advance. The enforced character of CHAR-2 is the primary volitional engagement — the person's will is not operative in the humiliation; it is done to them. The absence of the proper inner disposition of regard (entrepō evidence) shows that the failure of will to recognise proper standing enables CHAR-2 to become necessary.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 active-dishonour is deeply volitional — it requires the willful act of refused-acknowledgment. "Willful inner refusal to acknowledge worth" (Pass A on Joh 8:49, vc=35000). The absent-regard of Luk 18:2/4 is a sustained volitional disposition. VCG-02 structural dishonour is less volitionally constituted — it arrives as assignment rather than choice.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 is most volitionally engaged: "rulers dearly love shame" (Hos 4:18) — the will has chosen dishonour as its object. Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" — the will has oriented the evaluative faculty toward an earthly standard. Functioning CHAR-4 (VCG-01) requires the will's cooperation to renounce shameful ways (2Cor 4:2 — "we have renounced"). The volitional dimension is significant across all three VCGs.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Volition is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's willful act of dismissal (exoutheneō is consistently presented as a volitional disposition in its VCG-01 register — Luk 18:9: "trusted in themselves that they were righteous" and "treated others with contempt"). CHAR-6 is constituted by the will's sustained orientation toward moral cleanness and free-from-deliberate-wrongdoing choices.

---

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That the will is the decisive faculty in CHAR-1's operation: whether shame functions as wound, corrective, or borne-for-God's-sake depends ultimately on the orientation of the will toward or away from a greater referent. Shame without will engagement is merely paralysis. Shame with the will engaged toward God becomes either the gateway to restoration (M07-C) or the mark of faithful endurance (M07-A-VCG-03).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 primarily impairs volition: the humiliated cannot return to public life (2Sa 10:5), cannot respond (Mat 22:12), retreat rather than advance. The enforced character of CHAR-2 is the primary volitional engagement — the person's will is not operative in the humiliation; it is done to them. The absence of the proper inner disposition of regard (entrepō evidence) shows that the failure of will to recognise proper standing enables CHAR-2 to become necessary.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 active-dishonour is deeply volitional — it requires the willful act of refused-acknowledgment. "Willful inner refusal to acknowledge worth" (Pass A on Joh 8:49, vc=35000). The absent-regard of Luk 18:2/4 is a sustained volitional disposition. VCG-02 structural dishonour is less volitionally constituted — it arrives as assignment rather than choice.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

VCG-03 is most volitionally engaged: "rulers dearly love shame" (Hos 4:18) — the will has chosen dishonour as its object. Phili 3:19's "minds set on earthly things" — the will has oriented the evaluative faculty toward an earthly standard. Functioning CHAR-4 (VCG-01) requires the will's cooperation to renounce shameful ways (2Cor 4:2 — "we have renounced"). The volitional dimension is significant across all three VCGs.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Volition is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's willful act of dismissal (exoutheneō is consistently presented as a volitional disposition in its VCG-01 register — Luk 18:9: "trusted in themselves that they were righteous" and "treated others with contempt"). For the recipient, the will is engaged in the response: whether they retaliate (1Pe 3:9's temptation) or bless (1Pe 3:9's call). **[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Volition is CHAR-6's constituting faculty: the maintenance of innocence (Psa 73:13 — "I have kept my heart clean") is a volitional practice. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) is precisely a failure at the volitional level — the will's capacity for moral purity is so damaged by sustained idolatry that innocence-oriented choices are no longer possible. CHAR-6 is constituted by the will's sustained orientation toward moral cleanness and free-from-deliberate-wrongdoing choices.

---

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. Shame's primary relationship with agency is *impairing* — it withdraws the person's capacity to act, initiate, and present themselves. Ezr 9:6 — the inability to lift the face is the literal inability to present oneself before God to initiate worship or petition. Psa 127:5 — the man without sons "cannot speak with his enemies in the gate" — shame as the loss of public agency. Job 10:15 — "I cannot lift up my head" — shame as the inner paralysis of the agency to move forward. The backward-turning of the enemies under shame (Psa 35:4; 129:5) shows agency reversed — shame drives movement backward rather than forward.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 withdraws or collapses the recipient's agency: they cannot speak (Mat 22:12), cannot re-enter public space (2Sa 10:5), must retreat (Jer 48:39). In VCG-03, God is the agent; the proud person's agency is precisely what is overridden. CHAR-2 is the enforced withdrawal of agency from the person whose pride had inflated it beyond its proper scope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonorer exercises agency in the act of worth-denial (VCG-01). The dishonoured's agency may be affected when dishonour restricts their relational capacity (the poor man whose case cannot receive justice, Jam 2:6). The structural mode (VCG-02) restricts the recipient's agency in terms of what they can access or what roles they can occupy.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4's functioning enables the exercise of principled moral agency — the person who recognises and renounces the shameful can act with integrity. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) produces misdirected agency — the person acts, but in the direction of what is actually shameful. VCG-02's disordered desire overwhelms agency with appetite.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Agency is impaired in the recipient by CHAR-5: Psa 14:6 — the plans of the poor are shamed (targeted for dismissal) — their capacity to act on their own plans and hopes is suppressed by the contempt. Paul's concern that contempt toward Timothy (1Cor 16:11) would "devalue his ministry and undermine his standing" shows agency-impairment as the downstream effect of sustained CHAR-5. Conversely, the act of throwing off the cloak (Mar 10:50) is the regaining of agency in response to a stronger worth-assignment from Jesus.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 enables agency: the person with clean hands and a blameless heart can approach God's altar (Psa 26:6) — the agency of worship is enabled by CHAR-6. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) impairs agency in the specific domain of approach to God — the people cannot exercise the agency of genuine covenant approach because innocence-capacity has been lost.

---

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its ordinary form, CHAR-1 **impairs** agency. But in its corrective form, shame *activates* agency: 2Ch 30:15 — shame immediately produces the agency of consecration. In the voluntary-bearing register, agency is sustained against shame's impairing pull: the servant sets his face like flint (Isa 50:7) — agency maintained in the face of shame's threat. The eschatological resolution (Isa 54:4; Zep 3:19) restores the agency that shame had suppressed: shame removed means the person can once again speak and act without the inner paralysis.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 withdraws or collapses the recipient's agency: they cannot speak (Mat 22:12), cannot re-enter public space (2Sa 10:5), must retreat (Jer 48:39). In VCG-03, God is the agent; the proud person's agency is precisely what is overridden. CHAR-2 is the enforced withdrawal of agency from the person whose pride had inflated it beyond its proper scope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonorer exercises agency in the act of worth-denial (VCG-01). The dishonoured's agency may be affected when dishonour restricts their relational capacity (the poor man whose case cannot receive justice, Jam 2:6). The structural mode (VCG-02) restricts the recipient's agency in terms of what they can access or what roles they can occupy.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4's functioning enables the exercise of principled moral agency — the person who recognises and renounces the shameful can act with integrity. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) produces misdirected agency — the person acts, but in the direction of what is actually shameful. VCG-02's disordered desire overwhelms agency with appetite.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Agency is impaired in the recipient by CHAR-5: Psa 14:6 — the plans of the poor are shamed (targeted for dismissal) — their capacity to act on their own plans and hopes is suppressed by the contempt. Paul's concern that contempt toward Timothy (1Cor 16:11) would "devalue his ministry and undermine his standing" shows agency-impairment as the downstream effect of sustained CHAR-5. Conversely, the act of throwing off the cloak (Mar 10:50) is the regaining of agency in response to a stronger worth-assignment from Jesus.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 enables agency: the person with clean hands and a blameless heart can approach God's altar (Psa 26:6) — the agency of worship is enabled by CHAR-6. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) impairs agency in the specific domain of approach to God — the people cannot exercise the agency of genuine covenant approach because innocence-capacity has been lost.

---

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That CHAR-1 is fundamentally an agency-impairment phenomenon in its ordinary operation, and that the characteristic's resolution is tied to the restoration of agency. The shame-lifting promises are not merely about dignity restored in the abstract — they are about the concrete capacity to stand, speak, and act in the world and before God being restored to the person from whom shame had taken it.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 withdraws or collapses the recipient's agency: they cannot speak (Mat 22:12), cannot re-enter public space (2Sa 10:5), must retreat (Jer 48:39). In VCG-03, God is the agent; the proud person's agency is precisely what is overridden. CHAR-2 is the enforced withdrawal of agency from the person whose pride had inflated it beyond its proper scope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonorer exercises agency in the act of worth-denial (VCG-01). The dishonoured's agency may be affected when dishonour restricts their relational capacity (the poor man whose case cannot receive justice, Jam 2:6). The structural mode (VCG-02) restricts the recipient's agency in terms of what they can access or what roles they can occupy.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4's functioning enables the exercise of principled moral agency — the person who recognises and renounces the shameful can act with integrity. The inverted conscience (VCG-03) produces misdirected agency — the person acts, but in the direction of what is actually shameful. VCG-02's disordered desire overwhelms agency with appetite.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Agency is impaired in the recipient by CHAR-5: Psa 14:6 — the plans of the poor are shamed (targeted for dismissal) — their capacity to act on their own plans and hopes is suppressed by the contempt. Paul's concern that contempt toward Timothy (1Cor 16:11) would "devalue his ministry and undermine his standing" shows agency-impairment as the downstream effect of sustained CHAR-5. Conversely, the act of throwing off the cloak (Mar 10:50) is the regaining of agency in response to a stronger worth-assignment from Jesus.

---

CHAR-6 enables agency: the person with clean hands and a blameless heart can approach God's altar (Psa 26:6) — the agency of worship is enabled by CHAR-6. The incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) impairs agency in the specific domain of approach to God — the people cannot exercise the agency of genuine covenant approach because innocence-capacity has been lost.

---

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Pervasively. The moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, good, and true — is the primary internal generator of shame in the M07-B and M07-C registers. Shame is what the moral evaluation faculty produces when it accurately registers failure. The Proverbs pattern (Pro 3:35; 6:33; 13:5; 13:18; 18:3; 18:13) consistently presents shame as the moral-evaluation output of specific failures: folly inherits disgrace, deception produces shame, wickedness generates dishonour. The M07-C guilt-shame register is entirely about the moral evaluation faculty registering the person's own sin before God's holiness. The M07-B seared-conscience register is about the destruction of the moral evaluation faculty: those who cannot blush have lost the capacity for moral evaluation that should produce shame.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

In VCG-03, CHAR-2 is deeply morally evaluated: Pro 11:2 — "when pride comes, then comes disgrace" — is a wisdom-tradition moral evaluation of the pride to humiliation connection. God's abasing act is morally just. The VCG-01 and VCG-02 modes are more ambiguous morally — David's envoys were humiliated unjustly. The moral evaluation of CHAR-2 depends on whether the humiliation is just (corrective of pride) or unjust (inflicted on the innocent).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed moral evaluation (the worth-assessment capacity distorted). Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — is the clearest case of moral evaluation corrupted: the person evaluates themselves as honouring the law while their conduct denies it, and simultaneously dishonours God.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is constitutively the moral-evaluation faculty in its shame-recognitive mode. It is the characteristic most directly about moral evaluation. VCG-03 shows this faculty corrupted — the inverted conscience does evaluate, but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's distorted moral evaluation (treating persons as of less worth than they have) and through the community's moral evaluation of the contempt-act itself. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10; 1Cor 16:11; 1Th 5:20) are moral-evaluative instructions: despising a brother is wrong, and the community's moral evaluation must recognise it as wrong.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-6: the person who claims innocence (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) is making a moral-evaluative self-assessment — they are evaluating their own conduct against the standard of blameless moral integrity. God's confirmation of Abimelech's innocence (Gen 20:6) is the authoritative moral evaluation that validates the self-assessment. CHAR-6 depends on and engages the moral-evaluation faculty in its self-assessment mode.

---

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its corrective form, shame **enables and deepens** moral evaluation: entropē (1Cor 6:5; 15:34) uses shame to awaken the community's moral evaluation of their own failure. The gateway-of-shame passages (Eze 43:10-11) show shame as the precondition for the house of Israel receiving the moral design of the temple — shame clears the inner space for accurate moral perception. In its hardened form, shame's absence **impairs** moral evaluation catastrophically — the seared conscience neither evaluates nor corrects. In its acute wound-form (M07-A unjust shame), shame can **bypass** moral evaluation by arriving before it — the unjust wound produces shame regardless of what the moral evaluation faculty says about the person's actual standing.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

In VCG-03, CHAR-2 is deeply morally evaluated: Pro 11:2 — "when pride comes, then comes disgrace" — is a wisdom-tradition moral evaluation of the pride to humiliation connection. God's abasing act is morally just. The VCG-01 and VCG-02 modes are more ambiguous morally — David's envoys were humiliated unjustly. The moral evaluation of CHAR-2 depends on whether the humiliation is just (corrective of pride) or unjust (inflicted on the innocent).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed moral evaluation (the worth-assessment capacity distorted). Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — is the clearest case of moral evaluation corrupted: the person evaluates themselves as honouring the law while their conduct denies it, and simultaneously dishonours God.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is constitutively the moral-evaluation faculty in its shame-recognitive mode. It is the characteristic most directly about moral evaluation. VCG-03 shows this faculty corrupted — the inverted conscience does evaluate, but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's distorted moral evaluation (treating persons as of less worth than they have) and through the community's moral evaluation of the contempt-act itself. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10; 1Cor 16:11; 1Th 5:20) are moral-evaluative instructions: despising a brother is wrong, and the community's moral evaluation must recognise it as wrong.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-6: the person who claims innocence (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) is making a moral-evaluative self-assessment — they are evaluating their own conduct against the standard of blameless moral integrity. God's confirmation of Abimelech's innocence (Gen 20:6) is the authoritative moral evaluation that validates the self-assessment. CHAR-6 depends on and engages the moral-evaluation faculty in its self-assessment mode.

---

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That CHAR-1's relationship with moral evaluation is among its most analytically significant features. Shame is simultaneously produced by moral evaluation (when functioning), and can be the tool that restores moral evaluation (when deploying the corrective signal). The destruction of shame-receptivity (seared conscience) is simultaneously the destruction of moral evaluation — they are the same faculty in its shamed and shameless modes.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

In VCG-03, CHAR-2 is deeply morally evaluated: Pro 11:2 — "when pride comes, then comes disgrace" — is a wisdom-tradition moral evaluation of the pride to humiliation connection. God's abasing act is morally just. The VCG-01 and VCG-02 modes are more ambiguous morally — David's envoys were humiliated unjustly. The moral evaluation of CHAR-2 depends on whether the humiliation is just (corrective of pride) or unjust (inflicted on the innocent).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by failed moral evaluation (the worth-assessment capacity distorted). Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law while breaking it — is the clearest case of moral evaluation corrupted: the person evaluates themselves as honouring the law while their conduct denies it, and simultaneously dishonours God.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is constitutively the moral-evaluation faculty in its shame-recognitive mode. It is the characteristic most directly about moral evaluation. VCG-03 shows this faculty corrupted — the inverted conscience does evaluate, but by a wrong standard.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-5 through the contempt-er's distorted moral evaluation (treating persons as of less worth than they have) and through the community's moral evaluation of the contempt-act itself. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10; 1Cor 16:11; 1Th 5:20) are moral-evaluative instructions: despising a brother is wrong, and the community's moral evaluation must recognise it as wrong.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Moral evaluation is engaged in CHAR-6: the person who claims innocence (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) is making a moral-evaluative self-assessment — they are evaluating their own conduct against the standard of blameless moral integrity. God's confirmation of Abimelech's innocence (Gen 20:6) is the authoritative moral evaluation that validates the self-assessment. CHAR-6 depends on and engages the moral-evaluation faculty in its self-assessment mode.

---

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, and this is CHAR-1's most distinctive inner-faculty relationship. Conscience is the faculty that registers guilt, moral failure, and deviation from the right — and shame is what the conscience *feels* when it makes those registrations. The M07-B-VCG-04 material (Jer 6:15; 8:12; 3:3) is entirely about the conscience's relation to shame: the loss of the capacity for shame = the death of the conscience. The M07-C-VCG-01 material (Ezr 9:6; 2Ch 30:15; Jer 31:19; Eze 43:10-11) shows the conscience receiving the shame signal and activating corrective response. The M07-B-VCG-05 corrective-shame passages (1Cor 6:5; 15:34) explicitly invoke shame to activate the conscience. Conscience and shame are functionally fused in the CHAR-1 evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 may activate conscience as a secondary effect when the humiliated person recognises the moral cause (VCG-03: those who strive against God's servant are put to shame and their aggression's futility is recognised). But CHAR-2 primarily bypasses conscience as the receiving faculty — the humiliation arrives regardless of what the conscience says. The moral-corrective function of VCG-03 is delivered from outside (divine act) rather than through the conscience from within.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-3 engaging or impairing the conscience specifically. The judge's self-acknowledged absence of regard (Luk 18:4) is the closest — he is conscious of his lack of respect. Silent on conscience as the specific receptive faculty.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is the conscience's primary mode of shame-recognitive operation. 2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" — names the conscience as both CHAR-4's location and its relational field. VCG-03 shows the conscience inverted. The conscience is CHAR-4's defining constitutional location.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not directly evidence the conscience as the specific receptive faculty for CHAR-5. The contempt-er's conscience is implicated (the self-righteous person of Luk 18:9 has a malfunctioning conscience-conscience relationship), but the conscience as the faculty specifically engaged by CHAR-5 in its received form is not directly evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscience is CHAR-6's primary inner faculty: the clean conscience is what innocence produces and what guilt-shame's absence confirms. The absence of the guilty conscience is the inner condition of CHAR-6. The loss of innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) is simultaneously the loss of the conscience's capacity for guilt-recognition (the conscience that can no longer recognise its own moral failure cannot attain innocence). CHAR-6 and the conscience are structurally linked: functional conscience + no deliberate wrongdoing = CHAR-6's inner condition.

---

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame is conscience's primary experiential output, so the relationship is constitutive rather than enabling or impairing in the normal sense. Where the conscience functions, shame results from its registrations. Where shame is absent (seared conscience), conscience is absent. However, shame can also be the tool that *restores* conscience: the corrective-shame passages show shame being directed at someone to wake up their conscience (1Cor 6:5 — "I say this to your shame... can it be that there is no one among you wise enough?"). In this register, shame is the awakener of conscience rather than merely its product.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 may activate conscience as a secondary effect when the humiliated person recognises the moral cause (VCG-03: those who strive against God's servant are put to shame and their aggression's futility is recognised). But CHAR-2 primarily bypasses conscience as the receiving faculty — the humiliation arrives regardless of what the conscience says. The moral-corrective function of VCG-03 is delivered from outside (divine act) rather than through the conscience from within.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-3 engaging or impairing the conscience specifically. The judge's self-acknowledged absence of regard (Luk 18:4) is the closest — he is conscious of his lack of respect. Silent on conscience as the specific receptive faculty.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is the conscience's primary mode of shame-recognitive operation. 2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" — names the conscience as both CHAR-4's location and its relational field. VCG-03 shows the conscience inverted. The conscience is CHAR-4's defining constitutional location.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not directly evidence the conscience as the specific receptive faculty for CHAR-5. The contempt-er's conscience is implicated (the self-righteous person of Luk 18:9 has a malfunctioning conscience-conscience relationship), but the conscience as the faculty specifically engaged by CHAR-5 in its received form is not directly evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscience is CHAR-6's primary inner faculty: the clean conscience is what innocence produces and what guilt-shame's absence confirms. The absence of the guilty conscience is the inner condition of CHAR-6. The loss of innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) is simultaneously the loss of the conscience's capacity for guilt-recognition (the conscience that can no longer recognise its own moral failure cannot attain innocence). CHAR-6 and the conscience are structurally linked: functional conscience + no deliberate wrongdoing = CHAR-6's inner condition.

---

---

##### T3.9.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That the shame-conscience relationship is the structural core of CHAR-1. Shame is what a functioning conscience feels; the capacity for shame is the sign that conscience is alive; the loss of the capacity for shame (Jer 6:15; 8:12) is the death of conscience. The corrective deployment of shame (1Cor 6:5; 15:34) is the attempt to reactivate a conscience that has fallen asleep. This means CHAR-1 is essentially a conscience-phenomenon in its moral dimensions, and its engagement with conscience is the basis for its role in moral formation (see T5.5).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 may activate conscience as a secondary effect when the humiliated person recognises the moral cause (VCG-03: those who strive against God's servant are put to shame and their aggression's futility is recognised). But CHAR-2 primarily bypasses conscience as the receiving faculty — the humiliation arrives regardless of what the conscience says. The moral-corrective function of VCG-03 is delivered from outside (divine act) rather than through the conscience from within.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-3 engaging or impairing the conscience specifically. The judge's self-acknowledged absence of regard (Luk 18:4) is the closest — he is conscious of his lack of respect. Silent on conscience as the specific receptive faculty.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is the conscience's primary mode of shame-recognitive operation. 2Cor 4:2 — "commend ourselves to everyone's conscience in the sight of God" — names the conscience as both CHAR-4's location and its relational field. VCG-03 shows the conscience inverted. The conscience is CHAR-4's defining constitutional location.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not directly evidence the conscience as the specific receptive faculty for CHAR-5. The contempt-er's conscience is implicated (the self-righteous person of Luk 18:9 has a malfunctioning conscience-conscience relationship), but the conscience as the faculty specifically engaged by CHAR-5 in its received form is not directly evidenced. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscience is CHAR-6's primary inner faculty: the clean conscience is what innocence produces and what guilt-shame's absence confirms. The absence of the guilty conscience is the inner condition of CHAR-6. The loss of innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) is simultaneously the loss of the conscience's capacity for guilt-recognition (the conscience that can no longer recognise its own moral failure cannot attain innocence). CHAR-6 and the conscience are structurally linked: functional conscience + no deliberate wrongdoing = CHAR-6's inner condition.

---

---

#### T3.10 — Conscientiousness

##### T3.10.1 — Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is engaged at the output end of shame's corrective function. The priests of 2Ch 30:15 (vc=38506) demonstrate full conscientiousness in response to shame: inner shame (moral awareness activated) → decision to consecrate (volition) → immediate consecration (action). Eze 43:10-11 shows shame as the gateway to conscientious reception of the temple's design — shame activates the full integrated response. The M07-B-VCG-03 wisdom pattern (Pro 13:18 — "poverty and disgrace come to him who ignores instruction") is about the failure of conscientiousness (ignoring instruction = failure of the shame-conscience-volition-action integration) producing shame as the consequence.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-2 engaging the integrated moral-awareness/volition/action cycle of conscientiousness. The entrepō evidence implies that the absence of conscientiousness creates the conditions for CHAR-2, but CHAR-2 itself does not produce conscientiousness. Silent on direct engagement.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced directly. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 is the first step in conscientious action: moral awareness (conscience recognising the shameful) -> renunciation (volition acting on that recognition) -> principled conduct (action aligned with the moral awareness). 2Cor 4:2's full renunciation-and-open-statement sequence evidences this complete conscientiousness. VCG-03's inversion is the failure of conscientiousness at its first step (moral awareness corrupted).

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscientiousness is engaged in CHAR-6's maintenance: the sustained keeping of the heart clean (Psa 73:13) and the washing of hands in innocence (Psa 26:6) are acts of conscientious moral maintenance — the integrated moral awareness, volition, and action that keeps the inner moral condition of innocence operative. CHAR-6 is the outcome of conscientious practice; its loss (Hos 8:5) is the consequence of sustained non-conscientiousness (the repeated idolatrous choices that damage innocence-capacity).

---

---

##### T3.10.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Corrective shame **enables** conscientiousness by producing the moral-awareness that feeds the will and issues in action. Acute unjust shame **impairs** conscientiousness by paralyzing the agency component. The seared-conscience register **bypasses** conscientiousness entirely — the person acts without the moral awareness that should govern their acts.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-2 engaging the integrated moral-awareness/volition/action cycle of conscientiousness. The entrepō evidence implies that the absence of conscientiousness creates the conditions for CHAR-2, but CHAR-2 itself does not produce conscientiousness. Silent on direct engagement.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced directly. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 is the first step in conscientious action: moral awareness (conscience recognising the shameful) -> renunciation (volition acting on that recognition) -> principled conduct (action aligned with the moral awareness). 2Cor 4:2's full renunciation-and-open-statement sequence evidences this complete conscientiousness. VCG-03's inversion is the failure of conscientiousness at its first step (moral awareness corrupted).

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Conscientiousness is engaged in CHAR-6's maintenance: the sustained keeping of the heart clean (Psa 73:13) and the washing of hands in innocence (Psa 26:6) are acts of conscientious moral maintenance — the integrated moral awareness, volition, and action that keeps the inner moral condition of innocence operative. CHAR-6 is the outcome of conscientious practice; its loss (Hos 8:5) is the consequence of sustained non-conscientiousness (the repeated idolatrous choices that damage innocence-capacity).

---

---

##### T3.10.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That CHAR-1 is positioned as both a product and a trigger of conscientiousness. The person who lacks shame lacks the first component of conscientious functioning (moral awareness activated by guilt). The person who receives corrective shame has the first component restored. Shame's role in the conscientiousness system is that of moral-awareness trigger — without it, the system cannot function.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (S)

The 72-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-2 engaging the integrated moral-awareness/volition/action cycle of conscientiousness. The entrepō evidence implies that the absence of conscientiousness creates the conditions for CHAR-2, but CHAR-2 itself does not produce conscientiousness. Silent on direct engagement.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

Not evidenced directly. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 is the first step in conscientious action: moral awareness (conscience recognising the shameful) -> renunciation (volition acting on that recognition) -> principled conduct (action aligned with the moral awareness). 2Cor 4:2's full renunciation-and-open-statement sequence evidences this complete conscientiousness. VCG-03's inversion is the failure of conscientiousness at its first step (moral awareness corrupted).

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the 24-verse corpus. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is the outcome of conscientious practice; its loss (Hos 8:5) is the consequence of sustained non-conscientiousness (the repeated idolatrous choices that damage innocence-capacity).

---

---

#### T3.11 — Relational Capacity

##### T3.11.1 — Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Extensively and across all three registers. Shame is inherently relational — it always arises in relation to someone: enemies (M07-A-VCG-01), community (M07-A-VCG-01, M07-B), God (M07-C), allies (M07-A-VCG-02). The M07-A evidence shows shame damaging the relational capacity: the shamed person withdraws (turns back, covers the face), loses public voice (Psa 127:5 — cannot speak at the gate), and has their relational standing stripped. The M07-B corrective-shame passages show shame deployed within existing relationships (Paul to the Corinthians; community isolation of the disobedient in 2Th 3:14) — shame as a relational instrument for restoring broken relational faithfulness. The M07-C divine-encounter register shows shame as the inner state of a broken relational posture before God.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 severely impairs relational capacity. The shaved envoys cannot return to public social life; the silenced man cannot engage in dialogue; the defeated nations cannot sustain former relationships with neighbours (derision replaces respect). 1Cor 15:43's mortal body "sown in dishonor" is in a condition of diminished relational capacity; resurrection glory restores it. CHAR-2's relational dimension is fundamental: it is enacted through the relational field and its primary effect is the disruption of the person's relational standing and capacity.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is constitutively relational — it is the degradation of the relational-capacity in its worth-recognition mode. The judge who "neither fears God nor respects man" (Luk 18:2) has lost the relational-capacity component of appropriate regard for the worth of others. This is CHAR-3's most direct faculty engagement: it is the failure of the relational faculty's worth-recognition mode.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4's evaluative operation in VCG-01 engages the relational capacity through community norms (the social-moral judgments about hair, speech in assembly, financial conduct). The idolatrous-shameful-objects register (VCG-01 — Jer 3:24; 11:13; Hos 9:10) shows CHAR-4 operating in the person's relational capacity with God — the shameful object is what has replaced God in the person's devotional relation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is constitutively relational — it is the contempt-relation between persons, and its damage is in the relational field. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10) are specifically about protecting relational capacity within the community: do not despise your brother is a relational-capacity protection instruction. CHAR-5 impairs the relational capacity of the recipient by reducing their standing to zero in the contempt-er's relational field — and by extension, in the community's.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is specifically relational in its function: it is the inner moral condition that enables the relational approach to God (Psa 26:6 — "I wash my hands in innocence and go around your altar"). The relational capacity that CHAR-6 enables is specifically the person-to-God relational approach — worship, petition, covenant engagement. Its absence (Hos 8:5) blocks this relational capacity: the incapacity for innocence bars the approach to God that the covenant relationship requires.

---

---

##### T3.11.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In its ordinary wounded form, shame **impairs** relational capacity — withdrawal, face-covering, inability to speak at the gate. In its corrective form, shame is a *relational tool* — it is extended by one person toward another to restore right relationship (2Th 3:14; 1Pe 3:16). In the M07-C mode, shame before God is the precondition for restored relationship: Eze 43:10-11 — only when Israel is ashamed can the temple design (the design of right relationship with God) be disclosed. Shame before God, in the M07-C mode, is not the end of the relational capacity but the gateway to its restoration.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 severely impairs relational capacity. The shaved envoys cannot return to public social life; the silenced man cannot engage in dialogue; the defeated nations cannot sustain former relationships with neighbours (derision replaces respect). 1Cor 15:43's mortal body "sown in dishonor" is in a condition of diminished relational capacity; resurrection glory restores it. CHAR-2's relational dimension is fundamental: it is enacted through the relational field and its primary effect is the disruption of the person's relational standing and capacity.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is constitutively relational — it is the degradation of the relational-capacity in its worth-recognition mode. The judge who "neither fears God nor respects man" (Luk 18:2) has lost the relational-capacity component of appropriate regard for the worth of others. This is CHAR-3's most direct faculty engagement: it is the failure of the relational faculty's worth-recognition mode.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4's evaluative operation in VCG-01 engages the relational capacity through community norms (the social-moral judgments about hair, speech in assembly, financial conduct). The idolatrous-shameful-objects register (VCG-01 — Jer 3:24; 11:13; Hos 9:10) shows CHAR-4 operating in the person's relational capacity with God — the shameful object is what has replaced God in the person's devotional relation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is constitutively relational — it is the contempt-relation between persons, and its damage is in the relational field. The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10) are specifically about protecting relational capacity within the community: do not despise your brother is a relational-capacity protection instruction. CHAR-5 impairs the relational capacity of the recipient by reducing their standing to zero in the contempt-er's relational field — and by extension, in the community's.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is specifically relational in its function: it is the inner moral condition that enables the relational approach to God (Psa 26:6 — "I wash my hands in innocence and go around your altar"). The relational capacity that CHAR-6 enables is specifically the person-to-God relational approach — worship, petition, covenant engagement. Its absence (Hos 8:5) blocks this relational capacity: the incapacity for innocence bars the approach to God that the covenant relationship requires.

---

---

##### T3.11.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That CHAR-1's relational dimension is among its most theologically significant features. Shame is both the product of relational rupture (unjust wound from enemies, moral failure before God) and the gateway to relational restoration (corrective shame, penitential shame before God). The shame that closes the relationship (face turned away, mouth shut, presence withdrawn) is, when received as corrective, the opening through which relationship can be rebuilt. This makes shame a distinctively relational characteristic — it never operates in isolation from the person's relational field.

---

The shaved envoys cannot return to public social life; the silenced man cannot engage in dialogue; the defeated nations cannot sustain former relationships with neighbours (derision replaces respect). 1Cor 15:43's mortal body "sown in dishonor" is in a condition of diminished relational capacity; resurrection glory restores it. ---

## T4 — Interfaces

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, in a specific and distinctive way. God deploys shame as a judicial verdict and as a moral instrument directed at human persons. The M07-B evidence documents God "putting enemies to shame" (Psa 44:7; 53:5; 86:17; Zec 10:5), exposing idol-makers to shame (Isa 44:9-11; 45:16), and placing shame on those who opposed his servant (Isa 41:11; 42:17). This is God using shame as a tool of judgment — it moves from God toward the person as a consequence of their action against God or his people. More remarkably, God also deploys shame as a restorative instrument toward his own people: the commands in Eze 16:52; Eze 36:32; Eze 43:10 — "be ashamed and confounded for your ways, O house of Israel" — are divine invocations of shame directed at his covenant people as the gateway to renewal. God extends shame toward the human person both as judgment (on enemies) and as corrective mercy (on his own people).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Extensively evidenced in VCG-03. God extends CHAR-2 to the proud as a judicial act: "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" (2Sa 22:28); "the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power" (Isa 10:33); "I will change their glory into shame" (Hos 4:7). God also extends CHAR-2 redemptively through the mortal body's state (1Cor 15:43) — the dishonored mortal condition is God-ordained as the seed-state for the glorified body. The judicial basis is moral cause (pride, idolatry, opposition to God's servant); the redemptive basis is eschatological purpose.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

God extends CHAR-3 in the structural-assignment mode (VCG-02): the potter's sovereign assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) is God's prerogative in the creation and governance of persons. The basis is God's authority over his own creation; the content is the objective assignment of standing according to God's sovereign purpose.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

God is the standard against which CHAR-4's evaluative operation works ("in the sight of God," 2Cor 4:2). God's giving over of persons to dishonorable passions (Rom 1:24; 1:26) — "God gave them up" — shows God as the agent who permits the VCG-02 moral disorder as a consequence of idolatry. This is not God extending shamefulness but God releasing the person into the shamefulness their own choices have generated.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

God acts against CHAR-5 rather than extending it: 1Cor 1:28 — God choosing the despised to nullify things that are — is God's counter-movement against the world's contempt-verdicts. God's sovereign reversal of CHAR-5 is the theological foundation for why the recipient of contempt need not be defined by the contempt-verdict. God does not extend contempt-producing-shame toward persons; he extends the reversal of contempt and the vindication of the despised.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

God confirms and validates CHAR-6: Gen 20:6 (contextually) — God's response to Abimelech's appeal to innocence is to confirm it and grant protection. God is the authoritative validator of the innocence-claim: whether CHAR-6 is present is not merely a self-assessment but a reality confirmed or denied by God. God also reveals the incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) — the divine question "how long will they be incapable of innocence?" reveals that God tracks the moral condition of CHAR-6 and names its loss.

---

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The evidence reveals two distinct bases. To enemies and opponents, God extends shame as *responsive and conditional*: their hostility toward God's servant and people is what triggers the divine shaming. The shame is proportionate and retributive — their malice meets its reversal. To his own people, God extends shame as *covenantal and corrective*: the commands to "be ashamed" in Eze 36:32 ("it is not for your sake that I will act") are explicitly grounded in God's unilateral covenantal action *apart from* their deserving — the basis is grace rather than merit. The shame commanded before grace is not a precondition of merit but the appropriate inner posture of a person receiving what they have not earned.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Extensively evidenced in VCG-03. God extends CHAR-2 to the proud as a judicial act: "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" (2Sa 22:28); "the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power" (Isa 10:33); "I will change their glory into shame" (Hos 4:7). God also extends CHAR-2 redemptively through the mortal body's state (1Cor 15:43) — the dishonored mortal condition is God-ordained as the seed-state for the glorified body. The judicial basis is moral cause (pride, idolatry, opposition to God's servant); the redemptive basis is eschatological purpose.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

God extends CHAR-3 in the structural-assignment mode (VCG-02): the potter's sovereign assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) is God's prerogative in the creation and governance of persons. The basis is God's authority over his own creation; the content is the objective assignment of standing according to God's sovereign purpose.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

God is the standard against which CHAR-4's evaluative operation works ("in the sight of God," 2Cor 4:2). God's giving over of persons to dishonorable passions (Rom 1:24; 1:26) — "God gave them up" — shows God as the agent who permits the VCG-02 moral disorder as a consequence of idolatry. This is not God extending shamefulness but God releasing the person into the shamefulness their own choices have generated.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

God acts against CHAR-5 rather than extending it: 1Cor 1:28 — God choosing the despised to nullify things that are — is God's counter-movement against the world's contempt-verdicts. God's sovereign reversal of CHAR-5 is the theological foundation for why the recipient of contempt need not be defined by the contempt-verdict. God does not extend contempt-producing-shame toward persons; he extends the reversal of contempt and the vindication of the despised.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

God confirms and validates CHAR-6: Gen 20:6 (contextually) — God's response to Abimelech's appeal to innocence is to confirm it and grant protection. God is the authoritative validator of the innocence-claim: whether CHAR-6 is present is not merely a self-assessment but a reality confirmed or denied by God. God also reveals the incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) — the divine question "how long will they be incapable of innocence?" reveals that God tracks the moral condition of CHAR-6 and names its loss.

---

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

God's extension of shame as judgment reveals his holiness and justice — he takes moral reality seriously enough to expose and reverse what opposes it. God's extension of shame as corrective mercy toward his own people reveals his pastoral investment in their inner moral integrity — he does not want them to receive his grace without moral self-awareness, because the grace that bypasses shame-recognition is grace that cannot transform. The command "be ashamed" before "I will act for you" (Eze 36:32) reveals a God who is committed to the whole person's inner life, not merely their external circumstances. This disposition is consistent throughout M07-C: God arranges encounters (the temple design, Eze 43:10) specifically to produce shame in the inner person because shame before holiness is what opens the person to receive what God offers.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Extensively evidenced in VCG-03. God extends CHAR-2 to the proud as a judicial act: "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" (2Sa 22:28); "the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power" (Isa 10:33); "I will change their glory into shame" (Hos 4:7). God also extends CHAR-2 redemptively through the mortal body's state (1Cor 15:43) — the dishonored mortal condition is God-ordained as the seed-state for the glorified body. The judicial basis is moral cause (pride, idolatry, opposition to God's servant); the redemptive basis is eschatological purpose.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

God extends CHAR-3 in the structural-assignment mode (VCG-02): the potter's sovereign assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) is God's prerogative in the creation and governance of persons. The basis is God's authority over his own creation; the content is the objective assignment of standing according to God's sovereign purpose.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

God is the standard against which CHAR-4's evaluative operation works ("in the sight of God," 2Cor 4:2). God's giving over of persons to dishonorable passions (Rom 1:24; 1:26) — "God gave them up" — shows God as the agent who permits the VCG-02 moral disorder as a consequence of idolatry. This is not God extending shamefulness but God releasing the person into the shamefulness their own choices have generated.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

God acts against CHAR-5 rather than extending it: 1Cor 1:28 — God choosing the despised to nullify things that are — is God's counter-movement against the world's contempt-verdicts. God's sovereign reversal of CHAR-5 is the theological foundation for why the recipient of contempt need not be defined by the contempt-verdict. God does not extend contempt-producing-shame toward persons; he extends the reversal of contempt and the vindication of the despised.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

God confirms and validates CHAR-6: Gen 20:6 (contextually) — God's response to Abimelech's appeal to innocence is to confirm it and grant protection. God is the authoritative validator of the innocence-claim: whether CHAR-6 is present is not merely a self-assessment but a reality confirmed or denied by God. God also reveals the incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) — the divine question "how long will they be incapable of innocence?" reveals that God tracks the moral condition of CHAR-6 and names its loss.

---

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; God-to-human operation is extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Extensively evidenced in VCG-03. God extends CHAR-2 to the proud as a judicial act: "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" (2Sa 22:28); "the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power" (Isa 10:33); "I will change their glory into shame" (Hos 4:7). God also extends CHAR-2 redemptively through the mortal body's state (1Cor 15:43) — the dishonored mortal condition is God-ordained as the seed-state for the glorified body. The judicial basis is moral cause (pride, idolatry, opposition to God's servant); the redemptive basis is eschatological purpose.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

God extends CHAR-3 in the structural-assignment mode (VCG-02): the potter's sovereign assignment of vessels for dishonorable use (Rom 9:21) is God's prerogative in the creation and governance of persons. The basis is God's authority over his own creation; the content is the objective assignment of standing according to God's sovereign purpose.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

God is the standard against which CHAR-4's evaluative operation works ("in the sight of God," 2Cor 4:2). God's giving over of persons to dishonorable passions (Rom 1:24; 1:26) — "God gave them up" — shows God as the agent who permits the VCG-02 moral disorder as a consequence of idolatry. This is not God extending shamefulness but God releasing the person into the shamefulness their own choices have generated.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

God acts against CHAR-5 rather than extending it: 1Cor 1:28 — God choosing the despised to nullify things that are — is God's counter-movement against the world's contempt-verdicts. God's sovereign reversal of CHAR-5 is the theological foundation for why the recipient of contempt need not be defined by the contempt-verdict. God does not extend contempt-producing-shame toward persons; he extends the reversal of contempt and the vindication of the despised.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

God confirms and validates CHAR-6: Gen 20:6 (contextually) — God's response to Abimelech's appeal to innocence is to confirm it and grant protection. God is the authoritative validator of the innocence-claim: whether CHAR-6 is present is not merely a self-assessment but a reality confirmed or denied by God. God also reveals the incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) — the divine question "how long will they be incapable of innocence?" reveals that God tracks the moral condition of CHAR-6 and names its loss.

---

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, and the M07-C corpus (M07-C-VCG-01 and -03) is the primary evidence. The person in the M07-C mode moves toward God *through* shame: the penitential posture of lying down in shame (Jer 3:25, vc=37308/37470), the inability to lift the face to God that nonetheless constitutes a kind of prayer (Ezr 9:6), the conscience-driven shame that moves toward renewed service (2Ch 30:15). The M07-C-VCG-02 material shows the complementary movement: the person's movement toward God through trust simultaneously protects from shame — these are the two faces of the human-toward-God movement in shame's register (moving toward God through shame's guilt; moving toward God through trust and word). Both are movements toward God; they differ in what drives them (guilt-shame vs. confident trust).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Limited evidence. Eze 44:13 — Levites bearing shame as a restriction on their approach to God — shows CHAR-2 governing human-to-God access in the priestly context. CHAR-2 does not primarily operate as a human movement toward God; it is imposed on humans from God or from other humans.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Extensively evidenced in VCG-01. Joh 8:49 — "you dishonor me" (Jesus = God incarnate); Rom 2:23 — "you dishonor God by breaking the law"; Heb 6:6 — apostates "hold him up to contempt." The human-to-God direction of CHAR-3 is the active worth-denial of God's incarnate person and his moral authority. The inner posture required to avoid CHAR-3 toward God is described in its absence in Luk 18:2 — fearing God is the inner posture that prevents CHAR-3 toward God.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The idolatrous-shameful-objects register (VCG-01 — Jer 3:24; 11:13; Hos 9:10) is precisely about what the human conscience should assess as shameful in relation to God: the idol is "the shameful thing" (bo.shet — Jer 3:24) that has replaced God in the person's movement toward him. CHAR-4's proper functioning toward God means assessing idolatrous objects as shameful and recoiling from them toward God.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Human-to-God CHAR-5 is evidenced in the mockery of Jesus (Luk 23:11 — Herod and his soldiers treating Jesus with contempt and mockery). The acts directed at Jesus in his passion are CHAR-5 in its most concentrated form: the world's contempt-verdict on God incarnate. Act 4:11 (the builders rejecting the cornerstone) shows the human rejection of God's sent-one as CHAR-5 directed toward God through the mediating agency of Jesus. The inner posture that prevents CHAR-5 toward God is the recognition of divine worth — receiving the despised as "an angel of God, as Christ Jesus" (Gal 4:14).

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The primary human-to-God direction of CHAR-6 is worship and approach: Psa 26:6 — "I wash my hands in innocence and go around your altar, O Lord" — is the movement of the innocent person toward God in the cultic act of going around the altar. CHAR-6 is what enables this movement. The inner posture required is moral cleanness — the person who approaches God must have their inner moral condition aligned with the holiness they approach.

---

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The inner posture required for the shame-mediated movement toward God is *moral honesty* — willingness to let shame be what it is, to "lie down in our shame" (Jer 3:25) without defensiveness or hardening. The M07-B seared-conscience material shows what happens when this posture is refused: no movement toward God is possible because the inner faculty that registers failure (conscience) is dead. The M07-C gateway passages show that where this posture is maintained, shame becomes the specific inner preparation for receiving God's self-disclosure (Eze 43:10-11).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Limited evidence. Eze 44:13 — Levites bearing shame as a restriction on their approach to God — shows CHAR-2 governing human-to-God access in the priestly context. CHAR-2 does not primarily operate as a human movement toward God; it is imposed on humans from God or from other humans.

---

The inner posture required to avoid CHAR-3 toward God is described in its absence in Luk 18:2 — fearing God is the inner posture that prevents CHAR-3 toward God.

---

---

CHAR-6 is what enables this movement. The inner posture required is moral cleanness — the person who approaches God must have their inner moral condition aligned with the holiness they approach.

---

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

That shame before God is not the destruction of the relationship but its specific form of honesty. The relationship between the person and God can bear shame — it can receive the one who comes with the face not lifted, who lies down in shame, who groans and turns away. The Psalm evidence (Psa 25:2 — "in you I trust; let me not be put to shame; let not my enemies exult") shows the psalmist bringing shame-threat to God as a relational appeal. God is the one before whom shame is felt and to whom shame is brought for resolution. The human-to-God direction reveals a relationship in which honest inner moral experience is the appropriate content of the movement toward God.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Limited evidence. Eze 44:13 — Levites bearing shame as a restriction on their approach to God — shows CHAR-2 governing human-to-God access in the priestly context. CHAR-2 does not primarily operate as a human movement toward God; it is imposed on humans from God or from other humans.

---

---

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; human-to-God operation is extensively evidenced in M07-C.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)
