---

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, in two distinct ways. (1) **Unjust infliction** — enemies, adversaries, those who love falsehood actively working to cover another person's face with shame (Psa 4:2; 69:7; 44:15 — M07-A-VCG-01). This is shame as a weapon directed against the innocent. (2) **Corrective deployment** — Paul directing shame at the Corinthians (1Cor 6:5; 15:34), community isolation producing corrective shame in the disobedient (2Th 3:14), blameless conduct putting accusers to shame (Tit 2:8; 1Pe 3:16). The M07-B-VCG-05 material is the extensive evidence base for legitimate corrective deployment of shame person-to-person.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01 involves humans extending CHAR-2 to other humans: Ammonites shaving David's envoys, tenants beating servants. In the unjust register, CHAR-2 is inflicted by malicious agents. In the corrective register, legitimate authority can impose CHAR-2 as a judicial act. The giving direction is morally ambiguous — it can be unjust infliction or just correction.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 is primarily about humans extending dishonour toward other humans or toward God. The unjust judge (Luk 18:2/4) extends worth-denial to the widow. The rich receive honor while the poor man is dishonored (Jam 2:6). The head-covering symbolic acts extend disrespect toward divinely ordered authority structures.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 can be extended interpersonally through the articulation of moral evaluations: Paul's renunciation of shameful ways (2Cor 4:2) is both his own functioning CHAR-4 and an implicit invitation to the community's conscience to recognise the same standard. 1Cor 14:35's articulated moral-evaluative judgment extends a community's shared CHAR-4 evaluation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er extends CHAR-5 toward others through VCG-01's dismissive attitude, VCG-02's violent rejection, and VCG-03's verbal contempt. In every mode, the extending person must have a prior inner disposition of self-elevation or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9) to sustain the contemptuous dismissal of others. The person who gives CHAR-5 is one who has placed themselves above the person they despise — they must have an inflated inner self-assessment as the precondition for the contempt-extension.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse corpus does not evidence CHAR-6 being extended by one person toward another in a direct relational-giving sense. CHAR-6 is an inner moral condition of the individual, not primarily a characteristic extended toward others. Silent on the giving direction as a direct relational-extension.

---

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The corrective deployment evidence (Paul's letters; the community-discipline passages) shows that the giver of corrective shame must be acting from a position of genuine moral concern rather than hostility. Paul's distinction in 1Cor 4:14 (vc=34992) — "I do not write these things to *make you ashamed*, but to *admonish you as my beloved children*" — shows the fine line between legitimate corrective shame (motivated by affection and moral concern) and destructive shame-induction (motivated by hostility or self-elevation). The corrective giver must have their own standing grounded in what they appeal to — blameless conduct as the basis for causing opponents' shame (Tit 2:8; 1Pe 3:16).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01 involves humans extending CHAR-2 to other humans: Ammonites shaving David's envoys, tenants beating servants. In the unjust register, CHAR-2 is inflicted by malicious agents. In the corrective register, legitimate authority can impose CHAR-2 as a judicial act. The giving direction is morally ambiguous — it can be unjust infliction or just correction.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 is primarily about humans extending dishonour toward other humans or toward God. The unjust judge (Luk 18:2/4) extends worth-denial to the widow. The rich receive honor while the poor man is dishonored (Jam 2:6). The head-covering symbolic acts extend disrespect toward divinely ordered authority structures.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 can be extended interpersonally through the articulation of moral evaluations: Paul's renunciation of shameful ways (2Cor 4:2) is both his own functioning CHAR-4 and an implicit invitation to the community's conscience to recognise the same standard. 1Cor 14:35's articulated moral-evaluative judgment extends a community's shared CHAR-4 evaluation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er extends CHAR-5 toward others through VCG-01's dismissive attitude, VCG-02's violent rejection, and VCG-03's verbal contempt. In every mode, the extending person must have a prior inner disposition of self-elevation or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9) to sustain the contemptuous dismissal of others. The person who gives CHAR-5 is one who has placed themselves above the person they despise — they must have an inflated inner self-assessment as the precondition for the contempt-extension.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse corpus does not evidence CHAR-6 being extended by one person toward another in a direct relational-giving sense. CHAR-6 is an inner moral condition of the individual, not primarily a characteristic extended toward others. Silent on the giving direction as a direct relational-extension.

---

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The evidence from the corrective-shame passages implies that the person who can legitimately invoke shame in another must themselves have received the corrective-shame signal and responded to it. Paul's own apostolic authority (2Cor 10:8) is the basis for his freedom from shame — his authority is genuinely from God. The person who invokes corrective shame without having themselves experienced and received shame's corrective function is working from a position of moral inconsistency that undermines the legitimacy of the invitation.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01 involves humans extending CHAR-2 to other humans: Ammonites shaving David's envoys, tenants beating servants. In the unjust register, CHAR-2 is inflicted by malicious agents. In the corrective register, legitimate authority can impose CHAR-2 as a judicial act. The giving direction is morally ambiguous — it can be unjust infliction or just correction.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

VCG-01 is primarily about humans extending dishonour toward other humans or toward God. The unjust judge (Luk 18:2/4) extends worth-denial to the widow. The rich receive honor while the poor man is dishonored (Jam 2:6). The head-covering symbolic acts extend disrespect toward divinely ordered authority structures.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 can be extended interpersonally through the articulation of moral evaluations: Paul's renunciation of shameful ways (2Cor 4:2) is both his own functioning CHAR-4 and an implicit invitation to the community's conscience to recognise the same standard. 1Cor 14:35's articulated moral-evaluative judgment extends a community's shared CHAR-4 evaluation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The contempt-er extends CHAR-5 toward others through VCG-01's dismissive attitude, VCG-02's violent rejection, and VCG-03's verbal contempt. In every mode, the extending person must have a prior inner disposition of self-elevation or self-righteousness (Luk 18:9) to sustain the contemptuous dismissal of others. The person who gives CHAR-5 is one who has placed themselves above the person they despise — they must have an inflated inner self-assessment as the precondition for the contempt-extension.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse corpus does not evidence CHAR-6 being extended by one person toward another in a direct relational-giving sense. CHAR-6 is an inner moral condition of the individual, not primarily a characteristic extended toward others. Silent on the giving direction as a direct relational-extension.

---

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; the giving direction is evidenced in the corrective-shame passages.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01 involves humans extending CHAR-2 to other humans: Ammonites shaving David's envoys, tenants beating servants. In the unjust register, CHAR-2 is inflicted by malicious agents. ---

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, extensively in M07-A. The unjust-wound register (M07-A-VCG-01, -02) is almost entirely about shame received — the psalmist whose honour is exchanged for shame by enemies' deceit (Psa 4:2), Israel whose shame comes from surrounding nations (Eze 34:29; 36:6; 36:15), the mother whose shame comes from bereavement (Jer 15:9), the servants who receive shame through drought and helplessness (Jer 14:3-4). Received shame is the primary operational mode in the unjust-wound register. The corrective-shame register (M07-B-VCG-05; M07-C-VCG-03) also operates as received — the community receiving Paul's shame-direction (1Cor 6:5), Israel receiving the shame of the temple's design (Eze 43:10).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables receiving CHAR-2 to be transformative (corrective) rather than merely destructive is the person's willingness to recognise their proper standing. The envoys accept the king's compassion and wait for restoration (2Sa 10:5). What blocks transformation is the hardened pride that cannot integrate the corrective signal.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Paul receives dishonour (2Cor 6:8, vc=34963) without altering inner integrity — the key condition for receiving structural dishonour without inner displacement is the grounded knowledge of one's own standing before God. The poor man receives dishonour (Jam 2:6) — the evidence does not describe his inner response but implies that his worth before God is real regardless of the community's misassignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The corpus does not extensively describe a person receiving CHAR-4 from another — CHAR-4 is primarily produced within the individual conscience through its own evaluative operation. Silent on extensive evidence for the receiving direction.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables the person to receive CHAR-5 without being defined by it is grounded confidence in God's worth-assignment. The Galatians' non-contemptuous reception of Paul (Gal 4:14) — "received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus" — shows the alternative to CHAR-5's worth-cancellation: seeing through the physical weakness to the divine messenger behind it. The one who cannot receive CHAR-5 without being damaged is the one whose self-worth is entirely dependent on others' contempt-or-approval judgments.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 is not typically received from another person — it is maintained within the person through their own moral choices. The only receiving context is the divine confirmation (God confirming Abimelech's innocence, Gen 20:6) — but this is God validating CHAR-6 rather than God extending CHAR-6 to the person. Silent on receiving direction as an interpersonal dynamic.

---

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

For corrective received shame: an operative conscience enables reception (2Ch 30:15 — the priests receive the shame signal and act); moral hardening blocks it (Jer 3:3; 6:15 — the brazen forehead refuses shame). For unjust received shame: the question is not whether it is received (it is received regardless of the person's inner state) but how it is received — whether it overwhelms (Psa 44:15 — "all day long my disgrace is before me") or is absorbed with inner resilience (Pro 12:16 — the prudent ignores an insult) or is voluntarily borne (Heb 12:2; Act 5:41).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables receiving CHAR-2 to be transformative (corrective) rather than merely destructive is the person's willingness to recognise their proper standing. The envoys accept the king's compassion and wait for restoration (2Sa 10:5). What blocks transformation is the hardened pride that cannot integrate the corrective signal.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Paul receives dishonour (2Cor 6:8, vc=34963) without altering inner integrity — the key condition for receiving structural dishonour without inner displacement is the grounded knowledge of one's own standing before God. The poor man receives dishonour (Jam 2:6) — the evidence does not describe his inner response but implies that his worth before God is real regardless of the community's misassignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The corpus does not extensively describe a person receiving CHAR-4 from another — CHAR-4 is primarily produced within the individual conscience through its own evaluative operation. Silent on extensive evidence for the receiving direction.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables the person to receive CHAR-5 without being defined by it is grounded confidence in God's worth-assignment. The Galatians' non-contemptuous reception of Paul (Gal 4:14) — "received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus" — shows the alternative to CHAR-5's worth-cancellation: seeing through the physical weakness to the divine messenger behind it. The one who cannot receive CHAR-5 without being damaged is the one whose self-worth is entirely dependent on others' contempt-or-approval judgments.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 is not typically received from another person — it is maintained within the person through their own moral choices. The only receiving context is the divine confirmation (God confirming Abimelech's innocence, Gen 20:6) — but this is God validating CHAR-6 rather than God extending CHAR-6 to the person. Silent on receiving direction as an interpersonal dynamic.

---

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

In the corrective mode: the person who refuses corrective shame from another is in a state of moral hardening — conscience closed, inner faculty sealed against the signal. The M07-B-VCG-04 material (Jer 3:3; 6:15; 8:12; Mic 2:6) documents this state: brazen, desensitised, dismissive of the possibility that disgrace could overtake them. In the unjust-wound mode: the person who successfully does not receive unjust shame is not hardened but strong — the prudent who "ignores an insult" (Pro 12:16), the servant who sets his face like flint (Isa 50:7). The inner state is grounded confidence rather than armoured hardening.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables receiving CHAR-2 to be transformative (corrective) rather than merely destructive is the person's willingness to recognise their proper standing. The envoys accept the king's compassion and wait for restoration (2Sa 10:5). What blocks transformation is the hardened pride that cannot integrate the corrective signal.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Paul receives dishonour (2Cor 6:8, vc=34963) without altering inner integrity — the key condition for receiving structural dishonour without inner displacement is the grounded knowledge of one's own standing before God. The poor man receives dishonour (Jam 2:6) — the evidence does not describe his inner response but implies that his worth before God is real regardless of the community's misassignment.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The corpus does not extensively describe a person receiving CHAR-4 from another — CHAR-4 is primarily produced within the individual conscience through its own evaluative operation. Silent on extensive evidence for the receiving direction.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily a received characteristic. What enables the person to receive CHAR-5 without being defined by it is grounded confidence in God's worth-assignment. The Galatians' non-contemptuous reception of Paul (Gal 4:14) — "received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus" — shows the alternative to CHAR-5's worth-cancellation: seeing through the physical weakness to the divine messenger behind it. The one who cannot receive CHAR-5 without being damaged is the one whose self-worth is entirely dependent on others' contempt-or-approval judgments.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

CHAR-6 is not typically received from another person — it is maintained within the person through their own moral choices. The only receiving context is the divine confirmation (God confirming Abimelech's innocence, Gen 20:6) — but this is God validating CHAR-6 rather than God extending CHAR-6 to the person. Silent on receiving direction as an interpersonal dynamic.

---

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; received shame is extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is primarily a received characteristic. ---

---

#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. Within existing covenantal bonds (Israel-God relationship in M07-C; Paul-Corinthians in M07-B-VCG-05; family relationships in M07-B-VCG-03), shame functions as a relational signal — it can be received, corrected, and lead to restored relationship because the bond exists and can bear the weight. Across relational distance (enemies in M07-A, opponents in M07-B-VCG-01), shame is a judicial/moral verdict rather than a relational instrument — it is the exposure and collapse of standing before one who stands against the person, not a call to relational restoration. The community discipline passage (2Th 3:14) is notable: isolation from the disobedient person is prescribed precisely to signal the relational rupture as a precondition for shame-producing awareness. Relationship is the context within which corrective shame can work.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates both within existing bonds (David's king offering compassion to humiliated envoys) and across bonds (military opponents humiliating nations, God humbling the proud). The divine-abasement mode (VCG-03) is universal — God's corrective humiliation of pride crosses all covenantal boundaries. CHAR-2's scope is not covenantally limited.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The head-covering material (1Cor 11:4-5) operates within the covenant community. Jam 2:6's dishonoring of the poor operates within the community of believers. The dishonoring of Jesus (Joh 8:49) crosses the covenant community's internal boundary. CHAR-3 appears to operate most damagingly within existing relational bonds where worth-recognition is expected and violated.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 operates within community contexts (VCG-01: the shameful conduct of speech in the assembly, the shameful hair practices — all community-embedded evaluations) and within covenantal contexts (the idolatrous shameful-objects of Jer 3:24; 11:13 are specifically about Israel's covenantal infidelity). VCG-02 (disordered passions) crosses community boundaries — Rom 1:26-27 addresses a pattern of moral disorder that is cultural-historical in scope.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The commands against despising (Rom 14:3; 14:10; 1Cor 16:11; 1Th 5:20) operate within the covenant community. The Boaz-Ruth protection (Rut 2:15, vc=38516) operates across covenantal difference: Boaz protects Ruth, an outsider, from the contempt she would normally receive. The 1Sa 25:7/15 (vc=38530/38531) protection of Nabal's shepherds operates within a social context of armed men restraining themselves. CHAR-5's scope is not covenantally limited — contempt can cross any relational boundary; what is covenantally specific is the community's obligation to protect against contempt within its own relational field.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 operates specifically within the covenant relationship between the person and God: the approach to God's altar (Psa 26:6) is a covenantal act; the divine confirmation of innocence (Gen 20:6) is a covenantal response; the incapacity for innocence (Hos 8:5) is a covenantal failure condition. CHAR-6's scope is specifically covenantal-relational: it is the inner moral condition that the covenant relationship with God requires of the person.

---

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 crosses covenantal boundaries. The psalmist's enemies experience shame; Edom is covered with shame (Obd 10); Babylon's gods are put to shame (Jer 50:2) — these are not covenantal contexts. God's judicial deployment of shame against opponents crosses covenantal boundaries freely. What is covenantally specific is the *corrective and restorative* mode of shame: the commands to "be ashamed" in Eze 16:52; 36:32; 43:10 are directed at God's covenant people specifically, not universally. Corrective shame as gateway to renewed relationship appears to operate within the covenantal context, while judicial shame as consequence operates universally.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates both within existing bonds (David's king offering compassion to humiliated envoys) and across bonds (military opponents humiliating nations, God humbling the proud). The divine-abasement mode (VCG-03) is universal — God's corrective humiliation of pride crosses all covenantal boundaries. CHAR-2's scope is not covenantally limited.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The head-covering material (1Cor 11:4-5) operates within the covenant community. Jam 2:6's dishonoring of the poor operates within the community of believers. The dishonoring of Jesus (Joh 8:49) crosses the covenant community's internal boundary. CHAR-3 appears to operate most damagingly within existing relational bonds where worth-recognition is expected and violated.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 operates within community contexts (VCG-01: the shameful conduct of speech in the assembly, the shameful hair practices — all community-embedded evaluations) and within covenantal contexts (the idolatrous shameful-objects of Jer 3:24; 11:13 are specifically about Israel's covenantal infidelity). VCG-02 (disordered passions) crosses community boundaries — Rom 1:26-27 addresses a pattern of moral disorder that is cultural-historical in scope.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The Boaz-Ruth protection (Rut 2:15, vc=38516) operates across covenantal difference: Boaz protects Ruth, an outsider, from the contempt she would normally receive. ---

CHAR-6's scope is specifically covenantal-relational: it is the inner moral condition that the covenant relationship with God requires of the person.

---

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1's scope is universal in its judicial form (any moral agent can be put to shame by God's judgment); covenantally specific in its corrective-restorative form (shame as the gateway to knowing God's design is offered to those in covenantal relationship with him); and interpersonally broad in its unjust-wound form (anyone can inflict unjust shame on anyone else, as the psalmist's enemy-evidence shows).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates both within existing bonds (David's king offering compassion to humiliated envoys) and across bonds (military opponents humiliating nations, God humbling the proud). The divine-abasement mode (VCG-03) is universal — God's corrective humiliation of pride crosses all covenantal boundaries. CHAR-2's scope is not covenantally limited.

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

The 224-verse CHAR-1 corpus does not directly evidence shame operating in the person's relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The evidence is centred on the human-God and human-human axes.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Limited but present. Mar 1:25 (vc=30400) — Jesus silencing the demon — is CHAR-2 applied to an adversarial spiritual being: the demon's voice and presence are forcibly suppressed. Mar 4:39 (vc=30401) — the storm muzzled — applies the same authority to natural forces. These confirm the enforced-abasement mechanism applies beyond human persons when divine authority acts against them.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (S)

The 15-verse CHAR-3 corpus does not evidence worth-denial operating in relation to spiritual beings. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not evidence shamefulness-as-moral-evaluation operating in relation to spiritual beings. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (S)

The 24-verse CHAR-5 corpus does not directly evidence contempt-produced shame operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings in an explicit way. The world's contempt structures may be demonically energised (the parable of the tenants who reject the son could carry this dimension), but the text does not name this explicitly. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (S)

The 8-verse CHAR-6 corpus does not evidence innocence-as-counter-to-shame operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. Silent.

---

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (S)

Not directly evidenced in the CHAR-1 corpus. The M07-A unjust-wound material shows human enemies inflicting shame, but does not explicitly identify adversarial spiritual beings as the agents. The "enemies" of the Psalms could carry this dimension, but the text itself does not name it.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Limited but present. Mar 1:25 (vc=30400) — Jesus silencing the demon — is CHAR-2 applied to an adversarial spiritual being: the demon's voice and presence are forcibly suppressed. These confirm the enforced-abasement mechanism applies beyond human persons when divine authority acts against them.

The 16-verse CHAR-4 corpus does not evidence shamefulness-as-moral-evaluation operating in relation to spiritual beings. Silent.

---

Not evidenced in the corpus.

## T5 — Transformation

---

### T5

#### T5.1 — Nature of Transformation

##### T5.1.1 — Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation to their condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, in both directions. In the corrective mode (M07-B-VCG-05; M07-C-VCG-01 and -03), shame produces transformation of the person's orientation — from wrong-facing to right-facing, from self-defensive to penitent, from morally asleep to morally awake. 2Ch 30:15: shame → immediate consecration (condition transformed). Eze 43:10-11: shame → openness to receive God's design (orientation transformed). In the hardening mode (M07-B-VCG-04), shame's absence marks a transformation in reverse — the progressive desensitisation of the conscience. In the unjust-wound mode, shame damages the person's sense of standing and dignity — a transformation of condition.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, in two trajectories. (1) Corrective transformation: where the humiliated person receives the corrective signal, CHAR-2 produces reorientation of inner standing toward proper proportion. (2) Eschatological transformation: 1Cor 15:43 — the body sown in dishonor is raised in glory — the mortal state of humiliation is explicitly transitional rather than final. David's envoys' humiliation is reversible (2Sa 10:5). VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32; Jer 23:40 — perpetual shame) shows humiliation as permanent in judgment contexts. Reversibility depends on whether divine redemption addresses the humiliation.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 in its active mode produces moral self-contradiction in the dishonorer (Rom 2:23). Heb 6:6 shows apostatic dishonour of Christ as irreversibly damaging — "it is impossible to restore them again to repentance." In the structural mode (VCG-02), 2Ti 2:20 implies that the condition of dishonorable-vessel is tied to moral condition, implying reversibility through moral transformation (cleansing, 2Ti 2:21 context).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 produces moral discipline — the renunciation of the shameful and the embrace of transparent, truth-grounded conduct (2Cor 4:2). Inverted CHAR-4 (VCG-03) produces moral deepening of the inversion: "their end is destruction" (Phili 3:19). Rev 16:15's call to vigilance frames CHAR-4's proper functioning as a sustained transformation project oriented toward Christ's coming. Reversibility: the functioning conscience can be restored; the inverted conscience's trajectory ("their end is destruction") is presented as non-reversible in its current direction.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 produces transformation in two directions. (1) Destructive: sustained contempt deposits shame-identity (Bartimaeus's beggar-identity, Mar 10:50). (2) Redemptive: Jesus's reversal of contempt-verdicts (Act 4:11; 1Cor 1:28) transforms the despised into the chosen, overturning the contempt-system's accumulated verdict. The transformation is reversible in both directions: shame-identity can be abandoned (Mar 10:50 — throwing off the cloak); divine reversal can re-assign worth permanently.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 produces the transformation of relational access: from the barrier of guilt-shame to the openness of approach to God. The person with clean hands and a blameless heart (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) moves toward God without the inner collapse that guilt-shame would produce. Conversely, the loss of innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) produces the inverse transformation: from potential access to blocked access. Reversibility: maintained innocence (VCG-01) can be sustained through ongoing moral choices; lost innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) requires divine intervention for restoration — it is not self-reversible once the capacity has been so deeply damaged.

---

---

##### T5.1.2 — Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Both conditions are evidenced. The shame of the unjust wound is explicitly declared *reversible* by divine act: Isa 54:4 — "you will forget the shame of your youth"; Isa 61:7 — "instead of your shame there shall be a double portion." The shame of the seared conscience is not declared reversible within the evidence — the passages (Jer 6:15; 8:12) record it as a state of judgment with no restoration promised in context. The transformation shame produces in the corrective mode (2Ch 30:15; Eze 43:10-11) appears stable rather than temporary. The evidence thus shows: unjust shame is reversible by divine promise; appropriate guilt-shame is resolvable through atonement (Eze 16:63); seared-conscience shamelessness is presented as catastrophic and its reversal is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, in two trajectories. (1) Corrective transformation: where the humiliated person receives the corrective signal, CHAR-2 produces reorientation of inner standing toward proper proportion. (2) Eschatological transformation: 1Cor 15:43 — the body sown in dishonor is raised in glory — the mortal state of humiliation is explicitly transitional rather than final. David's envoys' humiliation is reversible (2Sa 10:5). VCG-04 evidence (Eze 32; Jer 23:40 — perpetual shame) shows humiliation as permanent in judgment contexts. Reversibility depends on whether divine redemption addresses the humiliation.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 in its active mode produces moral self-contradiction in the dishonorer (Rom 2:23). Heb 6:6 shows apostatic dishonour of Christ as irreversibly damaging — "it is impossible to restore them again to repentance." In the structural mode (VCG-02), 2Ti 2:20 implies that the condition of dishonorable-vessel is tied to moral condition, implying reversibility through moral transformation (cleansing, 2Ti 2:21 context).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 produces moral discipline — the renunciation of the shameful and the embrace of transparent, truth-grounded conduct (2Cor 4:2). Inverted CHAR-4 (VCG-03) produces moral deepening of the inversion: "their end is destruction" (Phili 3:19). Rev 16:15's call to vigilance frames CHAR-4's proper functioning as a sustained transformation project oriented toward Christ's coming. Reversibility: the functioning conscience can be restored; the inverted conscience's trajectory ("their end is destruction") is presented as non-reversible in its current direction.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 produces transformation in two directions. (1) Destructive: sustained contempt deposits shame-identity (Bartimaeus's beggar-identity, Mar 10:50). (2) Redemptive: Jesus's reversal of contempt-verdicts (Act 4:11; 1Cor 1:28) transforms the despised into the chosen, overturning the contempt-system's accumulated verdict. The transformation is reversible in both directions: shame-identity can be abandoned (Mar 10:50 — throwing off the cloak); divine reversal can re-assign worth permanently.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 produces the transformation of relational access: from the barrier of guilt-shame to the openness of approach to God. The person with clean hands and a blameless heart (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) moves toward God without the inner collapse that guilt-shame would produce. Conversely, the loss of innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) produces the inverse transformation: from potential access to blocked access. Reversibility: maintained innocence (VCG-01) can be sustained through ongoing moral choices; lost innocence-capacity (Hos 8:5) requires divine intervention for restoration — it is not self-reversible once the capacity has been so deeply damaged.

---

---

##### T5.1.3 — If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; transformation is extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, in two trajectories. (1) Corrective transformation: where the humiliated person receives the corrective signal, CHAR-2 produces reorientation of inner standing toward proper proportion. (2) Eschatological transformation: 1Cor 15:43 — the body sown in dishonor is raised in glory — the mortal state of humiliation is explicitly transitional rather than final. ---

---

---

#### T5.2 — Sequence of Inner States

##### T5.2.1 — Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The M07-C evidence is richest for sequence description. The guilt-shame sequence (M07-C-VCG-01): *awareness of sin → inner collapse before God's holiness → shame-posture (face not lifted, blushing) → corrective action or penitential stillness → (gateway opens to) renewed relationship with God*. Jer 31:19 evidences this: "after I had turned away, I relented; after I was instructed, I struck my thigh; I was ashamed, and I was confounded, because I bore the disgrace of my youth" — the sequence of turning → instruction → bodily expression of shame → confounded recognition. The M07-A unjust-wound sequence: *enemy aggression → received inner wound → face-covering → petition to God for vindication → (eventually) shame-removal and restoration*.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01: outer enforcing act -> inner collapse of standing -> withdrawal from public space -> eventual recovery when external sign removed. VCG-02: military defeat -> national identity stripped -> wailing and flight -> derision by neighbours. VCG-03 corrective: proud inner orientation -> divine judicial act -> inner deflation of pride -> ideally reorientation toward proper standing.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

For the dishonorer: defective inner worth-assessment -> willful act of worth-denial -> inner self-contradiction or moral hardening. For the dishonoured (in VCG-02 structural mode): sovereign or natural assignment of diminished standing -> received condition of dishonour -> sustained lived in that condition or transformation through moral change.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 sequence: conscience engages with conduct or desire -> applies God's standard -> recognises shamefulness -> produces recoil/renunciation -> principled conduct follows. Inverted CHAR-4 sequence: earthly standard applied -> shameful re-evaluated as honourable -> will orientated toward what disgraces -> deepening moral corruption.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Primary sequence: contempt directed at person -> inner wound of worth-cancellation -> formed shame-identity (if sustained) -> potential reversal through divine re-worth-assignment. The Bartimaeus narrative is the complete sequence: years of contempt -> beggar-identity formed -> Jesus calls -> immediate volitional abandonment of shame-identity -> restoration.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

VCG-01 sequence: moral integrity maintained through choices -> innocence present in heart and hands -> approach to God enabled without guilt-shame barrier. VCG-02 (Psa 73:13) sequence: innocence maintained but apparently failing to protect -> faith crisis about innocence's value -> (resolution in the wider psalm context: sanctuary encounter vindication). VCG-02 (Hos 8:5) sequence: sustained idolatry -> progressive loss of innocence-capacity -> incapacity for approach to God -> divine question naming the loss.

---

---

##### T5.2.2 — What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The corrective sequence (M07-C) reveals that shame is not the end-state but a *transition state* — it exists to produce the gateway opening, not to be the final condition. The unjust-wound sequence (M07-A) reveals that unresolved shame is a sustained inner burden that requires divine intervention for resolution — it does not self-resolve. The moral-consequence sequence (M07-B-VCG-03) is the simplest: moral failure → shame as the natural consequence, without necessarily implying a further sequence (the person may receive the shame and be changed, or may harden). The sequence across the sub-groups suggests that CHAR-1's transformative potential depends on which sequence is operative: the corrective sequence (M07-C) has a built-in forward movement; the unjust-wound sequence (M07-A) depends on external divine resolution; the hardening sequence (M07-B-VCG-04) has no built-in forward movement.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01: outer enforcing act -> inner collapse of standing -> withdrawal from public space -> eventual recovery when external sign removed. VCG-02: military defeat -> national identity stripped -> wailing and flight -> derision by neighbours. VCG-03 corrective: proud inner orientation -> divine judicial act -> inner deflation of pride -> ideally reorientation toward proper standing.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

For the dishonorer: defective inner worth-assessment -> willful act of worth-denial -> inner self-contradiction or moral hardening. For the dishonoured (in VCG-02 structural mode): sovereign or natural assignment of diminished standing -> received condition of dishonour -> sustained lived in that condition or transformation through moral change.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 sequence: conscience engages with conduct or desire -> applies God's standard -> recognises shamefulness -> produces recoil/renunciation -> principled conduct follows. Inverted CHAR-4 sequence: earthly standard applied -> shameful re-evaluated as honourable -> will orientated toward what disgraces -> deepening moral corruption.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Primary sequence: contempt directed at person -> inner wound of worth-cancellation -> formed shame-identity (if sustained) -> potential reversal through divine re-worth-assignment. The Bartimaeus narrative is the complete sequence: years of contempt -> beggar-identity formed -> Jesus calls -> immediate volitional abandonment of shame-identity -> restoration.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

VCG-01 sequence: moral integrity maintained through choices -> innocence present in heart and hands -> approach to God enabled without guilt-shame barrier. VCG-02 (Psa 73:13) sequence: innocence maintained but apparently failing to protect -> faith crisis about innocence's value -> (resolution in the wider psalm context: sanctuary encounter vindication). VCG-02 (Hos 8:5) sequence: sustained idolatry -> progressive loss of innocence-capacity -> incapacity for approach to God -> divine question naming the loss.

---

---

##### T5.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

VCG-01: outer enforcing act -> inner collapse of standing -> withdrawal from public space -> eventual recovery when external sign removed. VCG-02: military defeat -> national identity stripped -> wailing and flight -> derision by neighbours. ---

#### T5.3 — Mechanism of Change

##### T5.3.1 — What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformation, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Three mechanisms emerge from the evidence. (1) **Conscience-activation** — the primary corrective mechanism: shame activates the conscience, which then activates the will, which then activates action (2Ch 30:15; Jer 31:19; Eze 43:10). (2) **Encounter-triggered** — shame produced by confrontation with holiness (the temple's design, Eze 43:10) or divine grace (Eze 36:32) or atonement (Eze 16:63). The mechanism is the encounter itself rather than self-generated shame. (3) **Social/relational** — corrective shame deployed through community (2Th 3:14; 1Cor 6:5) — isolation, admonition, or blameless conduct producing the shame-signal in the target. These three mechanisms are distinct but all work through the conscience as the receiving faculty.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Three mechanisms: (1) Social-communal enactment (VCG-01 — community performs humiliation through bodily signs). (2) Military conquest (VCG-02 — victory strips the defeated of standing). (3) Divine sovereign act (VCG-03 — God directly brings the proud low through his word, action, or the natural consequence of pride reaching its limit, Pro 11:2).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The mechanisms of CHAR-3's production: (1) Willful inner refusal (VCG-01): the decision not to acknowledge worth, motivated by self-righteousness, contempt, or self-deception. (2) Sovereign assignment (VCG-02): God's prerogative to assign standings according to his purpose and the moral condition of the person.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The mechanism of functioning CHAR-4 is the conscience's engagement with God's standard as mediated through scripture, created order, and community norms. The mechanism of CHAR-4's inversion is the replacement of God's standard with an earthly one — "their god is their belly" (Phili 3:19) is the substitute-standard that inverts the evaluation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The mechanism of CHAR-5's damage is the worth-cancellation: treating the person as of no account (exoutheneō) removes their standing in the relational field, producing the felt shame of worth-denial. The mechanism of CHAR-5's reversal is divine re-worth-assignment: God choosing the despised (1Cor 1:28) and making the rejected stone the cornerstone (Act 4:11) overrides the contempt-system's verdict with an authoritative alternative assessment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The mechanism of CHAR-6's maintenance is the sustained moral choice to avoid deliberate wrongdoing and to remain in covenant faithfulness to God. Psa 26:6's "I wash my hands in innocence" implies an active, habitual practice. The mechanism of CHAR-6's loss (Hos 8:5) is the sustained choice of idolatry — the repeated moral choices to worship the golden calf rather than God, which over time damage the innocence-capacity until it is no longer accessible.

---

---

##### T5.3.2 — Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The conscience-activation mechanism operates primarily in prophetic and epistolary contexts (Jeremiah, Paul). The encounter-triggered mechanism operates primarily in the priestly and temple contexts (Eze 43; 2Ch 30). The social mechanism operates in communal contexts (2Th 3; 1Cor 6; Tit 2). Each mechanism is contextually appropriate — the mechanism that works in each context matches the social, institutional, and relational structure of that context.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Three mechanisms: (1) Social-communal enactment (VCG-01 — community performs humiliation through bodily signs). (2) Military conquest (VCG-02 — victory strips the defeated of standing). (3) Divine sovereign act (VCG-03 — God directly brings the proud low through his word, action, or the natural consequence of pride reaching its limit, Pro 11:2).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The mechanisms of CHAR-3's production: (1) Willful inner refusal (VCG-01): the decision not to acknowledge worth, motivated by self-righteousness, contempt, or self-deception. (2) Sovereign assignment (VCG-02): God's prerogative to assign standings according to his purpose and the moral condition of the person.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The mechanism of functioning CHAR-4 is the conscience's engagement with God's standard as mediated through scripture, created order, and community norms. The mechanism of CHAR-4's inversion is the replacement of God's standard with an earthly one — "their god is their belly" (Phili 3:19) is the substitute-standard that inverts the evaluation.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The mechanism of CHAR-5's damage is the worth-cancellation: treating the person as of no account (exoutheneō) removes their standing in the relational field, producing the felt shame of worth-denial. The mechanism of CHAR-5's reversal is divine re-worth-assignment: God choosing the despised (1Cor 1:28) and making the rejected stone the cornerstone (Act 4:11) overrides the contempt-system's verdict with an authoritative alternative assessment.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The mechanism of CHAR-6's maintenance is the sustained moral choice to avoid deliberate wrongdoing and to remain in covenant faithfulness to God. Psa 26:6's "I wash my hands in innocence" implies an active, habitual practice. The mechanism of CHAR-6's loss (Hos 8:5) is the sustained choice of idolatry — the repeated moral choices to worship the golden calf rather than God, which over time damage the innocence-capacity until it is no longer accessible.

---

---

##### T5.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; mechanisms are evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

---

#### T5.4 — Suffering and Affliction

##### T5.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or a context for it?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Extensively in M07-A. The unjust-wound sub-group is essentially suffering-and-shame: the suffering of enemy aggression, bereavement (Jer 15:9), drought (Jer 14:3-4), national catastrophe (Eze 7:18) produces shame as a component of the suffering experience. Shame is one of the inner dimensions of suffering when suffering involves exposure, loss of standing, or the collapse of what was trusted. The M07-A-VCG-03 (voluntary acceptance register) shows suffering and shame being consciously integrated: the servant accepts physical humiliation without flinching (Isa 50:6), the apostles rejoice in shame-suffering (Act 5:41), Christ endures the cross's shame (Heb 12:2).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates as suffering in VCG-01 and VCG-02: the humiliation of unjustly shaved envoys is suffering imposed on them; military defeat produces national suffering. The enduring-burden mode (VCG-04) shows CHAR-2 as sustained suffering. 1Cor 15:43 places CHAR-2 (bodily dishonor) within the context of mortal suffering as the frame for eschatological hope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonoured person suffers CHAR-3 as a form of relational injustice: the poor man dishonored (Jam 2:6) suffers the relational injustice of worth-misassignment. Paul receives dishonour "through slander and praise" (2Cor 6:8) — an apostolic suffering condition. The widow who cannot get justice (Luk 18:2/4) suffers the consequence of the judge's CHAR-3 toward her.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-4 operating in relation to suffering or affliction. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is directly connected to suffering and affliction in VCG-02: the servants beaten and treated shamefully (Mar 12:4; Luk 20:11) suffer physical violence as the vehicle of contemptuous rejection. Jesus's reception of CHAR-5 in the passion narrative (Luk 23:11) is suffering in its most concentrated form. Paul's reception of verbal contempt (2Cor 10:10 — critics dismissing his bodily presence and speech) is an apostolic suffering condition.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is tested by affliction in Psa 73:13: the psalmist has maintained innocence but suffers while the wicked prosper — this is CHAR-6 under the test of unexplained suffering. The suffering does not destroy the innocence (the psalmist has maintained it) but it tests its confidence: does innocence actually protect? The sanctuary encounter (Psa 73:17, outside the immediate corpus) reveals that it does, but the test is real and the suffering produces genuine existential questioning.

---

---

##### T5.4.2 — Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

All four. Suffering *produces* unjust shame (M07-A-VCG-01 — the victim of enemy aggression). Suffering *reveals* the inner quality of the person through their response to shame: Heb 12:2 reveals Christ's inner orientation by how he related to the cross's shame (joy-motivated will overcoming shame-pressure). Suffering *tests* the shame-bearing capacity: 1Pe 4:16 — "if anyone suffers as a Christian, let him not be ashamed" — the test of whether suffering produces shame-collapse or God-honouring response. Unjust shame *deepens* suffering: the mother whose bereavement is compounded by the "shaming and disgracing" (Jer 15:9) shows shame intensifying the suffering experience.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates as suffering in VCG-01 and VCG-02: the humiliation of unjustly shaved envoys is suffering imposed on them; military defeat produces national suffering. The enduring-burden mode (VCG-04) shows CHAR-2 as sustained suffering. 1Cor 15:43 places CHAR-2 (bodily dishonor) within the context of mortal suffering as the frame for eschatological hope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonoured person suffers CHAR-3 as a form of relational injustice: the poor man dishonored (Jam 2:6) suffers the relational injustice of worth-misassignment. Paul receives dishonour "through slander and praise" (2Cor 6:8) — an apostolic suffering condition. The widow who cannot get justice (Luk 18:2/4) suffers the consequence of the judge's CHAR-3 toward her.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-4 operating in relation to suffering or affliction. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is directly connected to suffering and affliction in VCG-02: the servants beaten and treated shamefully (Mar 12:4; Luk 20:11) suffer physical violence as the vehicle of contemptuous rejection. Jesus's reception of CHAR-5 in the passion narrative (Luk 23:11) is suffering in its most concentrated form. Paul's reception of verbal contempt (2Cor 10:10 — critics dismissing his bodily presence and speech) is an apostolic suffering condition.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is tested by affliction in Psa 73:13: the psalmist has maintained innocence but suffers while the wicked prosper — this is CHAR-6 under the test of unexplained suffering. The suffering does not destroy the innocence (the psalmist has maintained it) but it tests its confidence: does innocence actually protect? The sanctuary encounter (Psa 73:17, outside the immediate corpus) reveals that it does, but the test is real and the suffering produces genuine existential questioning.

---

---

##### T5.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; the suffering-shame relationship is extensively evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 operates as suffering in VCG-01 and VCG-02: the humiliation of unjustly shaved envoys is suffering imposed on them; military defeat produces national suffering. The enduring-burden mode (VCG-04) shows CHAR-2 as sustained suffering. 1Cor 15:43 places CHAR-2 (bodily dishonor) within the context of mortal suffering as the frame for eschatological hope.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The dishonoured person suffers CHAR-3 as a form of relational injustice: the poor man dishonored (Jam 2:6) suffers the relational injustice of worth-misassignment. Paul receives dishonour "through slander and praise" (2Cor 6:8) — an apostolic suffering condition. The widow who cannot get justice (Luk 18:2/4) suffers the consequence of the judge's CHAR-3 toward her.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (S)

The 16-verse corpus does not directly evidence CHAR-4 operating in relation to suffering or affliction. Silent.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is directly connected to suffering and affliction in VCG-02: the servants beaten and treated shamefully (Mar 12:4; Luk 20:11) suffer physical violence as the vehicle of contemptuous rejection. Jesus's reception of CHAR-5 in the passion narrative (Luk 23:11) is suffering in its most concentrated form. Paul's reception of verbal contempt (2Cor 10:10 — critics dismissing his bodily presence and speech) is an apostolic suffering condition.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is tested by affliction in Psa 73:13: the psalmist has maintained innocence but suffers while the wicked prosper — this is CHAR-6 under the test of unexplained suffering. The suffering does not destroy the innocence (the psalmist has maintained it) but it tests its confidence: does innocence actually protect? The sanctuary encounter (Psa 73:17, outside the immediate corpus) reveals that it does, but the test is real and the suffering produces genuine existential questioning.

---

---

#### T5.5 — Formation and Sanctification

##### T5.5.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the person over time toward greater likeness?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The M07-C evidence is the primary basis: the series Eze 16:52 → 16:54 → 16:61 → 16:63 → 36:32 → 43:10-11 presents a progressive formation arc in which shame before God's holiness is not a one-time event but an ongoing posture — Israel is repeatedly called to bear its disgrace, remember its ways, be ashamed before grace — and this shame-before-grace is the inner environment of ongoing covenant relationship with God. The M07-C-VCG-03 material (entropē — 1Cor 6:5; 15:34) shows shame as a sanctification tool — Paul uses it to form the Corinthians toward greater moral seriousness. The Proverbs wisdom pattern (M07-B-VCG-03) presents shame as a formative consequence that shapes the person who receives it toward wisdom (the one who receives instruction avoids disgrace; the one who ignores it suffers it).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 participates in sanctification specifically through VCG-03: God's systematic reduction of pride-structures is a formative act, not merely punitive. The repeated Day-of-the-Lord bringing-low of everything self-elevated (Isa 2 series) is God's programme of bringing human standing to its proper proportion so he alone is exalted. Pro 11:2 — "when pride comes, then comes disgrace, but with the humble is wisdom" — is wisdom-tradition formation.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The negative: CHAR-3's active form represents a corruption of the worth-recognition capacity that formation is meant to heal. The positive: learning to see and honour the worth of others — especially the poor, the weak, those the world despises — is part of the formation of the image-bearer toward the likeness of God. Jam 2:6's condemnation of dishonoring the poor is precisely a formation instruction: the community must learn to see worth where the world sees none.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 in its functioning form is a formation-essential faculty: the person who cannot recognise what is shameful cannot be formed toward moral maturity. Paul's renunciation of shameful ways (2Cor 4:2) as the basis for credible ministry shows CHAR-4 as a prerequisite for authentic Christian formation and community life. The revival of CHAR-4 is itself a formation goal: the corrective-shame passages in CHAR-1's M07-C material (1Cor 6:5; 15:34) are attempts to reactivate the community's dormant CHAR-4 capacity.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 participates in sanctification through the formation it requires: the person who receives contempt and responds with blessing rather than retaliation (1Pe 3:9) is being formed in the direction of Christ's own response to contempt. The protective-absence cases (Rut 2:15; 1Sa 25:7/15) show CHAR-5's prevention as an act of character formation in the protector — restraining oneself from contemptuous treatment of the vulnerable is a formative moral practice.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 participates in the longer arc of character formation: the sustained maintenance of innocence (Psa 73:13 — "I have kept my heart clean") over time through suffering and apparent futility is itself a formative practice. The person who maintains moral integrity even when it seems unrewarded is being formed in the direction of genuine covenant faithfulness — the formation that produces the character capable of the sanctuary encounter where innocence is vindicated.

---

---

##### T5.5.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Shame's role in the sanctification arc is specifically that of *moral-honesty maintenance*. The person in the formation arc cannot bypass shame: they must periodically return to the posture of the face-not-lifted (Ezr 9:6), the lying-down-in-shame (Jer 3:25), the being-ashamed-of-their-ways (Eze 36:32). This is not self-flagellation but the maintenance of accurate moral self-perception before God — the person knows who they are, what they have done, and how they stand before divine holiness. Formation requires this honesty; formation without it produces false confidence. The seared-conscience passages (Jer 6:15; 8:12) show what formation without shame-honesty produces: people who cannot be formed because they cannot be reached by the corrective signal.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 participates in sanctification specifically through VCG-03: God's systematic reduction of pride-structures is a formative act, not merely punitive. The repeated Day-of-the-Lord bringing-low of everything self-elevated (Isa 2 series) is God's programme of bringing human standing to its proper proportion so he alone is exalted. Pro 11:2 — "when pride comes, then comes disgrace, but with the humble is wisdom" — is wisdom-tradition formation.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The negative: CHAR-3's active form represents a corruption of the worth-recognition capacity that formation is meant to heal. The positive: learning to see and honour the worth of others — especially the poor, the weak, those the world despises — is part of the formation of the image-bearer toward the likeness of God. Jam 2:6's condemnation of dishonoring the poor is precisely a formation instruction: the community must learn to see worth where the world sees none.

---

---

---

The person who maintains moral integrity even when it seems unrewarded is being formed in the direction of genuine covenant faithfulness — the formation that produces the character capable of the sanctuary encounter where innocence is vindicated.

---

---

##### T5.5.3 — If the evidence is silent on formation and sanctification, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 participates in sanctification specifically through VCG-03: God's systematic reduction of pride-structures is a formative act, not merely punitive. ---

---

#### T5.6 — Eschatological Trajectory

##### T5.6.1 — Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is oriented?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, strongly. The M07-A-VCG-04 material is the primary evidence: Isa 54:4 — "you will not be ashamed... you will forget the shame of your youth... the reproach of your widowhood you will remember no more"; Isa 61:7 — "instead of your shame there shall be a double portion... they shall have everlasting joy"; Joe 2:26 — "my people shall never again be put to shame"; Zep 3:19 — "I will change their shame into praise and renown in all the earth." The M07-C-VCG-04 material extends this eschatologically: Isa 45:17 — "never be put to shame or confounded to all eternity"; Joe 2:27 — "my people shall never again be put to shame." Rev 3:18 (vc=34975) — the naked shame covered by Christ's garments — frames the present shame-condition within eschatological transformation.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, strongly. (1) The Day-of-the-Lord material (Isa 2:9-17; 13:11) points toward eschatological completion. (2) 1Cor 15:43 — body sown in dishonor, raised in glory — is the eschatological resolution of CHAR-2 at the individual level. (3) Hab 2:16 — "utter shame will come upon your glory" — is directed eschatologically: God's cup of judgment will finally execute the complete reversal of all proud human standing.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

The structural-dishonour mode (VCG-02) points toward its own eschatological resolution: 2Ti 2:20's vessel for dishonorable use is implicitly oriented toward the possibility of cleansing (2:21 context). Rom 9:21's potter-and-clay raises the deepest eschatological question: sovereign assignment of dishonour-standings as a condition of creaturely existence, and whether eschatological transformation re-assigns those standings.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Rev 16:15 frames CHAR-4's proper functioning as oriented toward the moment of Christ's coming: the one who "stays awake, keeping his garments on" avoids the shame of exposure at that moment. The eschatological fullness is the state in which moral vigilance has been sustained and the shameful has been renounced throughout — so that at Christ's coming no exposure occurs. CHAR-4's eschatological trajectory is toward the full activation and correct calibration of the moral-evaluative conscience.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Yes. Act 4:11 (the rejected stone becoming the cornerstone) is the paradigmatic eschatological statement of CHAR-5's reversal. 1Cor 1:28 (God choosing the despised to nullify things that are) is the eschatological programme: the world's contempt-verdicts are being overturned, and this overturning will be completed in the eschaton. The present experience of CHAR-5 anticipates its final reversal — shame from contempt is a temporary condition oriented toward the vindicating re-worth-assignment of God.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Psa 73:13's lament — maintained innocence apparently futile — is resolved in its wider context by the sanctuary encounter and the eschatological vindication of the righteous. The present experience of CHAR-6 (maintained innocence under suffering) anticipates its eschatological vindication: the person who maintains moral integrity will find it vindicated when "their end" is seen clearly (Psa 73:17). The eschatological fullness is the state in which innocence's protective function is fully confirmed and the wicked's apparently successful rejection of it is finally judged.

---

---

##### T5.6.2 — What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The present experience of shame anticipates two futures, in tension. (1) In the unjust-wound register: present shame anticipates its permanent removal and transformation into honour, praise, and double portion. The shame is real and painful now; its future is its opposite. (2) In the corrective register: present shame before God's holiness anticipates the fullness of knowing God's design — shame is the entry-point to a fuller relationship, not the permanent condition. Eze 43:11: when Israel is ashamed, the full design is disclosed — the future fullness (knowing the design, carrying it out) is what shame is the gateway toward. The eschatological direction of CHAR-1 is therefore toward its own resolution and replacement, not its perpetuation.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Yes, strongly. (1) The Day-of-the-Lord material (Isa 2:9-17; 13:11) points toward eschatological completion. (2) 1Cor 15:43 — body sown in dishonor, raised in glory — is the eschatological resolution of CHAR-2 at the individual level. (3) Hab 2:16 — "utter shame will come upon your glory" — is directed eschatologically: God's cup of judgment will finally execute the complete reversal of all proud human standing.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

---

---

---

---

---

##### T5.6.3 — If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; eschatological trajectory is strongly evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

---

---

#### T5.7 — Deposit Consequence

##### T5.7.1 — Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that deposit produce over time?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

T2.8 identified a functional deposit in the inner person — the "rottenness in the bones" (Pro 12:4) image of shame as structural inner damage, and the shame carried generationally (Ezr 9:7). The developmental consequence of this deposit is identity-formation shaped by shame: when shame is sustained without resolution, it becomes part of the person's inner self-understanding. Jeremiah's "spend my days in shame" (Jer 20:18) shows a life formed around the chronic shame-condition. Israel's identity is partially constituted by its shame-history — the post-exilic community in Ezr 9:7 defines itself partly through its inherited shame. This deposit drives the need for divine shame-removal: the eschatological promises (Isa 54:4; Zep 3:19) are not addressing a momentary feeling but a constitutively deposited inner condition that has shaped the person's and community's sense of self.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The deposit identified at T2.8 (permanent identity-marking) produces sustained consequence of restricted access and ongoing identity. The Levites permanently restricted from priestly service (Eze 44:13) carry the deposit as a vocational limitation. The warriors bearing shame into the pit (Eze 32) carry the deposit as a permanent identity-record. The deposit's developmental consequence is the narrowing of the person's relational scope — what they can access, where they can go, who they can be before God and community.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

For the dishonorer: the sustained practice of worth-denial toward God or persons establishes an entrenched inner disposition (the Luk 18:2/4 judge's recognized character trait) and produces the self-undermining inner contradiction (Rom 2:23). The deposit in the dishonorer's inner person is the hardened incapacity for genuine worth-recognition. For the dishonoured in the structural mode: the assigned standing of dishonour may become an identity-condition (2Ti 2:20).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 deposits moral discernment — the habituated capacity to recognise and renounce the shameful. Inverted CHAR-4 deposits moral blindness — the established incapacity to see what is actually shameful, and the established love of what disgraces (Hos 4:18). These deposits shape the person's long-term moral trajectory toward their eschatological destination.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The deposit of Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is the most direct evidence: sustained contempt deposits a shame-shaped self-understanding into the person's inner identity. The developmental consequence is the reduction of the person's sense of possibility (their plans are shamed, Psa 14:6), their ministry capacity is undermined (1Cor 16:11), and their relational standing is compromised. The reversal of this deposit requires an authoritative counter-word from outside (Jesus calling Bartimaeus) that overrides the accumulated contempt-deposit.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The deposit of sustained CHAR-6 maintenance is moral character formed through the habitual practice of keeping the heart clean and washing the hands in innocence. Psa 73:13's "I have kept my heart clean" is not a one-time act but a sustained pattern — and this sustained pattern deposits a moral-character quality into the person. The deposit of CHAR-6's loss (Hos 8:5) is the incapacity-condition: the accumulated moral choices of idolatry have so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity itself is lost. This deposit requires divine intervention for reversal.

---

---

##### T5.7.2 — Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers to this day" — explicitly names generational shame-accumulation. Dan 9:7-8 — "to our kings, to our princes, and to our fathers, because we have sinned against you" — names the corporate-generational character of the shame-condition. Israel's covenant shame is inherited across generations; the community that stands before God in confession (Dan 9; Ezr 9) carries the shame of its ancestors as part of its own inner-being condition. The eschatological promise that shame will be "forgotten" (Isa 54:4) operates at the same generational level — the whole identity-constituting memory of shame will be dissolved.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The deposit identified at T2.8 (permanent identity-marking) produces sustained consequence of restricted access and ongoing identity. The Levites permanently restricted from priestly service (Eze 44:13) carry the deposit as a vocational limitation. The warriors bearing shame into the pit (Eze 32) carry the deposit as a permanent identity-record. The deposit's developmental consequence is the narrowing of the person's relational scope — what they can access, where they can go, who they can be before God and community.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

For the dishonorer: the sustained practice of worth-denial toward God or persons establishes an entrenched inner disposition (the Luk 18:2/4 judge's recognized character trait) and produces the self-undermining inner contradiction (Rom 2:23). The deposit in the dishonorer's inner person is the hardened incapacity for genuine worth-recognition. For the dishonoured in the structural mode: the assigned standing of dishonour may become an identity-condition (2Ti 2:20).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Functioning CHAR-4 deposits moral discernment — the habituated capacity to recognise and renounce the shameful. Inverted CHAR-4 deposits moral blindness — the established incapacity to see what is actually shameful, and the established love of what disgraces (Hos 4:18). These deposits shape the person's long-term moral trajectory toward their eschatological destination.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

The deposit of Bartimaeus's beggar-identity (Mar 10:50) is the most direct evidence: sustained contempt deposits a shame-shaped self-understanding into the person's inner identity. The developmental consequence is the reduction of the person's sense of possibility (their plans are shamed, Psa 14:6), their ministry capacity is undermined (1Cor 16:11), and their relational standing is compromised. The reversal of this deposit requires an authoritative counter-word from outside (Jesus calling Bartimaeus) that overrides the accumulated contempt-deposit.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The deposit of sustained CHAR-6 maintenance is moral character formed through the habitual practice of keeping the heart clean and washing the hands in innocence. Psa 73:13's "I have kept my heart clean" is not a one-time act but a sustained pattern — and this sustained pattern deposits a moral-character quality into the person. The deposit of CHAR-6's loss (Hos 8:5) is the incapacity-condition: the accumulated moral choices of idolatry have so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity itself is lost. This deposit requires divine intervention for reversal.

---

---

##### T5.7.3 — If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; deposit is evidenced at T2.8.

---

## T6 — Relationships with Other Characteristics
