## T6 — Relationships with Other Characteristics

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

The deposit of sustained CHAR-6 maintenance is moral character formed through the habitual practice of keeping the heart clean and washing the hands in innocence. Psa 73:13's "I have kept my heart clean" is not a one-time act but a sustained pattern — and this sustained pattern deposits a moral-character quality into the person. The deposit of CHAR-6's loss (Hos 8:5) is the incapacity-condition: the accumulated moral choices of idolatry have so deeply distorted the inner moral faculty that innocence-capacity itself is lost. This deposit requires divine intervention for reversal.

---

---

## T6 — Relationships with Other Characteristics

---

### T6

#### T6.1 — Co-occurrence

##### T6.1.1 — Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

From the verse evidence, the following characteristics co-occur most significantly with CHAR-1. (1) **Contempt/rejection (CHAR-5, M07-G)**: the M07-B-VCG-01 psalmist-enemy material and the contempt-producing-shame mechanism show contempt as a frequent co-occurring trigger for shame. The Phase 3 cross-register flag confirmed the M06-M07 structural link: contempt is the source-side; shame is the received face. (2) **Humiliation as enforced abasement (CHAR-2, M07-D)**: Isa 50:6-7 (servant bearing disgrace and not being disgraced) shows CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 operating together in the same context; the distinction is inner experience vs. external abasement. (3) **Dishonour as relational worth-denial (CHAR-3, M07-E)**: the Psalm "reproach-shame-dishonor" trio (Psa 69:19) shows CHAR-1 co-occurring with dishonour. (4) **Innocence as counter (CHAR-6, M07-H)**: the M12-flagged innocence material (niq.qa.von; qe.ha.von) is structurally paired with CHAR-1 — innocence is the protective counter to shame.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-1 (shame as experienced inner state): enforced humiliation typically produces the felt inner shame-experience (Jer 48:39 — "turned his back in shame, Moab has become a derision" shows both simultaneously). CHAR-2 also co-occurs with CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): the violent treatment of the vineyard servants (VCG-01) overlaps with the contempt-mechanism of CHAR-5.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-5 (shame produced by contempt): the contempt-mechanism (CHAR-5) is frequently the source of the worth-denial (CHAR-3). CHAR-3 also co-occurs with CHAR-1 (felt shame) as the relational cause of CHAR-1's felt experience in the dishonoured person.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 co-occurs with CHAR-1 in the M07-B seared-conscience register (the loss of the capacity for shame = the loss of CHAR-4's functioning). The absence of CHAR-1's corrective shame-experience is simultaneously the loss of CHAR-4's evaluative operation. CHAR-4 also co-occurs with CHAR-6 (innocence as structural counter to shame) — the blameless conscience of CHAR-6 is the positive form of what CHAR-4's functioning conscience is oriented toward.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial): contempt-produced shame is a specific form of worth-denial, and the two characteristics share vocabulary (atimazō, exoutheneō) and often describe the same event from different analytical angles. CHAR-5 also co-occurs with CHAR-2 (enforced humiliation): VCG-02's violent rejection (servants beaten) is simultaneously CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame in the recipient) and CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing). CHAR-5 is causally related to CHAR-1: the contempt received (CHAR-5) produces the felt inner shame-experience (CHAR-1) in the recipient.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-1 (shame as experienced inner state) in its M07-C register: the guilt-shame of M07-C (the face that cannot be lifted before God, Ezr 9:6) is the condition that CHAR-6 structurally counters. Where CHAR-6 is present, M07-C's guilt-shame is absent; where CHAR-6 is absent, M07-C's guilt-shame is appropriate and present. CHAR-6 also co-occurs with CHAR-4 (shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment): CHAR-4's functioning conscience is the evaluative operation; CHAR-6 is the positive moral condition that results when the conscience's evaluation finds no deliberate wrongdoing.

---

---

##### T6.1.2 — What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 is a relational characteristic that attracts co-occurrence with its primary causes (contempt producing shame), its outer form (humiliation), and its structural opposites (honour, innocence). The pattern reveals CHAR-1 as positioned at the intersection of three axes: the moral axis (guilt → shame → correction or hardening), the relational axis (contempt/dishonour → shame → withdrawal or endurance), and the divine-encounter axis (sin → guilt-shame → gateway to God or seared conscience). CHAR-1's place in the inner-being landscape is as the emotional-moral register of the person's standing — it co-occurs with whatever challenges, strips, or exposes that standing.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-1 (shame as experienced inner state): enforced humiliation typically produces the felt inner shame-experience (Jer 48:39 — "turned his back in shame, Moab has become a derision" shows both simultaneously). CHAR-2 also co-occurs with CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): the violent treatment of the vineyard servants (VCG-01) overlaps with the contempt-mechanism of CHAR-5.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-5 (shame produced by contempt): the contempt-mechanism (CHAR-5) is frequently the source of the worth-denial (CHAR-3). CHAR-3 also co-occurs with CHAR-1 (felt shame) as the relational cause of CHAR-1's felt experience in the dishonoured person.

---

The absence of CHAR-1's corrective shame-experience is simultaneously the loss of CHAR-4's evaluative operation. CHAR-4 also co-occurs with CHAR-6 (innocence as structural counter to shame) — the blameless conscience of CHAR-6 is the positive form of what CHAR-4's functioning conscience is oriented toward.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial): contempt-produced shame is a specific form of worth-denial, and the two characteristics share vocabulary (atimazō, exoutheneō) and often describe the same event from different analytical angles. CHAR-5 also co-occurs with CHAR-2 (enforced humiliation): VCG-02's violent rejection (servants beaten) is simultaneously CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame in the recipient) and CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing). CHAR-5 is causally related to CHAR-1: the contempt received (CHAR-5) produces the felt inner shame-experience (CHAR-1) in the recipient.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 co-occurs most significantly with CHAR-1 (shame as experienced inner state) in its M07-C register: the guilt-shame of M07-C (the face that cannot be lifted before God, Ezr 9:6) is the condition that CHAR-6 structurally counters. ---

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; significant co-occurrence is evidenced.

#### T6.2 — Sequential Relationships

##### T6.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Several sequential relationships are evidenced. (1) **Contempt → Shame (M07-G → CHAR-1)**: contempt consistently precedes shame in the M07-B-VCG-01 enemy material — the enemy's hostile inner disposition produces the shame experienced by the psalmist. (2) **Sin → Guilt-shame → Corrective action (moral failure → CHAR-1 → responsiveness)**: in M07-C, the sin precedes the guilt-shame, and guilt-shame precedes the corrective response. (3) **Trust → Shame-protection (CHAR-1 avoided by trust)**: in M07-C-VCG-02, trust consistently precedes and protects from shame — shame's absence is the product of the prior trust-orientation. (4) **Shame → Silence (CHAR-1 → cessation of speech)**: Eze 16:63 shows shame producing silence as its consistent output — the sequence shame → inability to speak is evidenced multiple times.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Pride consistently precedes CHAR-2 in VCG-03 ("when pride comes, then comes disgrace," Pro 11:2). Wailing and flight consistently follow CHAR-2 in VCG-02. The sequence pride -> CHAR-2 -> deflation of pride is the primary sequential relationship.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Contempt/self-righteousness consistently precedes CHAR-3 in VCG-01 (the judge's absent-regard; Luk 18:9's self-righteousness producing contempt toward others). CHAR-3 (worth-denial) consistently precedes the felt shame of the dishonoured (CHAR-1 in its unjust-wound register). The sequence: inner disposition of self-sufficiency -> CHAR-3 (worth-denial) -> CHAR-1 (felt shame in the dishonoured).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

In VCG-02 (disordered desire), the sequence is: idolatry (theological cause) -> "God gave them up" -> dishonorable passions (VCG-02 CHAR-4 condition) -> shameless acts (Rom 1:27). In VCG-03 (inversion): earthly-orientation -> evaluation inversion -> glorying in shame. CHAR-4 comes after the determining condition (standard-choice, theological orientation) and before the expression in conduct.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Self-righteousness consistently precedes CHAR-5 in VCG-01 (Luk 18:9 — trusting in their own righteousness produces contempt toward others). The contempt-act (M06) consistently precedes CHAR-5 (the shame produced). CHAR-5 can precede the retaliation-response (1Pe 3:9) or the re-worth-assignment reversal (Act 4:11). The primary sequence: self-righteous self-assessment -> contempt-act (M06) -> CHAR-5 (received contempt-shame) -> either retaliation or blessing.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 consistently precedes approach to God (Psa 26:6 — innocence -> approach to altar). The loss of CHAR-6 consistently produces blocked access (Hos 8:5 — incapacity for innocence -> inability to approach). The sequence: CHAR-6 present -> approach to God enabled -> worship offered. CHAR-6 absent -> approach blocked -> the condition of M07-C's guilt-shame appropriate.

---

---

##### T6.2.2 — What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The contempt-precedes-shame sequence reveals CHAR-1's position as a *receiver* characteristic — it is downstream of what others do to or in the person. The sin-precedes-guilt-shame sequence reveals CHAR-1 as a *consequence* characteristic in its moral-failure register — it is downstream of moral failure. The shame-precedes-silence sequence shows CHAR-1 as a *producer* — it silences, closes, and withdraws the person who experiences it. CHAR-1 is therefore positioned in the middle of several sequences: it receives from upstream conditions and produces downstream effects.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Pride consistently precedes CHAR-2 in VCG-03 ("when pride comes, then comes disgrace," Pro 11:2). Wailing and flight consistently follow CHAR-2 in VCG-02. The sequence pride -> CHAR-2 -> deflation of pride is the primary sequential relationship.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Contempt/self-righteousness consistently precedes CHAR-3 in VCG-01 (the judge's absent-regard; Luk 18:9's self-righteousness producing contempt toward others). CHAR-3 (worth-denial) consistently precedes the felt shame of the dishonoured (CHAR-1 in its unjust-wound register). The sequence: inner disposition of self-sufficiency -> CHAR-3 (worth-denial) -> CHAR-1 (felt shame in the dishonoured).

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

In VCG-02 (disordered desire), the sequence is: idolatry (theological cause) -> "God gave them up" -> dishonorable passions (VCG-02 CHAR-4 condition) -> shameless acts (Rom 1:27). In VCG-03 (inversion): earthly-orientation -> evaluation inversion -> glorying in shame. CHAR-4 comes after the determining condition (standard-choice, theological orientation) and before the expression in conduct.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Self-righteousness consistently precedes CHAR-5 in VCG-01 (Luk 18:9 — trusting in their own righteousness produces contempt toward others). The contempt-act (M06) consistently precedes CHAR-5 (the shame produced). CHAR-5 can precede the retaliation-response (1Pe 3:9) or the re-worth-assignment reversal (Act 4:11). The primary sequence: self-righteous self-assessment -> contempt-act (M06) -> CHAR-5 (received contempt-shame) -> either retaliation or blessing.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 consistently precedes approach to God (Psa 26:6 — innocence -> approach to altar). The loss of CHAR-6 consistently produces blocked access (Hos 8:5 — incapacity for innocence -> inability to approach). The sequence: CHAR-6 present -> approach to God enabled -> worship offered. CHAR-6 absent -> approach blocked -> the condition of M07-C's guilt-shame appropriate.

---

---

---

#### T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships

##### T6.3.1 — Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The primary characteristic CHAR-1 produces is *silence/withdrawal* — not itself a named characteristic in the programme's current vocabulary but the inner-being cessation of speech, presence, and agency. Beyond this: (1) CHAR-1 in its corrective mode produces *contrition* and *moral reorientation* — the priests consecrating themselves (2Ch 30:15), Israel receiving the temple design (Eze 43:11). (2) CHAR-1 in the unjust-wound mode, when resolved by God, produces *praise* (Zep 3:19 — shame changed into praise; Psa 71:24 — enemies' disgrace becomes the content of the psalmist's praise). (3) CHAR-1 in its seared form produces *hardening* — the absence of shame produces progressive moral insensitivity.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is produced by pride (moral cause, VCG-03), military defeat (political cause, VCG-02), and social community's enacted judgment (social cause, VCG-01). CHAR-2 produces CHAR-1 (the inner shame experience) as its primary downstream consequence, and in extreme cases produces the VCG-04 enduring-burden condition. CHAR-2 is constituted by the mechanism of enforcement — it is definitionally enforced, not chosen.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by the failure or refusal of the worth-recognition faculty (internal cause) or by sovereign assignment (external cause, VCG-02). CHAR-3 produces CHAR-1 (felt shame) in the dishonoured and can produce CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing) when the worth-denial is enacted through public demotion. CHAR-3 is distinct from but frequently causally connected to CHAR-5.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is produced by the conscience's engagement with the moral standard. CHAR-4 produces moral conduct (through renunciation) or immoral conduct (through the inverted embrace of the shameful). CHAR-4 constitutes the moral-evaluative component of conscience — it is conscience in its shame-recognitive mode.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is produced by the contempt-act (M06's characteristic is the producing mechanism; CHAR-5 is its product in the recipient). CHAR-5 produces CHAR-1 (the felt shame-experience) in the recipient. CHAR-5 is a constitutive element of the contempt-shame dynamic: without a recipient who experiences the shame, the contempt remains only in the contempt-er. The dynamic requires both M06 (contempt-er's act) and CHAR-5 (recipient's received shame) to be complete.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is produced by the sustained moral choices of covenant faithfulness — it is the output of the volitional-moral process of avoiding deliberate wrongdoing. CHAR-6 produces the enabling condition for approach to God (Psa 26:6) — the relational access that guilt-shame would block. CHAR-6 is constitutively the positive pole of the guilt-shame polarity: it is what CHAR-1's M07-C guilt-shame register is the absence of. The two characteristics are structurally opposite: CHAR-6 present = CHAR-1's guilt-shame absent; CHAR-6 absent = CHAR-1's guilt-shame potentially present.

---

---

##### T6.3.2 — Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes, by multiple upstream characteristics. Contempt (CHAR-5) produces CHAR-1 in the psalmist-enemy material. Sin and moral failure produce CHAR-1 in the M07-B and M07-C registers. Misplaced trust (trusting Egypt, idols, human powers) produces CHAR-1 in M07-A-VCG-02 and M07-B-VCG-02 when the trusted object fails. Holiness (God's) produces CHAR-1 in the divine-encounter register (Ezr 9:6; Eze 36:32; Eze 43:10) — God's holiness encountered by the sinful person produces shame. CHAR-1 is thus a highly downstream characteristic in the inner-being landscape — it is the produced output of multiple upstream conditions and characteristics.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is produced by pride (moral cause, VCG-03), military defeat (political cause, VCG-02), and social community's enacted judgment (social cause, VCG-01). CHAR-2 produces CHAR-1 (the inner shame experience) as its primary downstream consequence, and in extreme cases produces the VCG-04 enduring-burden condition. CHAR-2 is constituted by the mechanism of enforcement — it is definitionally enforced, not chosen.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by the failure or refusal of the worth-recognition faculty (internal cause) or by sovereign assignment (external cause, VCG-02). CHAR-3 produces CHAR-1 (felt shame) in the dishonoured and can produce CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing) when the worth-denial is enacted through public demotion. CHAR-3 is distinct from but frequently causally connected to CHAR-5.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is produced by the conscience's engagement with the moral standard. CHAR-4 produces moral conduct (through renunciation) or immoral conduct (through the inverted embrace of the shameful). CHAR-4 constitutes the moral-evaluative component of conscience — it is conscience in its shame-recognitive mode.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is produced by the contempt-act (M06's characteristic is the producing mechanism; CHAR-5 is its product in the recipient). CHAR-5 produces CHAR-1 (the felt shame-experience) in the recipient. CHAR-5 is a constitutive element of the contempt-shame dynamic: without a recipient who experiences the shame, the contempt remains only in the contempt-er. The dynamic requires both M06 (contempt-er's act) and CHAR-5 (recipient's received shame) to be complete.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is produced by the sustained moral choices of covenant faithfulness — it is the output of the volitional-moral process of avoiding deliberate wrongdoing. CHAR-6 produces the enabling condition for approach to God (Psa 26:6) — the relational access that guilt-shame would block. CHAR-6 is constitutively the positive pole of the guilt-shame polarity: it is what CHAR-1's M07-C guilt-shame register is the absence of. The two characteristics are structurally opposite: CHAR-6 present = CHAR-1's guilt-shame absent; CHAR-6 absent = CHAR-1's guilt-shame potentially present.

---

---

##### T6.3.3 — Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-1 appears to be constitutive of the *conscience* experience in its shame-dimension: conscience's registration of failure *is* the experience of guilt-shame (M07-C). Shame and conscience are not separate — they are the same inner event described from two angles (moral registration vs. felt experience). This constitutive relationship is why the loss of shame = the loss of conscience (Jer 6:15; 8:12).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is produced by pride (moral cause, VCG-03), military defeat (political cause, VCG-02), and social community's enacted judgment (social cause, VCG-01). CHAR-2 produces CHAR-1 (the inner shame experience) as its primary downstream consequence, and in extreme cases produces the VCG-04 enduring-burden condition. CHAR-2 is constituted by the mechanism of enforcement — it is definitionally enforced, not chosen.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 produces CHAR-1 (felt shame) in the dishonoured and can produce CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing) when the worth-denial is enacted through public demotion. CHAR-3 is distinct from but frequently causally connected to CHAR-5.

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 constitutes the moral-evaluative component of conscience — it is conscience in its shame-recognitive mode.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

---

---

##### T6.3.4 — If no causal or constitutive relationship is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 is produced by pride (moral cause, VCG-03), military defeat (political cause, VCG-02), and social community's enacted judgment (social cause, VCG-01). CHAR-2 produces CHAR-1 (the inner shame experience) as its primary downstream consequence, and in extreme cases produces the VCG-04 enduring-burden condition. CHAR-2 is constituted by the mechanism of enforcement — it is definitionally enforced, not chosen.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is produced by the failure or refusal of the worth-recognition faculty (internal cause) or by sovereign assignment (external cause, VCG-02). CHAR-3 produces CHAR-1 (felt shame) in the dishonoured and can produce CHAR-2 (enforced downward movement of standing) when the worth-denial is enacted through public demotion. CHAR-3 is distinct from but frequently causally connected to CHAR-5.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is produced by the conscience's engagement with the moral standard. CHAR-4 produces moral conduct (through renunciation) or immoral conduct (through the inverted embrace of the shameful). CHAR-4 constitutes the moral-evaluative component of conscience — it is conscience in its shame-recognitive mode.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is produced by the contempt-act (M06's characteristic is the producing mechanism; CHAR-5 is its product in the recipient). CHAR-5 produces CHAR-1 (the felt shame-experience) in the recipient. CHAR-5 is a constitutive element of the contempt-shame dynamic: without a recipient who experiences the shame, the contempt remains only in the contempt-er. The dynamic requires both M06 (contempt-er's act) and CHAR-5 (recipient's received shame) to be complete.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is produced by the sustained moral choices of covenant faithfulness — it is the output of the volitional-moral process of avoiding deliberate wrongdoing. CHAR-6 produces the enabling condition for approach to God (Psa 26:6) — the relational access that guilt-shame would block. CHAR-6 is constitutively the positive pole of the guilt-shame polarity: it is what CHAR-1's M07-C guilt-shame register is the absence of. The two characteristics are structurally opposite: CHAR-6 present = CHAR-1's guilt-shame absent; CHAR-6 absent = CHAR-1's guilt-shame potentially present.

---

---

#### T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing

##### T6.4.1 — Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. (1) *Ka.lam* (H3637) appears in M07-D (humiliation as enforced abasement) as well as CHAR-1 — it spans the inner experience (CHAR-1) and the enforced outer movement (CHAR-2). (2) *Qa.lon* (H7036) appears in M07-E (dishonour) as well as CHAR-1 — it spans the relational-worth-denial dimension and the inner moral-consequence dimension. (3) *Atimazō* (G0818) appears in M07-E and CHAR-1 — dishonour as relational act and as experienced inner wound. (4) *Kataischunō* (G2617) spans CHAR-1 (the experience) and M07-G (contempt producing shame). Vocabulary sharing is extensive because shame's inner experience, outer abasement, relational worth-denial, and contempt-mechanism are all connected phenomena sharing root words.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 shares vocabulary significantly with CHAR-1: ka.lam, bosh, bo.shet, ke.lim.mah all appear in both. The distinction is the verse-emphasis: when the term names the enforced outer mechanism, it is CHAR-2; when it names the felt inner collapse, it is CHAR-1. Vocabulary sharing reflects the fact that inner and outer are aspects of the same shame-event differently observed.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 shares atimazō and atimia with CHAR-1 (where these terms name the felt experience of dishonour) and with CHAR-2 (where they name the enforced downward movement). The head-covering kataischunō (1Cor 11:4-5) appears in CHAR-1 for the shame-experience register and in CHAR-3 for the relational-disrespect register. Vocabulary sharing is significant and reflects the close analytical relationship between the cluster's characteristics.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 shares aischunē (G0152) with CHAR-1 (where it names the felt experience vs. CHAR-4 where it names the moral quality of conduct — 2Cor 4:2; Phili 3:19). CHAR-4 shares atimia (G0819) with CHAR-1 and CHAR-3 (where it names the relational worth-denial vs. CHAR-4 where it names the quality of disordered passions). The vocabulary sharing reflects the semantic overlap between the shameful quality and the shame-experience in the biblical vocabulary.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 shares exoutheneō with M06's contempt vocabulary. Atimazō (G0818) is shared with CHAR-3 (dishonour). The vocabulary sharing confirms that CHAR-5 is analytically positioned at the intersection of contempt (M06) and dishonour (CHAR-3): it is the received form of the contempt-act, experienced as worth-denial.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 shares its vocabulary (niq.qa.von, qe.ha.von) with M12 (purity/holiness) as the terms' primary register. This is the principal vocabulary-sharing relationship for CHAR-6: the same terms that name CHAR-6's inner-moral-innocence function are also the primary vocabulary of M12's purity register. The sharing reflects the fact that CHAR-6 is retained in M07 because of its shame-polarity function, while M12 holds the terms in their primary purity-holiness register.

---

---

##### T6.4.2 — Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Yes. The *bosh* root (H0954) generates *bosh*, *bo.shet*, *bu.shah*, *bosh.nah* — all within CHAR-1. The *aischun-* root generates *aischunē*, *aischunō*, *kataischunō* — also largely within CHAR-1 with some extension to M07-D. The *ke.lim.mah/ka.lam* root spans CHAR-1 (inner experience) and CHAR-2 (outer humiliation), revealing at the root level that the experience and the abasement are linguistically proximate phenomena.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 shares vocabulary significantly with CHAR-1: ka.lam, bosh, bo.shet, ke.lim.mah all appear in both. The distinction is the verse-emphasis: when the term names the enforced outer mechanism, it is CHAR-2; when it names the felt inner collapse, it is CHAR-1. Vocabulary sharing reflects the fact that inner and outer are aspects of the same shame-event differently observed.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 shares atimazō and atimia with CHAR-1 (where these terms name the felt experience of dishonour) and with CHAR-2 (where they name the enforced downward movement). The head-covering kataischunō (1Cor 11:4-5) appears in CHAR-1 for the shame-experience register and in CHAR-3 for the relational-disrespect register. Vocabulary sharing is significant and reflects the close analytical relationship between the cluster's characteristics.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 shares aischunē (G0152) with CHAR-1 (where it names the felt experience vs. CHAR-4 where it names the moral quality of conduct — 2Cor 4:2; Phili 3:19). CHAR-4 shares atimia (G0819) with CHAR-1 and CHAR-3 (where it names the relational worth-denial vs. CHAR-4 where it names the quality of disordered passions). The vocabulary sharing reflects the semantic overlap between the shameful quality and the shame-experience in the biblical vocabulary.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 shares exoutheneō with M06's contempt vocabulary. Atimazō (G0818) is shared with CHAR-3 (dishonour). The vocabulary sharing confirms that CHAR-5 is analytically positioned at the intersection of contempt (M06) and dishonour (CHAR-3): it is the received form of the contempt-act, experienced as worth-denial.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 shares its vocabulary (niq.qa.von, qe.ha.von) with M12 (purity/holiness) as the terms' primary register. The sharing reflects the fact that CHAR-6 is retained in M07 because of its shame-polarity function, while M12 holds the terms in their primary purity-holiness register.

---

---

##### T6.4.3 — What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The vocabulary sharing reveals that the distinction between CHAR-1 (inner experience) and CHAR-2 (outer humiliation) is an analytical distinction that the Hebrew does not always make morphologically — the same root can name both. The word-field of shame in Hebrew treats inner experience and outer abasement as aspects of the same reality. The analytical separation of these into distinct characteristics is programme-necessary for analytical precision, but the vocabulary confirms they are related faces of the same phenomenon.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

CHAR-2 shares vocabulary significantly with CHAR-1: ka.lam, bosh, bo.shet, ke.lim.mah all appear in both. The distinction is the verse-emphasis: when the term names the enforced outer mechanism, it is CHAR-2; when it names the felt inner collapse, it is CHAR-1. Vocabulary sharing reflects the fact that inner and outer are aspects of the same shame-event differently observed.

---

CHAR-3 shares atimazō and atimia with CHAR-1 (where these terms name the felt experience of dishonour) and with CHAR-2 (where they name the enforced downward movement). The head-covering kataischunō (1Cor 11:4-5) appears in CHAR-1 for the shame-experience register and in CHAR-3 for the relational-disrespect register. Vocabulary sharing is significant and reflects the close analytical relationship between the cluster's characteristics.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 shares aischunē (G0152) with CHAR-1 (where it names the felt experience vs. CHAR-4 where it names the moral quality of conduct — 2Cor 4:2; Phili 3:19). CHAR-4 shares atimia (G0819) with CHAR-1 and CHAR-3 (where it names the relational worth-denial vs. CHAR-4 where it names the quality of disordered passions). The vocabulary sharing reflects the semantic overlap between the shameful quality and the shame-experience in the biblical vocabulary.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 shares exoutheneō with M06's contempt vocabulary. Atimazō (G0818) is shared with CHAR-3 (dishonour). The vocabulary sharing confirms that CHAR-5 is analytically positioned at the intersection of contempt (M06) and dishonour (CHAR-3): it is the received form of the contempt-act, experienced as worth-denial.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 shares its vocabulary (niq.qa.von, qe.ha.von) with M12 (purity/holiness) as the terms' primary register. This is the principal vocabulary-sharing relationship for CHAR-6: the same terms that name CHAR-6's inner-moral-innocence function are also the primary vocabulary of M12's purity register. The sharing reflects the fact that CHAR-6 is retained in M07 because of its shame-polarity function, while M12 holds the terms in their primary purity-holiness register.

---

---

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Not applicable; significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced.

---

#### T6.5 — Distinctions

##### T6.5.1 — Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

CHAR-2 (Humiliation as enforced abasement, M07-D) is the closest neighbour. Both involve shame; both involve downward movement of standing. The precise distinction is: CHAR-1 is the *felt inner experience* — the collapse of dignity and confidence as an inner event; CHAR-2 is the *enforced outer movement* — the mechanism by which a person's standing is brought down by an external agent. A person can experience CHAR-1 (inner shame) without CHAR-2 (no external enforced abasement); and a person can undergo CHAR-2 (be publicly humiliated) without necessarily experiencing CHAR-1 in its full inner form (if they are morally insensitive or resilient). The servant who endures beating and spitting (Isa 50:6) undergoes CHAR-2 (physical humiliation) while CHAR-1 is present but borne (voluntarily accepted).

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The nearest neighbour distinction with CHAR-1: CHAR-2 is the outer-mechanism; CHAR-1 is the inner-experience. The distinction is of kind (mechanism vs. experience). CHAR-2 is also distinct from CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): CHAR-5's mechanism is specifically contempt/dismissal; CHAR-2's mechanism is enforced downward movement (which can be produced by contempt but also by military defeat, divine judgment, natural loss).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is most closely related to CHAR-5 (shame produced by contempt): both involve the treatment of persons as of diminished worth. The distinction: CHAR-3 names the relational verdict (worth-denial as the act and its structural effect); CHAR-5 names the specific mechanism (contempt/dismissal as the producing agent and its received shame as the specific outcome in the recipient). CHAR-3 is broader — worth-denial can be produced by contempt (CHAR-5), by structural assignment (VCG-02), or by hypocrisy and favoritism (VCG-01) without being contempt in the strict sense.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is most closely related to CHAR-1 in its moral-consequence register (M07-B — shame as the consequence of moral failure). The distinction: CHAR-1-M07-B is about shame as the experience that follows moral failure; CHAR-4 is about the conscience's recognition of what is shameful as a quality of conduct or desire. CHAR-4 is the evaluative faculty; CHAR-1-M07-B is the experiential consequence. They frequently occur together: the same act that CHAR-4 identifies as shameful produces CHAR-1's shame-experience in the person who commits it.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is most closely related to CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial) and to M06 (contempt as the producing mechanism). The distinction between CHAR-5 and CHAR-3: CHAR-5 names the specific mechanism (contempt as the producing force) and the received shame as the specific outcome; CHAR-3 names the relational verdict of worth-denial more broadly (which can arise from causes other than contempt). The distinction between CHAR-5 and M06: M06 holds the contempt-projection (the contempt-er's inner act); CHAR-5 holds the contempt-received shame (the recipient's inner experience). CHAR-5 and M06 are relational complements — they are the two faces of the same contempt-shame dynamic.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is most closely related to M12 (purity/holiness) through shared vocabulary, but the analytical distinction is clear: M12 holds the purity/holiness register of niq.qa.von and qe.ha.von as the primary meaning of these terms; CHAR-6 holds the innocence-as-counter-to-shame function of the same terms in every verse of the 8-verse corpus. The distinction is one of purpose and register: M12 = moral and ritual purity as the characteristic; CHAR-6 = innocence as specifically the protection against and structural counter to shame.

---

---

##### T6.5.2 — Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The boundary is inner vs. outer. When ka.lam means "the inner confounded feeling" it is CHAR-1 territory; when it means "the social-bodily demotion" it is CHAR-2 territory. Many verses show both simultaneously (the servants covering their heads — Jer 14:3 — evidence the inner shame-response as well as the bodily expression of being brought low). The Phase 5/7 separation into sub-groups handled this: M07-A/B/C carry the inner-experience dimension; M07-D carries the enforced-outer-abasement dimension. The boundary is analytically clean even when the verse evidence naturally shows both at once.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The nearest neighbour distinction with CHAR-1: CHAR-2 is the outer-mechanism; CHAR-1 is the inner-experience. The distinction is of kind (mechanism vs. experience). CHAR-2 is also distinct from CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): CHAR-5's mechanism is specifically contempt/dismissal; CHAR-2's mechanism is enforced downward movement (which can be produced by contempt but also by military defeat, divine judgment, natural loss).

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

CHAR-3 is most closely related to CHAR-5 (shame produced by contempt): both involve the treatment of persons as of diminished worth. The distinction: CHAR-3 names the relational verdict (worth-denial as the act and its structural effect); CHAR-5 names the specific mechanism (contempt/dismissal as the producing agent and its received shame as the specific outcome in the recipient). CHAR-3 is broader — worth-denial can be produced by contempt (CHAR-5), by structural assignment (VCG-02), or by hypocrisy and favoritism (VCG-01) without being contempt in the strict sense.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

CHAR-4 is most closely related to CHAR-1 in its moral-consequence register (M07-B — shame as the consequence of moral failure). The distinction: CHAR-1-M07-B is about shame as the experience that follows moral failure; CHAR-4 is about the conscience's recognition of what is shameful as a quality of conduct or desire. CHAR-4 is the evaluative faculty; CHAR-1-M07-B is the experiential consequence. They frequently occur together: the same act that CHAR-4 identifies as shameful produces CHAR-1's shame-experience in the person who commits it.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

CHAR-5 is most closely related to CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial) and to M06 (contempt as the producing mechanism). The distinction between CHAR-5 and CHAR-3: CHAR-5 names the specific mechanism (contempt as the producing force) and the received shame as the specific outcome; CHAR-3 names the relational verdict of worth-denial more broadly (which can arise from causes other than contempt). The distinction between CHAR-5 and M06: M06 holds the contempt-projection (the contempt-er's inner act); CHAR-5 holds the contempt-received shame (the recipient's inner experience). CHAR-5 and M06 are relational complements — they are the two faces of the same contempt-shame dynamic.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6 is most closely related to M12 (purity/holiness) through shared vocabulary, but the analytical distinction is clear: M12 holds the purity/holiness register of niq.qa.von and qe.ha.von as the primary meaning of these terms; CHAR-6 holds the innocence-as-counter-to-shame function of the same terms in every verse of the 8-verse corpus. The distinction is one of purpose and register: M12 = moral and ritual purity as the characteristic; CHAR-6 = innocence as specifically the protection against and structural counter to shame.

---

---

##### T6.5.3 — Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

The distinction between CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 is primarily one of *kind* (inner experience vs. outer mechanism) with a directional component (inward vs. outward focus). It is not a difference of constitutional level (both operate at the soul-body interface) or degree (CHAR-1 is not simply a lesser form of CHAR-2). They are analytically distinct characteristics that frequently co-occur and share vocabulary but evidence different inner-being content.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

The nearest neighbour distinction with CHAR-1: CHAR-2 is the outer-mechanism; CHAR-1 is the inner-experience. The distinction is of kind (mechanism vs. experience). CHAR-2 is also distinct from CHAR-5 (contempt producing shame): CHAR-5's mechanism is specifically contempt/dismissal; CHAR-2's mechanism is enforced downward movement (which can be produced by contempt but also by military defeat, divine judgment, natural loss).

#### T6.6 — Shared Verse Anchors

##### T6.6.1 — Does any verse in this characteristic's evidence base also function as a primary anchor in another characteristic's study?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Several CHAR-1 verses likely function as anchors or significant evidence in other clusters. Heb 12:2 (vc=34970) — Jesus despising the cross's shame — is a significant verse for Christological characteristics across multiple clusters. Ezr 9:6 (vc=65495) — inability to lift the face before God — is likely a primary anchor for guilt-related characteristics. Psa 22:5 (vc=34836) — trust producing shame-protection — is likely significant for the trust/faith characteristic study. However, these are projections based on what is known about the programme's characteristic set; the shared-anchor analysis requires the full cluster map to confirm.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Isa 50:6-7 (servant bearing disgrace and knowing he will not be put to shame) appears in both CHAR-2 (the physical humiliation register) and CHAR-1 (the voluntary-bearing mode). Shared anchors reflect the frequent co-occurrence of outer humiliation and inner shame-experience. The 2Sa 10:5 passage appears only in CHAR-2.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

1Cor 11:4-5 (vc=35009/35010) appear only in CHAR-3. Rom 9:21 (vc=34960) appears only in CHAR-3 (VCG-02). Joh 8:49 (vc=35000) appears only in CHAR-3. These verses are specific to CHAR-3 and do not appear as primary anchors in other characteristics.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

2Cor 4:2 (vc=34972) appears only in CHAR-4. Eph 5:12 (vc=34985) appears only in CHAR-4. Phili 3:19 (vc=65486) appears only in CHAR-4. These are specific to CHAR-4 and not shared with other characteristics — confirming CHAR-4's analytically distinctive space within M07.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Act 4:11 (vc=54638) appears only in CHAR-5 as the primary cornerstone-reversal anchor. 1Cor 1:28 (vc=54643) appears only in CHAR-5. Mar 10:50 (vc=37238) appears only in CHAR-5. These are specific to CHAR-5 and constitute its most theologically distinctive verse anchors.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Gen 20:5 (vc=22817/22821) appears only in CHAR-6. Psa 26:6 (vc=22819/22823) appears only in CHAR-6. Psa 73:13 (vc=22818/22822) appears only in CHAR-6. Hos 8:5 (vc=22820/22824) appears only in CHAR-6. These four verses (8 verse_context rows) are specific to CHAR-6 and constitute its entire corpus — confirming CHAR-6 as a compact but analytically distinct characteristic within M07.

---

##### T6.6.2 — What does the shared anchor reveal about the relationship between the two characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Where CHAR-1 verses function as anchors elsewhere, it reveals that the shame experience intersects with other major inner-being phenomena: trust/faith (the opposite of shame's collapse), guilt/contrition (the context of guilt-shame), suffering endurance (shame borne for Christ). CHAR-1 is not an isolated phenomenon but a characteristic that illuminates multiple adjacent inner-being realities.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Isa 50:6-7 (servant bearing disgrace and knowing he will not be put to shame) appears in both CHAR-2 (the physical humiliation register) and CHAR-1 (the voluntary-bearing mode). Shared anchors reflect the frequent co-occurrence of outer humiliation and inner shame-experience. The 2Sa 10:5 passage appears only in CHAR-2.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

1Cor 11:4-5 (vc=35009/35010) appear only in CHAR-3. Rom 9:21 (vc=34960) appears only in CHAR-3 (VCG-02). Joh 8:49 (vc=35000) appears only in CHAR-3. These verses are specific to CHAR-3 and do not appear as primary anchors in other characteristics.

#### T6.7 — Dimensional Sharing

##### T6.7.1 — How many of this characteristic's confirmed analytical dimensions are shared with another characteristic in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (G)

The programme's dimensional framework is not yet complete for all M07 characteristics and adjacent clusters; full dimensional sharing analysis requires Session D cross-cluster synthesis. The finding here is that the emotional/affective dimension is likely shared with M04 characteristics (joy, grief, mourning); the moral/conscience dimension is likely shared with M03 characteristics; the volitional dimension is likely shared with multiple characteristics. Specific dimensional sharing counts are not yet available.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet available pending Session D. CHAR-2's primary social/relational dimension is likely shared with CHAR-3 (dishonour as relational worth-denial) and CHAR-5 (shame from contempt). The bodily dimension is distinctive to CHAR-2 within M07.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet available pending Session D. CHAR-3's primary relational dimension is likely shared with CHAR-5. The specific worth-assessment dimension is likely distinctive to CHAR-3 within M07.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet available pending Session D. CHAR-4's primary moral-evaluative dimension is distinctive within M07 — it is the most directly moral-evaluative characteristic in the cluster. This dimension is likely shared with characteristics in M03 (conscience and grief register), M12 (purity/holiness), and the guilt clusters.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (G)

Full dimensional sharing data not yet available pending Session D. CHAR-5's primary relational dimension is likely shared with CHAR-3. The contempt-mechanism dimension (the specific role of contempt in producing shame) is likely shared with M06's contempt-projection characteristic across the cluster boundary.

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

CHAR-6's primary moral dimension is the dimension it shares most directly with M12. Within M07, CHAR-6's moral dimension is distinctive — it is the only positively-framed moral characteristic in M07 (all other M07 characteristics name what goes wrong; CHAR-6 names what protects and enables). This positive moral dimension is likely shared with the holiness and purity characteristics of M12, confirming the INTER_RELATIONSHIP flag's expectation.

---

## T7 — Lexical, Literary, and Scientific Analysis

---

### T7

#### T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis

##### T7.1.1 — What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

Primary Hebrew: *bosh* (H0954) — root meaning: to be ashamed, to become pale/confounded, to dry up (the withered-grass image of 2Ki 19:26 echoes this); the root suggests inner collapse/paling. *Ke.lim.mah* (H3639) — from *ka.lam* (to be wounded, humiliated); root suggests a cutting, wounding inner state of disgrace. *Bo.shet* (H1322) — the nominal form of *bosh*, naming shame as a condition or state. *Cha.pher* (H2659) — to be disappointed, disgraced, confounded; root related to searching/digging (seeking what is not found, then becoming ashamed of the failed seeking). Primary Greek: *aischunē* (G0152) — from *aischros* (ugly, base, shameful); root suggests the perception of ugliness or baseness in oneself. *Kataischunō* (G2617) — thoroughly put to shame, downward-shaming; the kata- prefix intensifies and specifies direction (downward). The roots collectively reveal: shame is an inner paling/collapsing, a wound that cuts, a seeking that fails, a perception of one's own baseness before what is right or holy.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Ka.lam (H3637) — root sense of wounding/cutting; the humiliation wounds the social existence. Sha.phel (H8213) — to be low, to be brought down; Hiphil: causing to be low; captures the downward-direction specificity. Bosh and bo.shet in the defeat/abasement register. Ke.lim.mah (H3639) — carried disgrace; the enduring-burden register. Qa.lon (H7036) — disgrace as natural fruit of pride. Qi.qa.lon (H7022) — utter disgrace, superlative form (Hab 2:16). Greek: atimia (G0819) — dishonor as assigned state (1Cor 15:43); fimoō (G5392) — muzzling/silencing as enforced voice-suppression. Roots collectively: enforced downward movement, wounding of social existence, silencing.

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Primary terms: Atimazō (G0818): to dishonour, treat as without honour — active verb, the dishonoring act. Atimia (G0819): dishonour as a state — the condition of assigned or received diminished worth. Entrepō (G1788) in its absence register: the failure of the regard-faculty. Paradeigmatizō (G3856): to expose publicly, hold up to contempt. Roots: a-timē — without honour, without worth — the alpha-privative of honour. Structural opposite: timaō (to honour, to assign worth) and timē (honour as assigned worth-recognition). The evidence pairs these explicitly in Joh 8:49. The CHAR-3 corpus is entirely NT — the OT vocabulary for relational worth-denial (qa.lah, H7034; entrepō in its absence register) is thinner. The NT's christological context gives CHAR-3 its sharpest definition: dishonour as what is directed at Jesus personally and at God through human hypocrisy. Person-type: the "unjust judge" (Luk 18:2) is the closest person-type but is not a technical term. Supplication: the widow's persistent coming to the judge (Luk 18:3) is a supplication for the reversal of CHAR-3 — the only supplication-context in the corpus.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Aischros (G0150) — shameful as an adjective/quality: it is disgraceful (modifying conduct or situation). Aschēmosunē (G0808) — indecency, impropriety: the noun naming the quality of what lacks proper form. Aischunē (G0152) in its evaluative register: the shame-quality of conduct (distinct from the shame-experience). Atimia (G0819) in the dishonorable-passions register: naming the quality of certain inner drives. Together these terms form a consistent vocabulary of moral-quality assessment — they are the adjective-and-noun vocabulary of what is shameful, not the verb-vocabulary of experiencing shame.

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Exoutheneō (G1848): root ex + ouden (nothing) = to treat as nothing. This is the most radical contempt-vocabulary in the NT: the zero-worth assignment. Atimazō (G0818): to dishonour through contemptuous action; root a-timē (without honour). Loidoria (G3059): verbal reviling, reputation-attack through hostile speech. The roots together reveal CHAR-5's mechanism: the contempt-er assigns zero worth (exoutheneō), strips honour through contemptuous treatment (atimazō), or attacks reputation through speech (loidoria). The shame produced in the recipient is the inner experience of having one's worth cancelled by another's active dismissal.

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Niq.qa.von (H5356A): from naqah (to be clean, to be free from guilt, to be acquitted). Root: moral cleanness as freedom from guilt-stain. The root sense is specifically the freedom from moral contamination that makes approach to God possible. Qe.ha.von (H5356B): bluntness/cleanness of the hands; the term appears to overlap with niq.qa.von in all four shared verses. The Pass A meanings confirm that in each verse the two terms point to the same moral-integrity condition rather than distinct qualities. The root meanings together reveal CHAR-6 as constituted by freedom from guilt-stain — the inner condition of having no deliberate moral failure that would produce guilt before God.

---

##### T7.1.2 — What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the characteristic operates?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

*Bosh* functions as both verb (to be ashamed — the most common usage) and noun (via *bo.shet* and *bu.shah*). The verbal usage dominates in the CHAR-1 corpus: "they are ashamed," "they were put to shame," "you shall not be ashamed" — the stative/passive verb is the primary grammatical form. This reveals that shame as experienced inner state is primarily *received* or *arrived at* rather than *active* — the person does not do shameing to themselves; shame happens to them or in them. The passive construction confirms the condition-character of CHAR-1 (T1.2.1): it is undergone rather than performed.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Ka.lam operates primarily as a verb (being humiliated). Sha.phel operates as verb (Hiphil — causing to be brought low) and adjective (sha.phel nefesh — lowly of spirit). The verbal dominance confirms CHAR-2's action-character: it is something done, not merely something possessed. Semantic range covers bodily-social, national-political, and cosmic dimensions (moon and sun ashamed, Isa 24:23) — CHAR-2 applies wherever pride-structures or elevated standing exists.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Primary terms: Atimazō (G0818): to dishonour, treat as without honour — active verb, the dishonoring act. Atimia (G0819): dishonour as a state — the condition of assigned or received diminished worth. Entrepō (G1788) in its absence register: the failure of the regard-faculty. Paradeigmatizō (G3856): to expose publicly, hold up to contempt. Roots: a-timē — without honour, without worth — the alpha-privative of honour. Structural opposite: timaō (to honour, to assign worth) and timē (honour as assigned worth-recognition). The evidence pairs these explicitly in Joh 8:49. The CHAR-3 corpus is entirely NT — the OT vocabulary for relational worth-denial (qa.lah, H7034; entrepō in its absence register) is thinner. The NT's christological context gives CHAR-3 its sharpest definition: dishonour as what is directed at Jesus personally and at God through human hypocrisy. Person-type: the "unjust judge" (Luk 18:2) is the closest person-type but is not a technical term. Supplication: the widow's persistent coming to the judge (Luk 18:3) is a supplication for the reversal of CHAR-3 — the only supplication-context in the corpus.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

Aischros is consistently adjectival — it modifies conduct, gain, or situations. Aschēmosunē is consistently nominal — naming the quality. The adjectival/nominal dominance confirms CHAR-4's quality-character: it is about the property of things (shameful conduct, indecent acts) rather than the experience of persons. The semantic range is limited: all primary CHAR-4 terms specifically name the quality of moral shamefulness — they do not range into the social-status register of the shame vocabulary.

---

**[CHAR-5] Shame produced by contempt and rejection** (E)

Exoutheneō operates as a verb (to despise, to treat as nothing). Atimazō operates as a verb (to dishonour, to treat shamefully). Loidoria is a noun (reviling, verbal abuse). The verbal dominance confirms CHAR-5's action-character: the contempt is always something done — an active verbal or physical or attitudinal act. The semantic range spans inner attitude (VCG-01 — the exoutheneō of the self-righteous), physical violence (VCG-02 — the atimazō of violent treatment), and verbal assault (VCG-03 — the loidoria of reputation-attack).

---

**[CHAR-6] Innocence as structural counter to shame** (E)

Both terms function primarily as nouns naming a condition: "in the innocence of my hands" (Gen 20:5; Psa 26:6) — the innocence is a quality of the hands named nominally. The nominal form confirms CHAR-6's quality-character: innocence is a condition the person possesses (or fails to possess), not a direction or act. The semantic range of niq.qa.von is narrow within this corpus: it specifically names the moral cleanness that enables approach to God and protects against guilt-shame. It does not range into the social-status vocabulary of shame's other terms.

---

---

##### T7.1.3 — What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

**[CHAR-1] Shame as experienced inner state** (E)

*Bosh* ranges from acute momentary shame (the servants covering heads before drought) to chronic existential shame ("spend my days in shame") to moral shame-as-consequence (the wicked clothed with shame) to shame-before-God (Ezr 9:6) to cosmic shame (even the moon will be ashamed, Isa 24:23). The semantic range is almost the entire register of human inner moral exposure — making *bosh* one of the most semantically broad shame-vocabulary items in the evidence. *Ke.lim.mah* is narrower: primarily the social-facing, communally-visible disgrace, the ongoing wound of being seen as dishonoured.

**[CHAR-2] Humiliation as enforced abasement** (E)

Ka.lam operates primarily as a verb (being humiliated). Sha.phel operates as verb (Hiphil — causing to be brought low) and adjective (sha.phel nefesh — lowly of spirit). The verbal dominance confirms CHAR-2's action-character: it is something done, not merely something possessed. Semantic range covers bodily-social, national-political, and cosmic dimensions (moon and sun ashamed, Isa 24:23) — CHAR-2 applies wherever pride-structures or elevated standing exists.

---

**[CHAR-3] Dishonour as relational worth-denial** (E)

Primary terms: Atimazō (G0818): to dishonour, treat as without honour — active verb, the dishonoring act. Atimia (G0819): dishonour as a state — the condition of assigned or received diminished worth. Entrepō (G1788) in its absence register: the failure of the regard-faculty. Paradeigmatizō (G3856): to expose publicly, hold up to contempt. Roots: a-timē — without honour, without worth — the alpha-privative of honour. Structural opposite: timaō (to honour, to assign worth) and timē (honour as assigned worth-recognition). The evidence pairs these explicitly in Joh 8:49. The CHAR-3 corpus is entirely NT — the OT vocabulary for relational worth-denial (qa.lah, H7034; entrepō in its absence register) is thinner. The NT's christological context gives CHAR-3 its sharpest definition: dishonour as what is directed at Jesus personally and at God through human hypocrisy. Person-type: the "unjust judge" (Luk 18:2) is the closest person-type but is not a technical term. Supplication: the widow's persistent coming to the judge (Luk 18:3) is a supplication for the reversal of CHAR-3 — the only supplication-context in the corpus.

---

**[CHAR-4] Shamefulness as moral-evaluative judgment** (E)

The semantic range is limited: all primary CHAR-4 terms specifically name the quality of moral shamefulness — they do not range into the social-status register of the shame vocabulary.
